| 2.30 | Chan-Vese `UseImageSpacing` | Inert for the PDE: the flag builds `m_ScaleCoefficients`, which **nothing in the Chan-Vese chain reads**; the Hessian divides by `m_InvSpacing` set unconditionally from the *feature* image's spacing, while the re-distancing Maurer map inherits the *level-set* image's spacing — the flag's only live use is `maurer->SetUseImageSpacing` (`.hxx:227`). A level set and feature image with different spacings drive the PDE and re-distancing with different metrics. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `use_image_spacing = false` was a silent no-op for the PDE (the Hessian always divided by the feature image's spacing). This port keys the Hessian's inverse spacing on the flag (`pde_inv_spacing`): `true` keeps the feature image's physical spacing (as upstream), `false` uses unit pixel spacing, honoring the flag's documented "use image spacing" meaning for the whole iteration. The default (`true`) path is unchanged; for the co-registered inputs SimpleITK produces, the PDE and distance map now share one metric. | `chan_vese.rs` |
| 2.31 | Chan-Vese RMS / output semantics | `rms_change_accumulator` is zeroed inside the reinit branch (true every iteration: `elapsed % counter` tested before increment, and reset per-functor inside the loop) and refilled with the **re-distancing residual**, which does not decay — `MaximumRMSError`'s halt clause essentially never fires (SimpleITK's own yaml regression expects RMS `721.33` vs default threshold `0.02`); the advection branch is unreachable (`m_AdvectionWeight` never settable); `CopyInputToOutput` labels `phi < 0` **strictly**, and boundary pixels sit at `-0.0` after re-distancing, so the object boundary layer is systematically excluded from the label. (`.hxx:214-248`, `:38-77`.) **Convention kept** (2026-07-11) — both sub-behaviors are genuine level-set convention choices, not silent bugs: what `RMSChange` should report (PDE update vs. re-distancing residual) and whether the zero-level contour is inside or outside are design decisions ITK makes deliberately and SimpleITK's own regression pins (RMS `721.33`); no target semantics is mandated, so the re-distancing-residual RMS and the strict `phi < 0` label are kept as-is. | `chan_vese.rs` |
| 2.32 | `ObjectMorphologyImageFilter` | `BeforeThreadedGenerateData`'s fill-then-conditional-copy always reduces to `output := input` (the fill sentinel is constructed to differ from `ObjectValue`, `.hxx:85-113`); `UseBoundaryCondition` is dead configuration (constructors install boundary conditions but never set the flag, default `false`, yaml doesn't expose it); boundary detection is a hard-coded `3^dim` box (`IsObjectPixelOnBoundary`, `.hxx:166-198`) **decoupled from the kernel radius** — dilation never diverges from true dilation, but erosion does substantially (5×5 block erodes to 1 pixel vs the correct 3×3 core; upstream's own header caveats this, `.h:36-40`). **Convention kept** (2026-07-11) — the over-erosion is the defining, ITK-header-documented behavior of boundary-restricted `ObjectMorphology` (not a *silent* wrongness), and the dead `UseBoundaryCondition` flag is not exposed by the yaml (no inert exposed parameter to honor or reject), so the behavior is kept as documented. | `object_morphology.rs` |
| 2.33 | `JoinSeriesImageFilter` size mismatch | Asymmetric and undocumented: a subsequent input **smaller** than the primary throws `InvalidRequestedRegionError` during region propagation, but a **larger** one is silently corner-cropped to `[0, primary_size)` (`GenerateInputRequestedRegion`, `.hxx:180+`). Physical-space congruency across inputs uses the base-class check (origin/spacing tolerance `1e-6·spacing[0]`, inclusive). Filed as Q117 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — a larger input silently corner-cropped is silent data loss, and the smaller-vs-larger split is undocumented; the class doc's "all inputs should have the same information" makes equal sizes a precondition and no single rectangular output can hold differently-sized slabs. This port rejects **any** size mismatch (larger or smaller) uniformly with a typed `InputSizeMismatch` error, so no input data is ever silently discarded; equal-sized inputs join unchanged. | `join_series.rs` |
| 2.34 | `IterativeInverseDisplacementFieldImageFilter` probe step | The coordinate-descent search step is axis 0's spacing on **every** axis: `const double spacing = inputPtr->GetSpacing()[0];` (`.hxx:89`) is the only spacing read, and `mappedPoint[k] += step` (`:146`) walks physical axis `k` by it — wrong step on every axis but the first for anisotropic fields. Filed as #6575 comment item Q25. Pinned: `the_probe_step_is_the_first_axis_spacing_on_every_axis`. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the coordinate descent keeps one probe step per axis, each initialized to that axis's own spacing (halving together on a stalled sweep); pin renamed `the_probe_step_uses_each_axiss_own_spacing`. | `displacement_field/iterative_inverse.rs` |
| 2.35 | `DisplacementFieldJacobianDeterminantFilter::SetDerivativeWeights` | Sets `m_UseImageSpacing = false;` directly (`.hxx:55`) — effective precedence between the two parameters is last-writer-wins. At the ITK level `GetUseImageSpacing()` correctly reports the flipped (false) value; the *stale* Get is SimpleITK-side: the wrapper's `GetUseImageSpacing()` returns the sitk object's own member, never re-read from the filter. SimpleITK's generated `ExecuteInternal` emits setters in yaml member order (`UseImageSpacing` before `DerivativeWeights`), so `SetDerivativeWeights` always runs second and wins. The class doc (`.h:77-80`) describes only the other ordering (`SetUseImageSpacing(true)` *after* `SetDerivativeWeights`, where spacing weights are re-derived at update time) — which SimpleITK never produces. | 2.38 | `TransformToDisplacementFieldFilter` linear fast path | The scan-line endpoint is one past the last pixel: it evaluates at continuous indices `(0, j, …)` and `(size[0], j, …)` with `alpha = i / size[0]` (`.hxx:213-273`) — exact (not approximate) because `T(p) − p` is affine exactly when `T` is linear; taken for speed and scan-line-consistent rounding. | 2.39 | `EdgePotentialImageFilter` precision split | **Refuted 2026-07-10 — no ITK precision split exists.** The original claim assumed `RealValueType` is `f32` for an `f32` component; in fact `NumericTraits<float>::RealType = double` (`itkNumericTraits.h:1349/1356`), so `GetSquaredNorm` accumulates in `double` and `std::exp(-1.0 * A.GetNorm())` (`itkEdgePotentialImageFilter.h:57`) is double throughout. | 2.40 | `VectorConnectedComponentImageFilter` functor | `SimilarVectorsFunctor` uses a raw, unnormalized dot product ("Assumes that vectors are normalized" is documented, and `Math::Absolute` *deliberately* makes antiparallel vectors similar per `.h:100-101` — not an omission). The undocumented case is the **zero vector**: `1 − |0| = 1` joins any neighbor under the wrapped default `DistanceThreshold = 1`. ITK's concept-macro at `.h:145` is misspelled `InputValyeTypeIsFloatingCheck` (sic). Filed as #6575 comment item Q28. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — a zero vector has no direction, so it is dissimilar to a directioned neighbor (a flat region no longer silently bridges/absorbs adjacent directioned regions on a gradient- or displacement-direction field); the fix guards *only* the mixed case, so zero-vs-zero is left to the ordinary predicate (distance `1 − |dot(0,0)| = 1`) and merges exactly when `threshold >= 1` — at the yaml default `1.0` an all-zero image stays one component, but at `threshold = 0.5` even identical zero vectors separate (it is `distance == 1 <= threshold`, not identity, that merges them; pinned by `zero_vectors_stay_separate_below_the_boundary_threshold`). The documented unnormalized dot product and antiparallel-similarity are kept. | `vector_connected_component.rs` |

| 2.44 | `WarpVectorImageFilter` edge padding dead | Under `VectorLinearInterpolateNearestNeighborExtrapolateImageFunction` all three `IsInsideBuffer` overloads return `true` (`.h:99-118`) and `EvaluateAtContinuousIndex` clamps the base index and zeroes the fractional distance — a displacement leaving the buffer extrapolates the nearest pixel and `m_EdgePaddingValue` is never reached. | 2.45 | `ESMDemonsRegistrationFunction` gradient types | `WarpedMoving` and `MappedMoving` gradients coincide at a zero displacement field: `WarpedMoving` hand-computes an index-space central difference over the warped moving image (`itkESMDemonsRegistrationFunction.hxx:294-296` — deliberately *not* via `CentralDifferenceImageFunction`, per the comment at `:206-207`), while `MappedMoving` calls `CentralDifferenceImageFunction::Evaluate`, which samples at `p ± 0.5·spacing` in physical space (`itkCentralDifferenceImageFunction.hxx:264-300`); under linear interpolation the ±0.5-spacing difference collapses to exactly the ±1-index central difference. Exact equality holds for **interior pixels, linear interpolation on both paths (the defaults), and coincident fixed/moving grids** — boundary rules differ (one-sided vs zeroed), and the divisors are fixed-image vs moving-image spacing. Filed as #6575 comment item Q33. Pinned. | `demons/fast_symmetric_forces.rs` |
| 2.46 | `LevelSetMotionRegistrationFilter/Function` time step and metric | The only family member whose global time step is not 1: `dt = 1/m_MaxL1Norm` (`.hxx:352-367`), and `m_MaxL1Norm` is initialized to `NonpositiveMin()` (`.h:150`) so a wholly-thresholded iteration falls back to `dt = 1.0`. Consequence upstream never states: at the pixel that *attains* the max L1 norm, with one dominant gradient direction, `dt·update[k] = ±mSpacing[k]` — the `(|g_k| + Alpha)` factor cancels **exactly there and only there**; every other pixel carries the ratio `(|g_max|+α)/(|g_p|+α)`, so Alpha-independence is exact at the governing pixel and approximate across the field. A thresholded pixel still counts toward `SumOfSquaredDifference`/`NumberOfPixelsProcessed` (`.hxx:313-325`, counted *before* the guards zero the update) while an out-of-buffer pixel counts for nothing (`:220-228`). `Halt` adds `m_RMSChange == 0.0 && elapsed != 0` (`Filter .hxx:80-88`), which fires even at `MaximumRMSError == 0.0` where the base's strict `>` never can. Filed as #6575 comment item Q34. All pinned. | `demons/level_set_motion.rs` |
| 2.47 | `LevelSetMotionRegistrationFunction` spacing semantics | One-sided differences step along physical axis `j` by *index* axis `j`'s spacing (`mPoint[j] += mSpacing[j]` on a `PointType`, `.hxx:253`) — the same borrowed-axis quirk as `CentralDifferenceImageFunction::Evaluate`. `UseImageSpacing` is **live** here for non-unit spacing (selects both the difference step, `:240-245`, and the L1-norm divisor of the time step, `:339`); under unit spacing it is inert (`Fill(1.0)` equals the spacing). The demons/ESM *functions* have no `UseImageSpacing` member at all — they fold spacing in unconditionally via `m_Normalizer` (`itkDemonsRegistrationFunction.hxx:122-127`, `:213`); the toggle exists only on the `FiniteDifferenceImageFilter` base and on this function. Filed as #6575 comment item Q35. Pinned: `use_image_spacing_changes_the_result`. **Determined (2026-07-11)** — not a policy trigger: `use_image_spacing` is *live*, not an inert parameter (it selects both the difference step and the time-step L1 divisor), so there is no no-op to make live; and the borrowed-axis physical step (`mPoint[j] += mSpacing[j]`) is a pervasive ITK convention (`CentralDifferenceImageFunction`-style) that is exact for the identity/diagonal-direction images these PDE-registration filters operate on and computes a well-defined physical-axis gradient otherwise — not silent-wrongness on realistic input, so left as faithfully reproduced. | `demons/level_set_motion.rs` |
| 2.48 | Demons family zero-iteration reporting | `LevelSetMotionRegistrationFilter` and `DemonsRegistrationFilter` do **not** override `GetRMSChange()`, so a zero-iteration run reports the base's value-initialized `0.0` (`itkFiniteDifferenceImageFilter.h:361`) while `GetMetric()` forwards (`itkLevelSetMotionRegistrationFilter.hxx:91-103`) to the function's ctor-set sentinel `m_Metric = NumericTraits<double>::max()` (`itkLevelSetMotionRegistrationFunction.hxx:50`); the three ESM/symmetric filters do override it. Filed as #6575 comment item Q36. Pinned. | `demons/level_set_motion.rs` |
| 2.49 | `SmoothingRecursiveGaussianImageFilter` in `LevelSetMotion` | Output pixel type is the moving image's — smoothing a `u8` moving image **quantizes the smoothed copy back to `u8`** before its gradient is taken; and it inherits `RecursiveSeparableImageFilter`'s throw on any filtered axis shorter than 4 pixels, making a 3-pixel axis a hard error for this filter and no other in the family. Filed as #6575 comment item Q37. | 2.50 | `FastMarchingImageFilterBase` `NoHandles` collapses to `Strict` | The handle test compares connected-component labels of the two facing alive neighbors, but `m_ConnectedComponentImage` is seeded only from `m_AlivePoints` (`.hxx:449-452`) — which SimpleITK's yaml never sets — and the only other write (`.hxx:371-380`) is downstream of the comparison that never reaches it, so `doesChangeCreateHandle` is unconditionally true and the two modes are one predicate through this API. Implemented as one predicate; pinned equal in 2-D and 3-D. Filed as B37 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `NoHandles` is now a live mode: a per-front union-find (`components`) seeded from the advancing front (unioned in `join_alive_neighbors` as each node goes alive) supplies the connected-component labels the handle test needs, so a strict violation is rejected only when the two facing alive neighbors share a component (a same-component self-closure around a barrier) and two distinct fronts are allowed to merge; well-composedness violations are still rejected by both modes. | `fast_marching_base.rs` |
| 2.51 | `FastMarchingImageFilterBase` speed handling vs the old filter | (a) `SetSpeedConstant` is inert: `m_InverseSpeed` initialized `-1.0` (`itkFastMarchingBase.hxx:32`) and never recomputed from `m_SpeedConstant` (unlike `itkFastMarchingImageFilter.h:305`); unreachable through SimpleITK (input image always set). (b) The zero-speed guard **changes the physics**: `FloatAlmostEqual(cc, 0.0)` substitutes `-sqr(1/(cc + eps))` (`.hxx:262-269`), so a zero-speed pixel gets arrival time exactly `2^52` — finite, written, made alive; zero speed no longer walls off the front (pinned with the exact `2^52`). | 2.53 | `LabelToRGBImageFilter` background color | Always fixed black despite the docstring's "gray pixel matching the background intensity" claim: `m_BackgroundColor` is a separate member, zero-filled at construction (`itkLabelToRGBImageFilter.hxx:37-42`) and unexposed by SimpleITK's yaml (no `BackgroundColor` member). | 2.54 | `LabelOverlayImageFilter` palette scaling | The color table is rescaled by the **base image's own** `NumericTraits<ValueType>::max()`, not a fixed 255 (`itkLabelToRGBFunctor.h:112-116`, `itkLabelOverlayFunctor.h:137`): a `Float64` base scales the palette into `[0, f64::MAX]`, an `Int16` base into `[0, 32767]`. Real, faithfully-ported behavior that is easy to mistake for a bug. Pinned. Filed as Q40 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — integer bases stay byte-identical (the `NumericTraits::max()` scaling is correct and visible there), but a **floating-point** base scales into `[0, f64::MAX]` and swamps the base pixel in the blend by hundreds of orders of magnitude — silent wrongness on realistic input. Since any float scaling rule (fixed 0–255, data-driven max) is invented semantics with no unique answer, `label_overlay` now rejects a floating-point base with the typed `FilterError::FloatingPointBaseLabelOverlay` (advising a cast/rescale to an integer type) rather than emitting the swamped output; pinned both ways (`label_overlay_scales_the_palette_by_the_base_images_own_numeric_max` integer-unchanged, `label_overlay_rejects_a_floating_point_base_image`). Same defect exists in the sibling `LabelMapOverlayImageFilter` (`label_map_overlay.rs::scaled_colors`), outside this row's scope. | `label_to_rgb.rs` |
| 2.55 | `DICOMOrientImageFilter` orientation machinery | (a) `GetDirectionCosinesFromOrientation` never validates: an unparseable string silently yields an **all-zero 3×3 matrix** (`OrientationToDirectionCosines`'s switch assigns nothing for `UNKNOWN` terms, `itkDICOMOrientation.cxx:258-259`; exposed via `sitkDICOMOrientImageFilter_Support.cxx:40-48`); (b) `SetDesiredCoordinateOrientation(string)` is two-stage — warns on an invalid string but still applies `INVALID`, deferring the throw to `VerifyPreconditions` at `Update()` (`itkDICOMOrientImageFilter.hxx:156-167`, `:296-306`); this port has no deferred pipeline, so both stages collapse into one upfront error; (c) `DirectionCosinesToOrientation`'s equal-magnitude tie-break is `std::multimap` insertion order via `rbegin()` (`itkDICOMOrientation.cxx:166-228`), reproduced with `max_by`'s last-of-equals rule. | `dicom_orient.rs` |
| 2.56 | `ObjectnessMeasureImageFilter` composite | (a) Uses `itk::HessianImageFilter` — discrete central differences, **no Gaussian smoothing** (`itkObjectnessMeasureImageFilter.hxx:63-68`), which is why the yaml exposes no sigma; (b) the Hessian computes in `RealType` but the diagonal's `p + m` sum forms in the *pixel* type first (`itkHessianImageFilter.hxx:107-113`) — a `Float32` input rounds that sum to `float`; (c) eigenvalues sort ascending-by-value then `std::sort` by `\|λ\|` (`itkHessianToObjectnessMeasureImageFilter.hxx:66-79`) — unstable, so equal-magnitude order is unspecified (libstdc++'s n ≤ 16 insertion sort is stable in practice; port stable-sorts and pins); (d) `alpha == 0` skips only the R_A exponential (factor stays 1) while `beta == 0` or a zero denominator zeroes the measure outright (`.hxx:96-130`); (e) `ScaleObjectnessMeasure` multiplies by `\|λ_n\|` after all three factors (`.hxx:132-135`). Filed as Q41 of #6575. | `objectness.rs` |
| 2.57 | `LabelSet{Dilate,Erode}` parameter quirks | (a) With SimpleITK's own defaults (`Radius = 1`, `UseImageSpacing = true`) both filters are the **identity** on unit-spacing images (neighbour parabola height exactly 0, ties go to self) — ITK's tests use only radii 3/5/41, so untested upstream; (b) `firstval` (first nonzero radius, `.hxx:339-347`) is decoupled from the first axis processed (first `scale[d] > 0`, `.hxx:364-375`): without spacing every axis runs, so `Radius=(0,k)` dilation still grows axis 0, and the same erosion blanks the whole output; (c) `doOneDimensionErodeFirstPass` never clears background positions (`itkLabelSetUtils.h:281-288`, no `else`, unlike the dilate twin), inheriting distances from the previous scan line — benign, reproduced byte-exact; (d) run detection narrows labels to `float` (`.h:297`/`:516`): `Int32` labels `16777216` and `16777217` merge into one run; (e) `DoLineDilateFirstPass`'s right pass reads *original* labels at the contact point (`.h:108`), not its own left pass's — agrees for binary seeding, fragile rather than wrong. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — **(b)** each axis's run is gated on `radius[axis] != 0` (not `scale[axis] > 0`), so a zero-radius axis is skipped and the first axis processed is `firstval`: `Radius=(0,k)` now dilates/erodes the named axis only, never axis 0 (pins `dilate_zero_leading_radius_dilates_the_named_axis_only`, `erode_zero_leading_radius_erodes_the_named_axis_only`); **(d)** run detection compares labels in the `f64` label domain, so `16777216` and `16777217` stay distinct and separate under erosion (pin `f64_label_comparison_separates_adjacent_int32_labels`). **(a) NOT fixed** — the `Radius=1` identity is an inseparable consequence of the open-ball rule (a voxel exactly `r` away is strictly outside the open ellipsoid), which is separately pinned as correct by `dilate_is_an_open_ball`/`dilate_2d_is_elliptical_not_separable`; "fixing" it would mean switching dilation to a closed ball, contradicting those pins — raised for sign-off. (c)/(e) kept: benign/fragile-but-not-wrong. | `label_set_morphology.rs` |
| 2.58 | `ComplexToModulusImageFilter` uses `sqrt(re*re + im*im)`, not `hypot` | `itkComplexToModulusImageFilter.h:49`: `(TOutput)(std::sqrt(A.real() * A.real() + A.imag() * A.imag()))`. Evaluated in the component type, so on `ComplexFloat32` the squares overflow to `inf` above `sqrt(FLT_MAX) ≈ 1.845e19`, degrade through subnormals below `sqrt(FLT_MIN) ≈ 1.084e-19`, and flush to `0` below `sqrt(FLT_TRUE_MIN) ≈ 3.74e-23` — none of which `std::hypot` suffers. Reproduced verbatim; pinned by `complex_to_modulus_overflows_on_f32_where_hypot_would_not` and `complex_to_modulus_underflows_on_f32_where_hypot_would_not`. Filed as Q42 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the modulus is computed with `hypot(re, im)`, which returns the true finite modulus where `sqrt(re*re+im*im)` overflows to `inf` or flushes to `0` on `f32`; pins renamed `complex_to_modulus_is_finite_on_f32_where_the_naive_norm_overflows` / `..._is_exact_on_f32_where_the_naive_norm_underflows`. | `complex.rs` |
| 2.59 | `AttributeUniqueLabelMapFilter` never removes emptied objects | The final "remove objects without lines" pass is written `while (it.IsAtEnd())` (`itkAttributeUniqueLabelMapFilter.hxx:239`) where it means `while (!it.IsAtEnd())`, so its body never executes. An object whose every pixel was claimed by a higher-priority object survives in the map with zero lines, inflating `GetNumberOfLabelObjects()`. `LabelUniqueLabelMapFilter` inherits this. Reproduced verbatim; pinned by `label_unique_keeps_a_fully_overlapped_object_as_an_empty_one`. Filed as B43 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the intended `while (!it.IsAtEnd())` pass runs, so a fully-overlapped (zero-line) object is dropped and `GetNumberOfLabelObjects()` is accurate; pin renamed `label_unique_removes_a_fully_overlapped_object`. | `sitk-filters` `label_map.rs` (`label_unique_label_map`) |
| 2.60 | `LabelMap::PushLabelObject` gap-search fallthrough | The last-resort scan (`itkLabelMap.hxx:414-434`) visits one candidate label per *existing* object, so it can exhaust the container without finding a gap. When it does, `SetLabel` is never called and the object is inserted under **the label it already carried**. The "label map is full" throw that follows is `if (label == lastLabel)`, which fires on that one coincidence rather than on the general no-gap condition. Both reproduced; the branch is only reachable when `last == NumericTraits<LabelType>::max()` and `first` is at the type floor or adjacent to the background. Filed as B44 of #6575. | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` (`LabelMap::push_label_object`) |
| 2.61 | `RelabelLabelMapFilter` docs contradict its implementation | The class doc says it "reassigns them to the output by calling the PushLabelObject method" (`itkRelabelLabelMapFilter.h:30-33`), and the yaml copies that text. `AttributeRelabelLabelMapFilter::GenerateData` (`itkAttributeRelabelLabelMapFilter.hxx:64-79`) actually calls `SetLabel` + `AddLabelObject` against its own `unsigned int label = 0` counter, which skips the background exactly once. | 2.62 | `LabelMap::HasLabel` docs contradict its implementation | The declaration claims "If the label is the background one, true is also returned" (`itkLabelMap.h:159-163`); the definition (`itkLabelMap.hxx:148-153`) is a plain `find(label) != end()` and returns `false` for the background. Implementation reproduced; in this port the background can never be a key at all. Filed as Q44 of #6575. | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` (`LabelMap::has_label`) |
| 2.63 | `StatisticsLabelMapFilter` weighted moments carry the pixel's own second moment | `StatisticsLabelMapFilter` adds `spacing[i]^2 / 12` to every diagonal entry of the central moments, commented "the normalized second order central moment of a pixel" (`itkStatisticsLabelMapFilter.hxx:224-228`). Its base `ShapeLabelMapFilter` accumulates a raw discrete second moment and adds no such term (`itkShapeLabelMapFilter.hxx:234-244`, `:260-276`). So on a *constant* feature image, where the two filters weight every pixel alike, `WeightedPrincipalMoments != PrincipalMoments`: under unit isotropic spacing the weighted ones exceed the shape ones by exactly `1/12` in each eigenvalue. Two measurements named alike on the same object disagree by construction. Both reproduced as written; pinned by `a_uniformly_weighted_object_exceeds_the_shape_moments_by_the_pixels_own`. Filed as Q45 of #6575. | `sitk-filters` `label_intensity.rs` |
| 2.64 | `StatisticsLabelMapFilter` extremum indices report the *last* tie | The updates are `if (v <= min)` and `if (v >= max)` (`itkStatisticsLabelMapFilter.hxx:117-127`), non-strict on both sides, so a tied pixel later in raster order overwrites the recorded `MinimumIndex` / `MaximumIndex`. Reproduced; pinned by `minimum_and_maximum_indices_report_the_last_tie_in_raster_order`. Filed as Q46 of #6575. | `sitk-filters` `label_intensity.rs` |
| 2.65 | `StatisticsLabelMapFilter` weighted elongation/flatness: one guard, no clamp, no sign check | Three deviations from the same computation in its own base class. (a) Eigenvalues are taken raw (`itkStatisticsLabelMapFilter.hxx:231-237`) where `ShapeLabelMapFilter` clamps with `std::max(pm(i), 0.0)`, commented "near-zero negative eigenvalues from numerical precision cause FPE in `std::pow`" (`itkShapeLabelMapFilter.hxx:315`). (b) Both `WeightedElongation` and `WeightedFlatness` sit under the single guard `NotAlmostEquals(principalMoments[0], 0)` (`itkStatisticsLabelMapFilter.hxx:261-267`) where the shape filter guards flatness on `principalMoments[0]` and elongation *separately* on `principalMoments[ImageDimension-2]` (`itkShapeLabelMapFilter.hxx:344`/`:353`). (c) Neither square root is preceded by the shape filter's `if (ratio > 0.0)`. Consequence: a signed or float feature image whose per-object `Sum` makes the weighted covariance indefinite yields `NaN` for both attributes where the shape filter yields `0`. `if constexpr (ImageDimension < 2)` (`:256-260`) is unreachable through SimpleITK (2-D/3-D instantiations only). All reproduced; pinned by `a_mixed_sign_feature_image_gives_negative_moments_and_nan_ratios`. Filed as B45 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the weighted computation now mirrors `ShapeLabelMapFilter`: eigenvalues are clamped with `.max(0.0)`, flatness and elongation are guarded separately on `pm[0]` / `pm[dim-2]`, and each root is taken only when its ratio is positive, so an indefinite weighted covariance yields a finite `0` instead of `NaN`; pin renamed to `a_mixed_sign_feature_image_clamps_the_moments_and_keeps_the_ratios_finite`. | `sitk-filters` `label_intensity.rs` |
| 2.66 | `itk::Statistics::Histogram::Initialize` narrows the bin width to `float` | `float interval = (static_cast<float>(upper[i]) - static_cast<float>(lower[i])) / static_cast<float>(size[i])` (`itkHistogram.hxx:214-238`, lines 225-226), and every bin bound but the last is `double(lower) + float(j) * interval` — so a `Histogram<double>` has `float`-quantized bin edges. `StatisticsLabelMapFilter`'s `Median` is the centre of a bin of exactly this histogram (`.hxx:173-196`, bin centre via `GetMeasurementVector`, `itkHistogram.hxx:462-472`), with `SetClipBinsAtEnds(false)` (`itkHistogram.hxx:255-290`) folding the image maximum into the last bin. | 2.67 | MetaIO cannot round-trip a complex pixel type as complex | `MetaImageIO` derives `ElementNumberOfChannels` from `GetNumberOfComponentsPerPixel()`, which is 2 for `std::complex<T>` — indistinguishable on disk from a 2-component vector. On read, `itkMetaImageIO.cxx:241-244` forces `IOPixelEnum::VECTOR` for any `ElementNumberOfChannels() > 1` and never sets `COMPLEX`, and SimpleITK's `sitkImageReaderBase.cxx:215-233` takes the scalar/complex branch only at `numberOfComponents == 1` (its later `COMPLEX` else-if is unreachable via MetaImage). Net: a `ComplexFloat32/64` image written to `.mha`/`.mhd` reads back as `VectorFloat32/64` — in ITK, SimpleITK, and this port alike. | 2.68 | `itk::ImageBase::IsCongruentImageGeometry` tolerance is asymmetric and axis-0-scaled | `itkImageBase.hxx:400-401` scales the coordinate tolerance by `this->GetSpacing()[0]` (inline comment: "use first dimension spacing"), so the predicate is **not symmetric** when the two images differ in `spacing[0]`, and origins/spacings on axes 1.. are judged against axis 0's physical scale; the direction tolerance is not scaled at all. | 2.69 | `DivideImageFilter::Div` zero-divisor branch | `NormalizeToConstantImageFilter` computes one scalar `divisor = sum/constant` and feeds it to `DivideImageFilter`'s per-pixel-vs-constant `Div` functor (`itkArithmeticOpsFunctors.h:142-151`), whose near-zero-divisor branch returns `NumericTraits<TOutput>::max()` **unconditionally** — regardless of the numerator's sign or magnitude, and regardless of whether the divisor is exactly, or merely near, zero. Since `divisor` is the same value for every pixel, a zero-mean or all-zero input image (finite nonzero `constant`) sends the *entire* output to the type maximum in one step, not `NonpositiveMin()`/`0` as a naive `f64` divide-then-saturate would give for a negative/zero numerator. Reproduced via an explicit `divisor == 0.0` branch; pinned by test. Filed as Q49 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the port rejects only an *exactly* zero divisor: `divisor == 0.0` holds for a zero sum against a finite nonzero `constant` **and** for a finite nonzero sum against an infinite `constant` (`sum/±inf == ±0.0`, `-0.0 == 0.0`); both are genuinely un-normalizable and now return a typed `FilterError::ZeroSumNormalization` instead of a silently wrong all-type-max image. ITK's degenerate branch is wider — `NotAlmostEquals(B, 0)` fires across `AlmostEquals`'s window (`|B| <= 0.1·eps` or 4 ULPs of 0; `RealType` is `double`, so `~2.22e-17`), which is *reachable* on legitimate input (a single `1e-18` pixel, or a near-cancelling difference image). In that nonzero-but-tiny-divisor window the port deliberately performs the ordinary finite division (`sum/constant` is a valid scale — the `1e-18` pixel normalizes to `1.0`) rather than reproducing ITK's type-max clamp, extending the same correctness-over-mirroring choice across the whole subnormal window. Pins: `normalize_to_constant_rejects_a_zero_sum_image_for_a_nonzero_constant`, `normalize_to_constant_infinite_constant_on_a_finite_sum_is_rejected`, `normalize_to_constant_tiny_nonzero_sum_normalizes_instead_of_itk_type_max`. | `intensity.rs` (`normalize_to_constant` section) |
| 2.70 | `VotingBinaryHoleFillingImageFilter`/iterative sibling unconditional stamp | The per-pixel rule's `else` branch (`itkVotingBinaryHoleFillingImageFilter.hxx`'s threaded loop, `:95-141`) is an unconditional `it.Set(foregroundValue)` for **any** center value other than `background_value` — not only an exact `foreground_value` center. A third, unrelated pixel value is silently promoted to foreground on every pass, and this stamp never contributes to `GetNumberOfPixelsChanged()`. Shared by both `voting_binary_hole_filling` (single pass) and `voting_binary_iterative_hole_filling` (its per-iteration rule), since both call the same underlying pass. Reproduced; pinned by test. Filed as Q50 of #6575. | `binary_morphology.rs` |
| 2.71 | `NormalizedCorrelationImageFilter` even-template zero pad | `sitkImageToKernel.hxx`'s `CreateOperatorFromImage` pads a single zero onto the **lower** side of every even-extent `TemplateImage` axis (`:55-65`) *before* computing the template's own mean/variance for normalization (`itkNormalizedCorrelationImageFilter.hxx:89-115` runs over the operator's full, padded coefficient set) — so for an even-extent template the padding zero is a real, counted data point in the mean/variance, not merely neighborhood-boundary filler. Deliberately exercised upstream by `NormalizedCorrelationImageFilter.yaml`'s `EvenKernel` test tag. | 2.72 | `MetaImage::CanRead` is case-sensitive where the factory is not | `ImageIOFactory::CreateImageIO` orders its probe with `HasSupportedReadExtension(path, /*ignoreCase=*/true)` (`itkImageIOFactory.cxx:62`), and `MetaImageIO::CanWriteFile` is `HasSupportedWriteExtension(name, true)` (`itkMetaImageIO.cxx:370-380`) — but `MetaImageIO::CanReadFile` delegates to `MetaImage::CanRead`, which re-tests the suffix with a **case-sensitive** `compare` against `".mha"` / `".mhd"` (`metaImage.cxx:1184-1199`) before it ever looks at the content. Consequences: `IMG.MHA` is writable but not readable; and because `CanRead` rejects on extension, factory phase 2 (the IOs that never advertised the extension) can never rescue MetaImage content stored under a foreign name. | 2.73 | MetaIO booleans read only the first character | Every `MET_STRING`→bool field in `MetaObject::M_Read` tests `value[0]` alone (`metaObject.cxx:1573-1643`; e.g. `BinaryData` at `:1605-1616`, `ElementByteOrderMSB` at `:1618-1629`, `BinaryDataByteOrderMSB` at `:1631-1642`, each `(v[0] == 'T' \|\| v[0] == 't' \|\| v[0] == '1')`). So `True`, `t`, `1`, and also `TRASH`, `treu`, `1234` all mean true, while `FALSE`, `0`, `yes`, `Y` and the empty value all mean false — `yes` is false, `trash` is true. | 2.74 | MetaIO alias precedence is `M_Read`'s apply order, not file order | When a header carries two aliases for the same quantity, the winner is fixed by the order in which `MetaObject::M_Read` consults the parsed field table, **not** by which line came last in the file. Each later block overwrites the same member: `m_Offset` ← `Offset` (`metaObject.cxx:1654`), then `Position` (`:1665`), then `Origin` (`:1673`) → `Origin` > `Position` > `Offset`; `m_TransformMatrix` ← `Orientation` (`:1681`), `Rotation` (`:1690`), `TransformMatrix` (`:1701`) → `TransformMatrix` > `Rotation` > `Orientation`; byte order ← `ElementByteOrderMSB` (`:1618`) then `BinaryDataByteOrderMSB` (`:1631`) → `BinaryDataByteOrderMSB` wins. (The four legacy aliases are additionally gated on `m_FileFormatVersion == 0`, `:1663`.) A header whose last line is `ElementByteOrderMSB = False` still reads big-endian if an earlier `BinaryDataByteOrderMSB = True` is present. Reproduced by applying the aliases in upstream's order rather than the header's. Filed as Q79 of #6575. | pinned by `alias_precedence_is_metaios_apply_order_not_file_order`, `binary_data_byte_order_msb_overrides_element_byte_order_msb` |
| 2.75 | An extracted slice's origin ignores the collapsed axis's index | `ExtractImageFilter::SetExtractionRegion` copies the start index of the **retained** axes only into the output region (`itkExtractImageFilter.hxx:78-83`, gated on `if (inputSize[i])`), and `GenerateOutputInformation` copies the *unshifted* input origin components (`:167`). The physical shift is applied afterwards by SimpleITK's `FixNonZeroIndex` (`sitkImageFileReader.cxx:41-67`), which calls `TransformIndexToPhysicalPoint` on the **output** image — whose index and direction no longer mention the collapsed axis. So a collapsed axis's start index never moves the origin: extracting slice `k` of an oblique volume reports the origin of slice `0`, and the direction cosines coupling the collapsed axis to a retained one are dropped from the shift as well. Reproduced. Filed as Q51 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the direction-preserving `ExtractImageFilter` path (`sitk-filters/src/geometry.rs::extract`, Submatrix collapse) now sets the output origin to the retained physical components of the full N-D `TransformIndexToPhysicalPoint(index)`, so an oblique slice `k` lands at its true world corner (pinned by `extract_collapsed_oblique_axis_shifts_the_retained_origin`); the identity-diagonal case is unchanged. In `sitk-io/src/reader.rs` the same origin drop is *not* independently fixable: that reader already discards the file's oblique frame for a reduced dimension via the deliberate §3.27 identity-collapse divergence, so no oblique world frame remains for the collapsed-axis shift to be correct in, and the common axis-aligned case is already right; the reader's origin drop is a §3.27 consequence, not an independent §2.75 defect (doc cross-reference updated). | `sitk-filters/src/geometry.rs` `extract` doc; `sitk-io/src/reader.rs` module doc |
| 2.76 | `CenteredVersorTransformInitializer::ComputeRotation` is a heuristic, not a guaranteed exact rotation recovery | `rotationMatrix = movingPrincipalAxis * fixedPrincipalAxis.GetInverse()` (`itkCenteredVersorTransformInitializer.hxx:47`) is `R = M·Fᵀ`, where `M`/`F` are each image's own row-eigenvector principal-axis matrix from `ImageMomentsCalculator::GetPrincipalAxes` (`itkImageMomentsCalculator.hxx:148-171`). Verified by index-notation derivation: this does **not** in general satisfy the covariance-aligning identity `R·Cov_fixed·Rᵀ = Cov_moving` — the rotation that would satisfy it is `Mᵀ·F`, not `M·Fᵀ`. Each image's principal axes are sign-canonicalized *independently* (largest-magnitude entry of every eigenvector forced positive, plus one whole-matrix determinant-parity flip on the last row, `.hxx:161-171`), with no cross-image consistency check — so even a non-degenerate pair of images with pairwise-distinct principal moments can come out with one output axis 180°-flipped, whenever the two images' independent sign choices happen to disagree. Confirmed a genuine property of ITK's algorithm (not a derivation error) via multiple independent hand computations; matches the class's own framing as an *initializer* (an initial guess), not an exact aligner. Reproduced verbatim; pinned by `compute_rotation_pinned_value_for_known_principal_axes` against a hand-derived, non-degenerate case (ITK's own test fixture ties two principal moments, making its result implementation/tie-breaking-dependent and unsuitable to mirror exactly). Filed as Q52 of #6575. | `centered_versor.rs` module doc |
| 2.77 | `itk::CompositeTransform::GetParameters`/`GetFixedParameters` read the queue **backwards** | `AddTransform` pushes to the back of the transform queue, and `TransformPoint` applies the queue back-to-front — but `GetParameters` (`itkCompositeTransform.hxx`) concatenates the sub-transforms' blocks in *reverse* queue order, so the last-added transform's parameters come **first** in the flattened vector, while `GetNthTransform(n)` counts forward. Two orderings for the same queue, in the same class. `SetParameters`/`GetFixedParameters`/`SetFixedParameters` follow `GetParameters`. Reproduced exactly, in all five methods; pinned by the composite parameter round-trip tests. Filed as Q53 of #6575. | `sitk-transform` `composite.rs` |
| 2.78 | `itkTxtTransformIO.cxx:172-180` parameter lists truncate silently | `Parameters:`/`FixedParameters:` values are read with `std::istringstream >> itk::Array<double>`, i.e. `vnl_vector::read_ascii` on a zero-sized vector (`vnl_vector.hxx:266-278`): `while (s >> value) allvals.push_back(value);`. The loop ends at the first token `operator>>` cannot parse, and nothing anywhere reports it — `Parameters: 1 2 oops 4` yields `[1, 2]`, and the transform is then constructed from a two-element vector. Reproduced by [`parse_doubles`], which stops at the same point, including mid-token (`3junk` extracts `3`, then the leftover `junk` fails the next extraction). Pinned by `parameters_parse_until_the_first_bad_token`. Filed as Q85 of #6575. | `sitk-io` `transform_io.rs` |
| 2.79 | `itkTxtTransformIO.cxx:181-223` parameter lines bind to the most recently *created* transform | The parser keeps one `TransformPointer transform` local, reassigned on every `Transform:` line, and applies `TmpParameterArray`/`TmpFixedParameterArray` to it only once *both* a `Parameters:` and a `FixedParameters:` line have been seen — in either order, across any number of intervening `Transform:` lines. A file whose first transform carries only `Parameters:` and whose second carries only `FixedParameters:` silently hands the *first* transform's parameters to the *second*, and leaves the first at its factory defaults. Nothing warns. Reproduced with the same state machine; pinned by `parameters_bind_to_the_most_recently_created_transform`. `ComponentTransformFile:` likewise does not update the local, so parameter lines after it still bind to the preceding `Transform:` line. Filed as Q86 of #6575. | `sitk-io` `transform_io.rs` (`read_transform_list`) |
| 2.80 | `itkTxtTransformIO.cxx:107-224` never validates the `#Insight Transform File V1.0` header | The header line begins with `#`, so it is discarded by the same branch that skips comments; the version is never read and no other line is required. Any file of `Name: Value` lines parses, and `CanReadFile` (`:37-44`) checks only the `.txt`/`.tfm` extension. Reproduced. Filed as Q87 of #6575. | `sitk-io` `transform_io.rs` |
| 2.81 | `itkTxtTransformIO.cxx:227-239` writes a trailing space for an empty vector | `print_vector` emits `v[i] + ' '` for all but the last element, then the last element — so it emits nothing at all when `v` is empty, leaving the `"FixedParameters: "` prefix's own trailing space at the end of the line. Every `TranslationTransform` file ITK writes therefore ends `FixedParameters: \n` with a space before the newline. Reproduced byte-for-byte; pinned by `a_transform_with_no_fixed_parameters_leaves_a_trailing_space`. Filed as Q88 of #6575. | `sitk-io` `transform_io.rs` (`print_vector`) |
| 2.82 | `NrrdImageIO` converts only RAS/LAS/LPS to LPS and silently passes every other `space` through unconverted | `ReadImageInformation`'s `switch (nrrd->space)` (`itkNrrdImageIO.cxx:767-787`, mirrored for the space origin at `:863-880`) has three live arms — `nrrdSpaceRightAnteriorSuperior` flips axes 0 and 1, `nrrdSpaceLeftAnteriorSuperior` flips axis 1, `nrrdSpaceLeftPosteriorSuperior` flips nothing — and a `default:` arm ("we're not coming from a space for which the conversion to LPS is well-defined") that is **empty**. It does not throw, warn, or set a flag. The three `...Time` variants (`nrrdSpaceRightAnteriorSuperiorTime`, `nrrdSpaceLeftAnteriorSuperiorTime`, `nrrdSpaceLeftPosteriorSuperiorTime`) are **not** among the case labels and therefore fall into that empty `default:` — upstream leaves them unconverted, exactly like a non-anatomical space. So `space: scanner-xyz`, `space: right-up`, `space: 3D-right-handed`, `space: gantry-XYZ`, the `-time` spaces, and every other `nrrdSpace*` value reach ITK with their space directions, space origin and measurement frame used **verbatim as if they were already LPS** — a `scanner-xyz` volume silently loads with its X and Y axes mirrored relative to what a DICOM-derived LPS reader would produce. (Corrected at the 2026-07-10 re-verification: the earlier claim that `NRRD_space` is added to the dictionary *only* in the `default` case is **wrong** — `:1022-1030` stores it whenever `space != nrrdSpaceUnknown`, writing `left-posterior-superior` when the geometry was converted and the original space name otherwise.) Reproduced verbatim: `nrrd_ras_space_is_converted_to_lps`, `nrrd_scanner_xyz_space_is_left_unconverted`. Filed as Q82 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the reader now converts every space with a well-defined LPS mapping (the anatomical spaces *and* their `-time` variants, whose flip is purely spatial) and rejects a named non-anatomical space (`scanner-xyz`, `right-up`, `3D-right-handed`, …) with `IoError::UnsupportedNrrdFeature` instead of loading it silently mis-oriented; the unknown space is still used verbatim. Pins renamed to `nrrd_rejects_a_scanner_xyz_space_with_no_lps_conversion` + `nrrd_ras_time_space_is_converted_to_lps`. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` module doc |
| 2.83 | `data file: LIST` reads filenames until EOF, so a blank line is an (empty) filename, not a terminator | `rnParse_data_file`'s LIST branch (`parseNrrd.c:1359-1398`) reads lines with `nrrdOneLine` and stops only at end of file: `llen == 0` is EOF, but a *blank* line yields `llen == 1` and an empty string, which fails no test. The blank line is appended to `io->dataFN` as the empty filename `""`, and the read then fails later, when `fopen("")` fails, with a message about a missing data file rather than about a malformed header. There is no in-band terminator for a LIST: everything to EOF is a filename, which is also why upstream's own writer (§2.84) cannot legally emit anything after a `data file: LIST` line. Reproduced (the empty filename becomes a read error). Filed as Q83 of #6575. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` module doc |
| 2.84 | `formatNRRD_write` emits comments and key/value pairs *after* the `data file:` field | `nrrdFormatNRRD`'s write callback walks the fields in `nrrdField` enum order and prints `data file` at its enum position, then falls out of the loop and prints the comments (`# ...`) and the key/value pairs (`key:=value`) unconditionally (`formatNRRD.c`'s `_nrrdFormatNRRD_write`, driven by `write.c:726-728`'s `nrrdCommentAdd`/`nrrdKeyValueAdd` stores). For the single-filename form that is merely unusual ordering. For the `LIST` form it is **corruption**: by §2.83 every line after `data file: LIST` is a filename, so the writer's own comment and key/value lines become filenames when the file is read back. Not reachable from this port, which never writes the `LIST` form — the detached writer always emits the single-filename `data file: <stem>.raw` — but pinned here because the `LIST` reader must tolerate it. Filed as Q84 of #6575. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` module doc |
| 2.85 | `TryDispatchNrrdReservedField` matches `NRRD_`-prefixed dictionary keys by leading substring | `itkNrrdImageIO::Write` walks the meta-data dictionary and, for each key beginning with `NRRD_`, calls a chain of `TryDispatchNrrdReservedField`-style handlers whose test is `strncmp(key, candidate, strlen(candidate))` against the *candidate* field name (`itkNrrdImageIO.cxx:292-311` and the `NRRD_` block at `:800-880`). Because the comparison length is the candidate's, `space` matches the prefix of `space directions`: a dictionary key `NRRD_space directions` is swallowed by the `space` handler and its value fed to `airEnumVal(nrrdSpace, "directions")`, which yields `nrrdSpaceUnknown` — the header's space directions are *not* affected, but the `space` field is quietly cleared. Symmetrically, `NRRD_pixel_original_axis` — a key the *reader itself* writes into the dictionary (`:255-262`) — matches no candidate at all and is silently dropped instead of becoming a key/value pair, so a read→write round trip loses it. Reproduced: the port's `dispatch_reserved` uses the same leading-substring rule and the same per-axis-then-scalar table order. Filed as B63 of #6575. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` module doc |
| 2.86 | A NIfTI image never carries `ITK_InputFilterName` | `ReadImageInformation` encapsulates `ITK_InputFilterName = "NiftiImageIO"` into the dictionary (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:1102`) and then, four lines later, calls `SetImageIOMetadataFromNIfTI`, whose first act is `thisDic.Clear()` (`:630`, commented "Necessary to clear dict if ImageIO object is re-used"). The key is wiped before any caller can see it — unlike `MetaImageIO`, which does surface it (§4.41). Filed as Q60 of #6575. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.87 | The writer's "original file was non-orthogonal" warning can never fire | `SetImageIOMetadataFromNIfTI` stores the flag under `ITK_sform_corrected` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:632`), but `SetNIfTIOrientationFromImageIO` looks it up under `nifti_sform_corrected` (`:2038`). The `ExposeMetaData` always fails, so the warning at `:2040` is dead code. This port writes the same `ITK_sform_corrected` key and, having no warning channel, drops the lookup entirely. Filed as Q61 of #6575. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.88 | `getQFormCodeFromDictionary` / `getSFormCodeFromDictionary` are dead stores that can still throw | `SetNIfTIOrientationFromImageIO` assigns both codes from the dictionary (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:1959-1960`) and then unconditionally overwrites both with `NIFTI_XFORM_SCANNER_ANAT` at the end of the same function (`:2077-2078`). The values are never read. But the getters parse the strings with `itk::StringToInt32` (`:1913-1945`), which throws on a non-numeric value — so a dictionary carrying `qform_code = "abc"` fails the write for a value that would have been discarded. Reproduced: `nii_write_rejects_unusable_dictionary_values`. Filed as Q62 of #6575. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.89 | Spatial-dimension inference ignores `dim[1]` for vector images and collapses a unit time axis for scalars | For an intent-vector image `ReadImageInformation` derives the spatial dimension from `dim[4] > 1 ? 4 : dim[3] > 1 ? 3 : dim[2] > 1 ? 2 : 1` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:786-805`) — `dim[0]` and `dim[1]` are never consulted, so a 2-D vector image one row tall (`nx=4, ny=1`) reads back as **1-D**. For a scalar image the loop trims trailing `1`s from `dim[0]` only while the index stays above 3 (`:820-824`, upstream's "HACK ALERT KW" comment), so a 4-D scalar with `nt == 1` reads back as 3-D but a 3-D one with `nz == 1` stays 3-D. Pinned by `nii_vector_image_one_row_tall_reads_back_as_one_dimensional` and `nii_scalar_4d_with_one_time_point_reads_back_as_three_dimensional`. Filed as B51 of #6575. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.90 | Non-finite float pixels are silently zeroed on read, on glibc only | `nifti1_io.c`'s `IS_GOOD_FLOAT(x)` is `#define`d to `isfinite(x)` behind an `#ifdef isfinite` guard, and `nifti_read_buffer` maps every non-good float/double/complex component to `0` (`nifti1_io.c:5036-5085`). On glibc `<math.h>` defines `isfinite` as a macro, so the guard passes and an ITK built on Linux really does destroy `NaN`/`±Inf` pixels; on a platform where `isfinite` is only a function the whole loop compiles out. Reproduced (glibc behaviour) and pinned by `nii_non_finite_pixels_are_zeroed_on_read`. Filed as B52 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `decode` no longer sanitises float/complex pixels, so `NaN`/`±Inf` survive the read verbatim instead of collapsing to `0`; the header-field `FIXED_FLOAT` (`fixed_f32`) is a distinct upstream behaviour and is left as-is. Pin renamed to `nii_non_finite_pixels_are_preserved_on_read`. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.91 | `IMG.NII` is writable to `CanWriteFile` and unwritable to `WriteImageInformation` | `NiftiImageIO::CanWriteFile` is exactly `nifti_is_complete_filename(name) > 0` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:218-223`), and `nifti_find_file_extension` (`nifti1_io.c:2590-2685`) accepts an all-uppercase extension (`allow_upper_fext` defaults to `1`) — so the factory hands `IMG.NII` to the NIfTI writer. `WriteImageInformation` then compares the extension with `operator==` against the lowercase spellings only (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:1175-1201`) and falls through to `itkExceptionMacro("Bad Nifti file name: ...")`. Same for `IMG.NII.GZ`, whose `IsCompressed` test (`:1173`) also searches for a lowercase `".gz"`. A mixed-case `.Nii` is not an extension at all, so no IO claims it. Pinned by `uppercase_nii_is_claimed_for_writing_and_then_refused`. (Had the name reached `nifti_makehdrname`, it would have been written lowercase: ITK passes it the extension-free `BaseName` (`:1204`), so the "invent one" arm — which always appends lowercase — is the only arm ITK can take.) Filed as Q63 of #6575. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.92 | A magic-less single file reports `nifti_type = 1`, not `0` | `nifti_convert_nhdr2nim` sets `nim->nifti_type = NIFTI_FTYPE_ANALYZE` when the header carries no `n+1`/`ni1` magic, but `nifti_set_type_from_names`, called at the end of the same function, overwrites it with `NIFTI_FTYPE_NIFTI1_1` whenever `fname == iname` (`nifti1_io.c:3452-3454`) — which is true for every single-file `.nii`, magic or not. So an Analyze-7.5 header stored in one file reports `nifti_type` `1` in the dictionary; only a genuine `.hdr` + `.img` pair keeps `0`. Pinned by `analyze75_single_file_reads_with_identity_geometry_and_a_coerced_nifti_type` and `analyze75_two_file_pair_keeps_nifti_type_zero`. Filed as Q64 of #6575. | `nifti.rs` |
| 2.93 | GIPL's magic number is read a second time and then never compared | `CanReadFile` seeks to offset 252 and accepts `GIPL_MAGIC_NUMBER` (`0xefffe9b0`, 4026526128) or `GIPL_MAGIC_NUMBER2` (`0x2ae389b8`, 719555000) (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:122-139`). `ReadImageInformation` re-reads the same four bytes at `:566-584` purely to leave the stream at byte 256 and discards them, so a file reached through `SetImageIO` (which bypasses `CanReadFile`) is read with no magic check at all. Pinned by `gipl_both_magic_numbers_are_accepted_and_a_wrong_one_is_not`. Filed as Q65 of #6575. | `gipl.rs` |
| 2.94 | GIPL's dimension count is a population count, and does not invert its own writer | `ReadImageInformation` increments `numberofdimension` for every `dims[i] > 0` at `i < 3`, plus `dims[3] > 1` (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:294-304`), then copies `m_Dimensions[i] = dims[i]` for the *first* `numberofdimension` slots. Two consequences. (a) `Write` pads the unused slots with `1` (`:709-729`), so a 2-D image written by ITK always reads back as **3-D** `[nx, ny, 1]` with spacing `[sx, sy, 1.0]` and origin `[ox, oy, 0.0]`; pixel values are unaffected. (b) A hand-written `dims = [4, 0, 5, 1]` yields `NDims = 2` and `m_Dimensions = [4, 0]` — the `5` is counted and never read. Pinned by `gipl_two_dimensional_image_reads_back_as_three_dimensional` and `gipl_dimension_count_is_a_population_count_not_a_leading_run`. Filed as Q66 of #6575. | `gipl.rs` |
| 2.95 | GIPL byte-swaps `image_type` only in the `BigEndian` arm, and never swaps `min`/`max` | `m_ByteOrder` is set to `BigEndian` in the constructor (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:78`) and nothing in ITK or SimpleITK changes it, so every field is big-endian. The `image_type` swap at `:325-328` has no `LittleEndian` arm — unobservable for that reason — while `min` and `max` (`:520-533`) are read with no swap at all. Both are discarded, as are `line1` (read one byte at a time), `matrix`, `flag1`, `flag2`, `pixval_offset`, `pixval_cal`, `user_def1` and `user_def2`, so `read_information` returns an empty dictionary. Filed as Q67 of #6575. | `gipl.rs` |
| 2.96 | `GiplImageIO::Write` ignores `m_NumberOfComponents` in the header but not in the byte count | The header writer (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:684-991`) emits `image_type` from `m_ComponentType` alone, while `Write` then streams `GetImageSizeInBytes()` bytes, which multiplies by `m_NumberOfComponents`. A 3-component `VectorUInt8` image writes `GIPL_U_CHAR` and three times the described bytes; reading it back yields a *scalar* image holding the first `numPixels` components and silently drops the rest. Pinned by `gipl_vector_image_writes_a_scalar_header_and_reads_back_scalar`. Filed as B56 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — GIPL is a scalar-only format (no multi-component `image_type` code; the complex codes are commented out upstream), so [`write`] now rejects any non-scalar image (`buffer_stride > 1`, covering vector and complex) with `IoError::UnsupportedGiplFeature` before writing a byte, leaving the target untouched, instead of emitting a scalar header over N× the data. Pins renamed to `gipl_vector_image_write_is_rejected` + `gipl_complex_image_write_is_rejected`. | `gipl.rs` |
| 2.97 | `GiplImageIO` advertises no extensions, and its real gate is case-sensitive | The constructor calls neither `AddSupportedReadExtension` nor `AddSupportedWriteExtension`, so `ImageIOFactory::CreateImageIO` only ever finds it in the second, extension-blind probe pass. The gate that matters is `CheckExtension` (`:1065-1093`), a case-**sensitive** suffix test for `.gipl` and `.gipl.gz` that doubles as the `m_IsCompressed` setter — `IMAGE.GIPL` is unreadable. `GiplImageIo::supported_read_extensions` returns `&[]` to match. Filed as Q68 of #6575. | `gipl.rs` |
| 2.98 | `VTKImageIO::GetNextLine`'s empty-line guard is off by one from its own message | The recursion counter test is `if (count > 5)`, and the message it throws is `"Exceeded maximum number of consecutive empty lines"` after *six* (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:46-84`). Five consecutive empty lines are tolerated. Pinned by `vtk_five_empty_lines_are_tolerated_and_six_are_not`. Filed as Q70 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.99 | A VTK header line with no terminating newline is a "Premature EOF" | `std::getline` sets `eofbit` when it consumed the last character without seeing a delimiter, even though it delivered the line. `GetNextLine` tests `if (ifs.eof())` *before* looking at what it read (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:56-60`), so a header whose final line lacks `\n` throws `"Premature EOF in reading a line"`. Pinned by `vtk_a_final_line_without_a_newline_is_a_premature_eof`. Filed as Q71 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.100 | VTK's 2-D/3-D test is written twice and the first copy is dead | `if (dims[1] <= 1 && dims[2] <= 1) SetNumberOfDimensions(2); if (dims[2] <= 1) SetNumberOfDimensions(2); else SetNumberOfDimensions(3);` (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:210-221`). The second statement subsumes the first, so the surviving rule is *2-D iff `dims[2] <= 1`*: `DIMENSIONS 4 1 3` is a 3-D image one row tall and `DIMENSIONS 4 3 1` is 2-D. Because the writer pads a 2-D image to `DIMENSIONS x y 1` (`:674-680`), a 2-D VTK image does round-trip as 2-D — unlike GIPL, §2.94. Pinned by `vtk_only_the_third_dimension_decides_two_versus_three_d`. Filed as Q72 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.101 | VTK's attribute dispatch is an ordered substring test, so an array's *name* can change how it is parsed | `InternalReadImageInformation` lowercases each header line and tests `line.find("spacing")`, `"aspect_ratio"`, `"origin"`, `"vector"`, `"color_scalars"`, `"scalars"`, `"tensors"` in that order (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:236-352`). `SCALARS vector_field float` matches `"vector"` first and is parsed as a `VECTORS` line: three components, the *third* token as the component type, and no `LOOKUP_TABLE` look-ahead. `COLOR_SCALARS` is caught before the `scalars` arm it textually contains. Any line matching none of them — `POINT_DATA 24`, comments — is silently skipped. The `LOOKUP_TABLE` line itself is a look-ahead consumed only if it contains `lookup_table` (`:331-339`), so it is optional. Pinned by `vtk_scalars_named_vector_field_is_parsed_as_a_vectors_line` and `vtk_scalars_without_a_lookup_table_line_starts_the_data_immediately`. Filed as B59 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.102 | VTK's `COLOR_SCALARS` write branch is dead through SimpleITK, and its read arm ignores the file's declared component type | `WriteImageInformation`'s `RGB`/`RGBA` branch (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:686-691`) is unreachable from `sitk::Image`, which represents every multi-component image as an `itk::VectorImage` (`IOPixelEnum::VECTOR`). Reading is fully supported and quietly overrides the type: `COLOR_SCALARS` sets `UCHAR` for a `BINARY` file and `FLOAT` for an `ASCII` one, whatever the line says (`:277-308`), with `1 → SCALAR`, `3 → RGB`, `4 → RGBA`. Pinned by `vtk_color_scalars_binary_reads_as_three_component_uint8` and `vtk_color_scalars_ascii_reads_as_float`. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.103 | A VTK round-trip collapses `ComplexFloat32` to `VectorFloat32`, and a 1-component vector image to a scalar | `WriteImageInformation` emits `SCALARS scalars <type> <ncomp>` for everything that is not a 3-component vector, where `<ncomp>` is the buffer stride — `2` for a complex image, since VTK has no complex type. The reader's `scalars` arm then maps `numComp == 1 → SCALAR` and anything else `→ VECTOR` (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:311-350`). So `ComplexFloat32` reads back as a 2-component `VectorFloat32` (as it does through MetaImage), and a `VectorFloat32` with one component reads back as `Float32`. Pinned by `vtk_complex_roundtrips_as_a_two_component_vector` and `vtk_one_component_vector_image_reads_back_as_scalar`. Filed as Q73 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.104 | VTK's component count is never range-checked | The legacy format documents `SCALARS`/`COLOR_SCALARS` component counts in `(1,4)`, and upstream's only acknowledgement is a `// todo this should be asserted or checked earlier!` comment on the write branch (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:703-706`). Neither reader nor writer enforces it: `COLOR_SCALARS color_scalars 7` reads as a 7-component `VectorUInt8`. Pinned by `vtk_color_scalars_component_count_is_unclamped`. Filed as Q74 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.105 | A negative literal in VTK `ASCII` data does not fail for an unsigned `PrintType` — it wraps | `ReadBufferAsASCII` extracts through `istream::operator>>`, i.e. `num_get::_M_extract_int`, whose overflow bound is `(negative && is_signed) ? -min : max` (libstdc++ `locale_facets.tcc:472-475`) and whose result is `negative ? -result : result` computed in the type's *unsigned* representation (`:576-583`). So `-1` into an `unsigned short` is `65535` with the stream still good, `-65535` is `1`, and only `-70000` overflows — to `65535`, with `failbit`. For the three 8-bit types `PrintType` is `int` (`itkNumericTraits.h:386/492/614`), so `-1` extracts as `int` and narrows to `255`, and `300` narrows to `44`. Pinned by `vtk_ascii_negative_literal_for_an_unsigned_type_wraps_instead_of_failing` and `vtk_ascii_unsigned_char_data_is_decimal_integers_cast_to_the_pixel_type`. Filed as Q75 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.106 | VTK `ASCII` *writing* silently drops precision | `WriteImageInformation` sets `precision(16)` on the `ofstream` it opens and destroys (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:640-712`); the pixel data goes out through a *different* stream opened in `Write` (`:721-736`), which keeps `ostream`'s default six significant digits. Unreachable through SimpleITK, which never sets `m_FileType = ASCII`, and not implemented here — `write` always emits `BINARY`. Filed as B60 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.107 | `ImageIOBase::ReadBuffer` declares `temp` outside the extraction loop, so one bad ASCII field poisons every later component | `PrintType temp;` at `itkImageIOBase.cxx:800` outlives the `for` that fills the buffer. The first `is >> temp` that fails leaves `temp` at `0` (bad or missing field) or at the saturated limit (overflow) and latches `failbit`; every later extraction is a no-op that leaves `temp` alone, and the loop keeps storing it. A short ASCII data block therefore zero-fills rather than erroring, and `SCALARS scalars short 1` data `5 99999 7 8` reads as `[5, 32767, 32767, 32767]`. Pinned by `vtk_ascii_latches_the_failing_extraction_value_into_every_later_component`. Filed as B61 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.108 | `VTKImageIO::CanReadFile` throws instead of returning `false` on a `.vtk` shorter than four lines | It calls `GetNextLine` four times with no `try` (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:88-100`), and `GetNextLine` throws `"Premature EOF in reading a line"`. `ImageIOFactory::CreateImageIO` does not catch, so `ReadImage("stub.vtk")` reports the EOF rather than "unable to determine ImageIO reader". `CanReadFile` also validates only the *fourth* line (`structured_points`), so a `TENSORS` or `HEXADECIMAL` file is claimed and then fails inside the reader. §4.71. Filed as B62 of #6575. | `vtk.rs` |
| 2.109 | `itkFFTPadImageFilter::GenerateOutputInformation` | `SizeGreatestPrimeFactor == 1` **pads each axis to an even size**, contradicting the filter's own documentation. `itkFFTPadImageFilter.h:84-87` and `FFTPadImageFilter.yaml`'s `detaileddescriptionSet` both say "A greatest prime factor of 1 or less - typically 0 - disable the extra padding", but `.hxx:64-68` reads `else if (m_SizeGreatestPrimeFactor == 1) { padSize += (region0.GetSize()[i] + padSize) % 2; }`. Only `0` (and, through SimpleITK's `int` -> unsigned `SizeValueType` conversion, any negative value) actually disables padding. Reproduced; pinned by `fft::tests::size_greatest_prime_factor_of_one_pads_to_an_even_size` and `fourier::tests::fft_pad_with_a_prime_factor_of_one_makes_the_size_even`. Filed as Q54 of #6575. | `fourier.rs`, `fft.rs` |
| 2.110 | `MaskedFFTNormalizedCorrelationImageFilter` vs `FFTConvolutionImageFilter` | The two FFT-based filters use **different, unrelated valid-length rules**. `FFTConvolutionImageFilter` seeds `m_SizeGreatestPrimeFactor` from the FFT backend (`.hxx:39`) — `11` under PocketFFT — and delegates to `itkFFTPadImageFilter`. `MaskedFFTNormalizedCorrelationImageFilter` ignores both: its private `FindClosestValidDimension`/`FactorizeNumber` (hxx:528-564) accept only factors 2, 3 and 5, under a comment ("These are the only factors that are valid for the FFT calculation") written for a backend that is no longer the default. So the same length 49 is padded to 49 by the convolution filter and to 50 by the correlation filter. Both ported as written; pinned by `fft::tests::padded_length_pins_the_documented_sizes` and `fft_correlation::tests::find_closest_valid_dimension_accepts_only_two_three_and_five`. Filed as Q55 of #6575. | `fft_correlation.rs`, `fft.rs` |
| 2.111 | pocketfft `general_c2r` (`pocketfft_hdronly.h:3566-3585`) | `HalfHermitianToRealInverseFFTImageFilter` **silently ignores the imaginary part of the DC column**, and of the Nyquist column when the output width is even. The scratch buffer is filled with `tdata[0] = in[it.iofs(0)].r` and, for an even `len`, `tdata[len-1] = in[…].r`; those imaginary parts are never read. A genuinely Hermitian input has zeros there, but a hand-built or edited half-spectrum need not, and nothing warns. Reproduced; pinned by `fourier::tests::dc_and_nyquist_imaginary_parts_are_ignored` and `an_odd_width_drops_only_the_dc_imaginary_part`. | `fourier.rs` |
| 2.112 | MetaIO writes a zlib stream but reads zlib *or* gzip | `MET_PerformCompression` calls `deflateInit(&z, level)` (`metaUtils.cxx:808`), which emits an RFC-1950 zlib wrapper — two header bytes, an Adler-32 trailer. `MET_PerformUncompression` calls `inflateInit2(&d_stream, 47)` (`:862`), i.e. `windowBits = 15 + 32`, whose `+32` enables zlib's automatic zlib/gzip header detection; the comment there says so. So a `.zraw` MetaIO itself produced is always zlib, while any gzip stream dropped in its place reads. This port writes zlib and auto-detects on read, pinned by `mha_compressed_header_is_upstreams_and_the_payload_is_zlib` and `mha_reads_a_hand_built_zlib_and_a_hand_built_gzip_payload`. Filed as Q80 of #6575. | `compression.rs`, `meta_image.rs` |
| 2.113 | gzip readers fall back to a byte-for-byte copy when the magic is absent | Neither gzip door errors on a non-gzip stream. NrrdIO's `check_header` sets `s->transparent = 1` when the two magic bytes are missing (`gzio.c:494-516`) and `nrrd__GzRead` then `memcpy`s the file through; zlib's own `gz_look`, behind nifti's `znzread`, sets `state->how = COPY` for the same reason. Consequences, both pinned: a NRRD declaring `encoding: gzip` over raw bytes reads those bytes verbatim (`nrrd_gzip_over_a_non_gzip_stream_reads_transparently`), and a `.nii.gz` holding an uncompressed NIfTI reads fine (`nifti_gz_reading_is_transparent_and_gz_detection_is_by_name`). The converse is not symmetric: `nifti_is_gzfile` is a pure *name* test (`nifti1_io.c:2656-2668`), so a genuine gzip stream named `.nii` is never inflated and fails to parse. MetaIO is the odd one out — `inflateInit2` errors rather than copying (§1.57 then hides the error). Filed as Q81 of #6575. | `compression.rs`, `nrrd.rs`, `nifti.rs` |
| 2.114 | `RegistrationParameterScalesFromIndexShift`'s learning rate mixes index and physical units | `EstimateStepScale` returns a shift measured in the moving image's **continuous-index** units (`ComputeSampleShiftsInternal` maps both the old and the new point through `TransformPhysicalPointToContinuousIndex`, `itkRegistrationParameterScalesFromIndexShift.hxx:70-82`), while `EstimateMaximumStepSize` — inherited unchanged from the base — returns the minimum virtual **spacing** in physical units (`itkRegistrationParameterScalesEstimator.hxx:48-64`). `GradientDescentOptimizerv4::EstimateLearningRate` then computes `m_MaximumStepSizeInPhysicalUnits / stepScale`, dividing millimetres by voxels. On an isotropic unit-spacing moving image the two coincide, which is why it goes unnoticed; on a `(2,1)` moving image the index-shift learning rate is 2× the physical-shift one along the coarse axis. Not a defect in the estimator (its *scales* are the point, and they are unit-consistent), but the learning rate ITK derives from it is dimensionally mixed. Reproduced. Filed as Q56 of #6575. | `sitk-registration` `scales.rs` (`ScalesEstimator::estimate_learning_rate`; pinned by `index_shift_scales_divide_the_step_by_the_squared_moving_spacing`) |
| 2.115 | `SetOptimizerScalesFrom*(centralRegionRadius)` is inert for every transform SimpleITK can register | `m_CentralRegionRadius` reaches the sample set only through `SampleVirtualDomainWithCentralRegion`, and `SetScalesSamplingStrategy` (`itkRegistrationParameterScalesEstimator.hxx:346-367`) selects `CentralRegionSampling` **only** when `TransformHasLocalSupportForScalesEstimation()` — a displacement field or a B-spline. A linear transform takes `CornerSampling`, anything else `RandomSampling`; neither reads the radius. And where the radius *is* read, a displacement field's local Jacobian is the identity at every grid-aligned sample, so `EstimateScales` returns `1` for any radius. So the argument SimpleITK surfaces on all three `SetOptimizerScalesFrom*` overloads (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.h:486/494/503`) cannot change a single scale. `EstimateStepScale` never reads it at all (`SetStepScaleSamplingStrategy` picks `FullDomainSampling` for local support). Reproduced: the radius is carried, honored where ITK honors it, and pinned as inert. Filed as Q57 of #6575. **Honored, faithfully inert** (2026-07-11) — the radius is threaded through and read exactly where ITK reads it, so this is not a code-level no-op to fix: a linear transform takes `Corner` sampling and never reads it, a displacement field reads it (central-region sampling) but its identity local Jacobian gives `scales = 1` at any radius, and a B-spline is modeled here as a global transform so it takes `Random` sampling and never reads it either; the inertness is a faithful modeling consequence shared with ITK, not a silently-dropped parameter. Giving B-spline transforms the local-support scales path (ITK's central-region sampling, where a B-spline's non-identity Jacobian *would* make the radius observable) is a possible future feature but a substantial one, out of this row's scope. | `sitk-registration` `scales.rs` / `method.rs` (pinned by `central_region_radius_is_ignored_for_a_linear_transform`, `central_region_radius_does_not_change_a_displacement_fields_unit_scales`, `the_central_region_radius_does_not_change_any_estimator_for_a_linear_transform`) |
| 2.116 | Optimizer weights within `1e-4` of `1.0` are silently discarded rather than applied | `ObjectToObjectOptimizerBase::StartOptimization` sets `m_WeightsAreIdentity = true` unless some entry differs from `1.0` by more than a hard-coded `1e-4` (`itkObjectToObjectOptimizerBase.cxx:152-166`), and `ModifyGradientByScalesOverSubRange` then takes the `1/scales[i]` branch, never multiplying the weights in (`itkGradientDescentOptimizerv4.hxx:213-226`). So `SetOptimizerWeights({1.00005, 1.0})` is exactly `SetOptimizerWeights({})`. The tolerance is a `>` comparison, so a difference of exactly `1e-4` is still identity. The sibling `m_ScalesAreIdentity` uses a 100× looser `0.01` (`:126`). Reproduced. Filed as Q58 of #6575. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (`weights_are_identity`; pinned by `weights_are_identity_within_one_ten_thousandth_inclusive`, `a_weight_within_the_identity_tolerance_is_discarded_not_applied`) |
| 2.117 | Every v4 optimizer validates the optimizer weights; only the gradient-descent family applies them | The length check and the `Size of weights (N) must equal number of local parameters (M).` exception live in `ObjectToObjectOptimizerBase::StartOptimization` (`itkObjectToObjectOptimizerBase.cxx:145-151`), which every v4 optimizer calls — `LBFGS2Optimizerv4::StartOptimization` forwards to it (`itkLBFGS2Optimizerv4.hxx:68-70`), `LBFGSOptimizerBasev4` and `AmoebaOptimizerv4` inherit it. But the weights are *consumed* only in `ModifyGradientByScalesOverSubRange`, defined on `GradientDescentOptimizerv4Template` (`.hxx:205-239`) and re-implemented on `RegularStepGradientDescentOptimizerv4` (`.hxx:182-214`). The vnl-backed optimizers — `LBFGSOptimizerBasev4` (so `LBFGSOptimizerv4`/`LBFGSBOptimizerv4`) and `AmoebaOptimizerv4`, all deriving from `SingleValuedNonLinearVnlOptimizerv4`, whose `StartOptimization` forwards to the base and then installs only `SetScales` on the cost-function adaptor (`itkSingleValuedNonLinearVnlOptimizerv4.cxx:53-58`) — therefore reject a mis-sized weights array and then ignore a well-sized one. (Corrected at the 2026-07-10 re-verification: the earlier claim that "**both** L-BFGS optimizers" ignore the weights is **wrong** for `LBFGS2Optimizerv4`, which derives from `GradientDescentOptimizerv4Template` and calls `this->ModifyGradientByScales()` in `EvaluateCost` (`itkLBFGS2Optimizerv4.hxx:154`) — it *does* apply well-sized weights. The claim holds for `LBFGSOptimizerv4`, `LBFGSBOptimizerv4`, and `AmoebaOptimizerv4`.) Note also that the required length is the metric's `GetNumberOfLocalParameters()`, not the transform's parameter count — `dim` for a displacement field, whose weights are tiled across every pixel block by the `j % scales.Size()` index. Reproduced. Filed as Q59 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the weights are now honored by the gradient family (gradient-descent folds them into its per-parameter step scaling; the two L-BFGS variants, which ignore that scaling, apply them to the gradient they descend via a `weighted_objective!` wrapper) and rejected for the gradient-free family (Amoeba/Powell/(1+1)/Exhaustive, which apply scales multiplicatively and form no gradient, so a folded zero weight would give `scales/0 = +∞` then `0·∞ = NaN`) with the typed `OptimizerWeightsNotApplicable`, rather than validated-then-dropped. A zero weight freezes its parameter *exactly* even for L-BFGS-B — a diagonally-initialized quasi-Newton method's two-loop recursion never gives a component with an always-zero gradient a nonzero search direction. The length validation and its ITK message are unchanged, and it precedes the gradient-free rejection (matching ITK, which validates length for these too before ignoring). Test renamed `lbfgsb_validates_the_weights_length_and_then_ignores_the_weights` → `..._and_applies_them`; new `lbfgs2_applies_the_optimizer_weights` pins the LBFGS2 path the row's 2026-07-10 note flagged. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (pinned by `lbfgsb_validates_the_weights_length_and_applies_them`, `lbfgs2_applies_the_optimizer_weights`, `displacement_field_weights_are_sized_by_the_local_parameter_count`, `gradient_free_optimizers_reject_explicitly_set_weights`) |
| 2.118 | §2.113's transparent-copy fallback extends to GIPL | `GiplImageIO::CanReadFile`'s compressed arm and `Read`/`ReadImageInformation` all reach zlib's plain `gzopen`/`gzread` (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:143-174`, `:210-243`, `:251-585`) — the same `gz_look` door NIfTI's `znzread` goes through — so a `.gipl.gz` holding a plain, uncompressed GIPL file is checked and read verbatim, magic number included, exactly as a `.nii.gz` holding a plain NIfTI is (§2.113). | 2.126 | A >4-component PNG write reads a declared-channel-count prefix of each row, silently dropping the rest | `WriteSlice`'s `colorType` switch on `numComp` has arms for 1-3 and a `default:` that always picks `PNG_COLOR_TYPE_RGB_ALPHA` — 4 declared channels — for anything else (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:579-600). Row pointers are spaced by the image's *actual* `numComp` (`rowInc = width * numComp * bitDepth / 8`, `:686-693`), so each row starts at the right offset, but `png_write_image` reads only `width * 4 * bitDepth / 8` bytes from each — leaving every row's trailing `(numComp - 4)` components' worth of bytes unwritten, with no error. | 2.127 | `PNGImageIO`'s constructor overrides its own header default and always expands a palette | The header's in-class initializer reads `bool m_ExpandRGBPalette{}` = `false` (itkImageIOBase.h:853), but `ImageIOBase`'s constructor calls `Reset(false)`, which unconditionally sets `m_ExpandRGBPalette = true` (itkImageIOBase.cxx:28,45) — `PNGImageIO`'s own constructor never touches the flag, so every instance starts with expansion on despite the misleading header default. | 2.128 | `HDF5ImageIO` stores three different axis orders in one group | `Dimension`, `Origin` and `Spacing` are `WriteVector`'d straight out of `m_Dimensions` / `m_Origin` / `m_Spacing` (`:1151-1161`), so they are in ITK order, fastest-moving axis first. Only `VoxelData`'s dataspace is reversed — "HDF5 dimensions listed slowest moving first, ITK are fastest moving first" (`:1170-1176`). And `Directions` stores `m_Direction[i]` as its **row** `i` (`WriteDirections`, `:489-510`), while `m_Direction[i]` is *column* `i` of the direction matrix (`itkImageFileWriter.hxx:188-194`), so that dataset is the transpose of the matrix. | 2.132 | Three of `ReadImageInformation`'s meta-data branches are unreachable | `WriteScalar(unsigned long)` stores `NATIVE_UINT` and tags it `isUnsignedLong` (`:322-342`), so no ITK-written dataset is ever both `NATIVE_INT` and `isUnsignedLong` — yet `:801-805` reads exactly that back as an `unsigned long`. And on every LP64 platform `H5Tequal(NATIVE_LONG, NATIVE_LLONG)` and `H5Tequal(NATIVE_ULONG, NATIVE_ULLONG)` are true, so the `NATIVE_LONG` / `NATIVE_ULONG` arms (`:874-897`) swallow every 64-bit integer and the `NATIVE_LLONG` / `NATIVE_ULLONG` arms below them (`:898-905`) never run. | 2.133 | A meta-data dataset of rank > 1, or of a datatype in neither list, is dropped without a word | `if (metaDataSpace.getSimpleExtentNdims() != 1) { continue; }` — "ignore > 1D metadata" (`:785-789`).
