| 2.139 | `PHOTOMETRIC_MINISWHITE` samples are read out un-inverted | `ReadGenericImage`'s grayscale arm is `PutGrayscale`, a plain `std::copy_n` of the scanline, directly beneath the comment `// check inverted` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:1400`, inside `ReadGenericImage` at `:1328`) — which never grew a body. A `MINISWHITE` page, whose `0` means white, is therefore loaded with its raw sample values and displayed inverted. The `tiff` crate *does* invert, so this port inverts back through the crate's own involution (`!x`, `0xffff - x`, `0xffff_ffff - x`). Pinned by `minis_white_reads_its_raw_samples_uninverted`. Filed as B81 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the raw, tone-inverted value is silently wrong, not a format quirk to reproduce; [`read`] now keeps the `tiff` crate's own already-correct inversion instead of reversing it, which also lets a 32-bit-float `MINISWHITE` page read (the former §4.101 refusal existed only to keep that reversal invertible); pinned by `minis_white_reads_the_true_photometric_value_not_the_raw_sample` and `minis_white_float32_reads_the_crates_own_inverted_value`. | `tiff.rs` |
| 2.140 | A multi-sample `MINISBLACK`/`MINISWHITE` page reads back as one component of half-rows | `GetFormat` branches on `m_Photometrics` alone and returns `GRAYSCALE` for `PHOTOMETRIC_MINISBLACK` whatever `m_SamplesPerPixel` is (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:111-114`); `ReadImageInformation`'s `switch (this->GetFormat())` then sets `SetNumberOfComponents(1)` (`:436-440`) and `ReadGenericImage` copies `m_InternalImage->m_Width` components off a `width * SamplesPerPixel` scanline. A grey+alpha page therefore yields, per row, the interleaved samples of its first `width / 2` pixels. Reproduced exactly; pinned by `two_sample_grayscale_keeps_the_first_half_of_each_row` and `page_rows_truncates_a_multi_sample_grayscale_row`. Upstream's own writer emits the mirror-image of this file — see §2.141. Filed as B82 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — dropping every sample past the first is silent data loss, not a shape to reproduce; [`layout_for`] now reports the page's true `SamplesPerPixel` for `GRAYSCALE` too, so a `MINISBLACK` page reads back as a vector image with every sample intact, and [`page_rows`] no longer has a truncating stride to reproduce. A `MINISWHITE` page is only readable where the `tiff` crate's `invert_colors` can invert it — single-sample `Gray` with an unsigned-integer or 32/64-bit float sample (decoder/mod.rs:713-769); a multi-sample (`ColorType::Multiband`) or signed / non-32-bit-float single-sample `MINISWHITE` page makes [`read`] error with `UnknownInterpretation`, so [`layout_for`] refuses it at `read_information` time too (`crate_can_invert_whiteiszero`) rather than advertising components [`read`] cannot deliver, symmetric with the `RGB` arm's `colortype()` decodability guard. Pinned by `two_sample_grayscale_reads_as_a_two_component_vector_image`, `page_rows_copies_every_sample_of_each_row`, and `minis_white_pages_the_crate_cannot_invert_are_refused_by_both_read_paths`. | `tiff.rs` |
| 2.141 | `InternalWrite` writes `PHOTOMETRIC_RGB` for *every* component count other than 1 | The photometric choice is `if (m_NumberOfComponents == 1) MINISBLACK else RGB`, with `SamplesPerPixel` set to the true count and `EXTRASAMPLE_ASSOCALPHA` appended only when it exceeds 3 (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:725-751`). A two-component image is therefore written as RGB with `SamplesPerPixel = 2` — a file no TIFF reader can interpret as colour, and which upstream's own reader takes back as a *one*-component grayscale of half-rows (§2.140), because `GetFormat` returns `RGB_` and `SetNumberOfComponents(m_SamplesPerPixel)` (`:441-444`) only when the photometric survives the reader. This port writes the same bytes; on the way back in the `tiff` crate refuses the file, so the port refuses it too (§4.102). Pinned by `tiff_write_of_a_two_component_image_emits_photometric_rgb_with_two_samples`. Filed as B83 of #6575. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — writing an unreadable file is a round-trip failure, not a shape to reproduce; a 2-component image now writes `PHOTOMETRIC_MINISBLACK` with `SamplesPerPixel = 2` and one `ExtraSamples::Unspecified` sample, a standard TIFF construct that [`layout_for`]'s §2.140 fix reads back intact; pinned by `tiff_roundtrip_two_component_vector_uint8` (renamed from `tiff_write_of_a_two_component_image_emits_photometric_rgb_with_two_samples`). | `tiff.rs` |
| 2.142 | Spacing survives a TIFF round-trip only to `f32` precision, and a `RESOLUTIONUNIT` without an `XRESOLUTION` yields a spacing of `25.4` | Two quirks of the same field. (a) `WriteImageInformation` stores `25.4 / m_Spacing[i]` through `TIFFSetField(TIFFTAG_XRESOLUTION, ...)` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:587`, `:794`), whose libtiff field `td_xresolution` is a `float`; `ReadImageInformation` divides it back out in `double` (`:379`). A spacing of exactly `1.0` therefore reads back as `25.4 / static_cast<double>(25.4f)` = `1.0000000150184933`. (b) `Clean()` seeds `m_XResolution = m_YResolution = 1` (`itkTIFFReaderInternal.cxx:175-176`) and the read guard is `m_ResolutionUnit > 0 && m_XResolution > 0` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:375`) — which that seed passes. A page carrying `RESOLUTIONUNIT = 2` and no resolution tag at all is thus assigned a spacing of `25.4 / 1`, not `1.0`. Both reproduced; pinned by `tiff_spacing_round_trips_only_to_float_precision`, `resolution_unit_without_a_resolution_tag_yields_a_spacing_of_25_4`, `resolution_unit_centimetre_divides_ten` and `double_to_rational_matches_libtiff`. Filed as Q108 of #6575. | `tiff.rs` |
| 2.143 | `MatlabTransformIO`'s second record is always named the literal `"fixed"`, and the name is never checked on read | `Write()` (`itkMatlabTransformIO.cxx:132-141`) writes the fixed-parameters record under the literal name `"fixed"`, never the transform's own type name or anything derived from it. `Read()` (`:75-123`) never inspects `mathdr2.name()` at all — only `mathdr2.cols()` is checked before `ReadMat` reads the vector. A `.mat` file whose second record carries any other name still reads back identically, as long as record order and column-vector shape hold. Reproduced, pinned by `the_fixed_record_name_is_never_validated_on_read`. | `transform_matlab.rs` module doc |
| 2.144 | `MatlabTransformIO` writes a `CompositeTransform` as one opaque record pair, never flattened — only an *empty* composite can be read back | `TransformFileWriterTemplate::Update`'s composite-flattening `CompositeTransformIOHelper` runs only on the float↔double precision-*mismatch* write path (`itkTransformFileWriterSpecializations.cxx:276-323`); the common double→double path this crate always takes has its own full specialization that pushes the transform onto `m_TransformList` **whole** (`:328-335`). `MatlabTransformIO::Write` therefore writes a composite as its own aggregate `GetParameters()`/`GetFixedParameters()` (`itkCompositeTransform.hxx:594-741`) under the name `CompositeTransform_double_D_D` — one record pair, no sub-transform boundary recorded anywhere in the file. Reading it back always constructs a *fresh, empty* `CompositeTransform` for that name (there is nothing in the file to reconstruct a queue from) and calls `SetFixedParameters`/`SetParametersByValue` on it exactly as for any other transform; an empty composite expects 0 parameters and 0 fixed parameters, so only an empty composite round-trips, and a non-empty one fails with a parameter-count mismatch on read. This matches upstream's own test coverage for this IO: `itkIOTransformMatlabGTest.cxx`'s only composite case is `WriteAndReadEmptyCompositeTransform`; no non-empty composite is exercised anywhere in ITK's own suite. Reproduced. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the write-then-fail asymmetry is closed at write: `write_transform` refuses a non-empty composite with `IoError::UnsupportedMatlabTransformFeature` (no unreadable file is produced), while an empty composite still writes and round-trips. Pinned by `an_empty_composite_round_trips_through_a_mat_file` and `a_non_empty_composite_is_rejected_at_write`. See §5.29. | `transform_matlab.rs` module doc |
| 2.145 | Unlike `.tfm`/`.h5`, `MatlabTransformIO` places no restriction on composite nesting | Because `Write` never special-cases `CompositeTransform` at all (§2.144), a composite containing a composite writes without error. `.tfm`'s `serialize` (`sitk-io` `transform_io.rs`) and `.h5`'s `write_one_transform` (`transform_hdf5.rs`) both explicitly reject a composite anywhere but index 0 — the flattening `CompositeTransformIOHelper::GetTransformList`/`BuildTransformList` shape upstream's own `.tfm`/`.h5` writers use enforces "composite is 1st or not at all"; Matlab's writer has no such helper in its path and thus no such check. Reproduced. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the §2.144 write guard subsumes nesting: a composite containing a composite makes the outer composite non-empty, so `write_transform` refuses it too. Pinned by `a_nested_composite_is_rejected_at_write`. | `transform_matlab.rs` module doc |
| 2.146 | `SetInitialTransformAsBSpline` scale factors: absolute, silently optional, never validated | Three behaviors of one loop (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod_CreateParametersAdaptor.hxx:163-193`). (a) **Absolute, not cumulative**: every level's adaptor is built before the run and each reads `bsplineTransform->GetTransformDomainMeshSize()` off the *initial* transform (`:147`, `:62-68`), so `requiredMeshSize = initialMesh · scaleFactors[level]` — `[1,2,4]` gives meshes `1×,2×,4×` the one the caller set, not `1×,2×,8×`. (b) **A missing or zero factor is a null adaptor, not an error**: `bsplineScaleFactor` is left at `0` when `m_TransformBSplineScaleFactors.size() <= level` (`:168-172`) and `CreateTransformParametersAdaptorBSpline` returns `nullptr` on `scaleFactor < 1` (`:43-46`), which `ImageRegistrationMethodv4` skips (`itkImageRegistrationMethodv4.hxx:327`). That level keeps whatever grid the transform carries in from the coarser level. (c) **Length is never checked** against the number of levels in either direction — `SetTransformParametersAdaptorsPerLevel`'s `itkExceptionStringMacro` (`itkImageRegistrationMethodv4.hxx:809-814`) cannot fire because the vector is built with exactly `numberOfLevels` entries, and factors past the last level are silently dropped. Contrast `m_ShrinkFactorsPerLevel.size() != m_SmoothingSigmasPerLevel.size()`, which *does* raise (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:842-845`). All three reproduced; pinned by `bspline_scale_factors_multiply_the_initial_mesh_size_not_the_previous_levels` and `a_zero_or_missing_bspline_scale_factor_leaves_the_level_unadapted`. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — behaviors (b) and (c) are the silent no-ops fixed: `execute_with_initial_transform` now validates a non-empty factor list against the level count and rejects a length mismatch (`BSplineScaleFactorLength`, in either direction) or a `< 1` entry (`BSplineScaleFactorTooSmall`), so the caller's per-level intent is unambiguous instead of silently skipping a level or dropping trailing factors; an empty list still means "no adaptation". The mesh-**absolute** semantics of (a) is unchanged, as required. Test renamed `a_zero_or_missing_bspline_scale_factor_leaves_the_level_unadapted` → `a_zero_or_short_bspline_scale_factor_list_is_rejected`. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (`set_initial_transform_as_bspline`) |
| 2.147 | The B-spline adaptor's required domain mixes the shrunk fixed image's origin with the full-resolution fixed image's extent | `CreateTransformParametersAdaptorBSpline` takes `SetRequiredTransformDomainOrigin`/`Direction` from `ShrinkImageFilter`'s output on the fixed image, but `SetRequiredTransformDomainPhysicalDimensions` from `fixedImage->GetSpacing()[i] * (size[i] - 1)` at **full resolution** (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod_CreateParametersAdaptor.hxx:53-84`). ITK's own multi-level B-spline test uses the identical recipe (`itkBSplineImageRegistrationTest.cxx:250-285`), so this is the upstream idiom rather than a SimpleITK slip. Two consequences neither states. (a) `ShrinkImageFilter`'s centre-preserving origin shift (`itkShrinkImageFilter.hxx:276-295`) moves the domain origin per level — for a 40-voxel unit-spacing axis the domain is `[0.5, 39.5]` at shrink 2 and `[0, 39]` at shrink 1 — so the transform domain *translates* as the pyramid refines. (b) The extent `spacing·(size−1)` spans voxel *centres*, whereas `itk::BSplineTransformInitializer` builds its domain from the ½-voxel-expanded bounding box (`sitk-transform` `bspline.rs`, `BSPLINE_TRANSFORM_DOMAIN_EPSILON`); so even a scale factor of `1` re-grids an initializer-built transform onto a strictly smaller domain — the outer half-voxel margin around the fixed image's voxel centres is no longer covered. Reproduced; the per-level grid origin and spacing are pinned in `bspline_scale_factors_multiply_the_initial_mesh_size_not_the_previous_levels` and `a_zero_or_missing_bspline_scale_factor_leaves_the_level_unadapted`. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs`, `sitk-transform` `bspline.rs` (`adapt_transform_parameters`) |
| 2.148 | `gdcm::StringFilter::ToString` and the meta-data dictionary loop (`dicom.rs` `string_filter_to_string`, `metadata`) | `GDCMImageIO`'s dictionary loop stringifies every readable tag through `StringFilter::ToString`. Three quirks are reproduced. (a) For a VR the filter does not special-case, upstream reaches `default: gdcm_assert(0)` (`gdcmStringFilter.cxx:411-421`), a **no-op** under `NDEBUG`, and returns the empty `std::string` the value was initialised with — an unhandled VR contributes an empty value rather than throwing; the port's `_ => String::new()` arm matches. (b) An ASCII value keeps its DICOM trailing-space padding — `ToString` truncates only at the first NUL, so `"MONOCHROME2 "` and `"1\2\3 "` reach the dictionary with the pad byte intact. (c) `FL`/`FD` floats format through `std::ostream`'s `%g` default (6 significant digits). | Reproduced; (b) is pinned by `metadata_dictionary_keys_and_values` and (c) by `default_float_formatting_matches_ostream`. | `dicom.rs` (`string_filter_to_string`, `metadata`) |
| 2.149 | `itk::ImageSeriesReader::GenerateData`'s non-uniform-sampling detector silently turns on meta-data collection mid-series, regardless of `MetaDataDictionaryArrayUpdate`, and the collected array's index no longer tracks the series position | `needToUpdateMetaDataDictionaryArray` starts `false` unless `m_MetaDataDictionaryArrayUpdate` is set (`itkImageSeriesReader.hxx:294-295`), but the per-slice loop compares each slice's own real (never `ITK_ImageOrigin`-overridden) origin to the *previous* slice's and, whenever that disagrees with the spacing `GenerateOutputInformation` derived from the first/last files (itself possibly built from an *overridden* `position1`/`positionN`, `:159-160`, `:172-173`), sets `needToUpdateMetaDataDictionaryArray = true` unconditionally — no re-check of the caller's setting (`:439-452`). Only slices processed *after* that point are pushed onto `m_InternalMetaDataDictionaries` (`:465-475`); nothing is back-filled for the slices read before activation. So `GetMetaDataDictionaryArray()[k]` means "the `k`-th slice whose dictionary happened to be collected," not "slice `k` of the series," the moment any two adjacent real origins disagree with the declared spacing — which an `ITK_ImageOrigin` override at just the first/last files can trigger even for a file set the caller considers uniform. | `image_series_reader.rs` (`ImageSeriesReader::execute`, `ImageSeriesReader::meta_data_keys`); pinned by `non_uniform_sampling_activates_collection_mid_series_and_shifts_the_slice_index` and `meta_data_dictionary_array_update_off_collects_nothing_when_spacing_is_uniform` |
| 2.150 | `itk::ImageSeriesWriter::WriteFiles` replaces a singular 2×2 direction submatrix with the identity, by upstream's own admission arbitrarily | Slicing the top-left 2×2 submatrix out of a 3×3 direction matrix can produce a singular matrix (e.g. a direction whose Z column is not orthogonal to X/Y in a way that survives truncation); when `vnl_determinant(direction.GetVnlMatrix()) == 0.0` exactly, `WriteFiles` calls `direction.SetIdentity()` (`itkImageSeriesWriter.hxx:210-220`), with its own comment stating "replacing the orientation with an identity is as arbitrary as any other choice." Every non-singular submatrix, however skewed, passes through unmodified — there is no orthogonality correction, only this one degenerate-case fallback. | `image_series_writer.rs` (`project_2d_geometry`); pinned by `singular_2x2_submatrix_falls_back_to_identity` |
| 2.151 | `LabelMapOverlayImageFilter`/`LabelMapContourOverlayImageFilter` palette scaling swamps a floating-point feature | The sibling of §2.54: the output pixel type is `RGBPixel<typename TFeatureImage::PixelType>` (`itkLabelMapOverlayImageFilter.h:57-58`), so the shared `LabelOverlayFunctor`'s `m_RGBFunctor.AddColor` scales every palette byte by `NumericTraits<FeaturePixelType>::max()` (`itkLabelToRGBFunctor.h:112-116`), keyed on the **feature** image's own component type. For every integer feature this is faithful and visible (a `UInt16` feature scales the palette into `[0, 65535]`). But a **floating-point** feature scales into `[0, f64::MAX]`, which swamps the feature pixel in the blend `opaque*opacity + p1*(1-opacity)` by hundreds of orders of magnitude and makes the overlay meaningless — the identical silent-wrongness §2.54 documents for `LabelOverlayImageFilter`, in a different filter. Verified against ITK source 2026-07-11 (`itkLabelMapOverlayImageFilter.h`/`.hxx`, `itkLabelOverlayFunctor.h`). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the same honor-or-reject rule as §2.54: integer features stay byte-identical, but a scalar floating-point feature is rejected with the typed `FilterError::FloatingPointFeatureLabelMapOverlay` (advising a cast/rescale to an integer type) rather than emitting the swamped output. The guard lives in the single shared owner `overlay_onto`, so it covers both `label_map_overlay` and `label_map_contour_overlay`; a complex/vector feature still falls through to the existing scalar-required error. Pinned both ways (`label_map_overlay_rescales_the_palette_to_the_feature_types_max` integer-unchanged on a `UInt16` feature, `label_map_overlay_rejects_a_floating_point_feature_image` for f32 and f64). New finding (this port's sibling audit of §2.54); not yet filed upstream. | `sitk-filters` `label_map_overlay.rs` (`overlay_onto`) |
| 2.152 | `gdcm::PixelFormat::SetBitsStored` silently remaps bitmask-spelled Bits Stored values and drops out-of-range ones | `SetBitsStored` (`gdcmPixelFormat.h:134-149`, vendored under ITK `Modules/ThirdParty/GDCM`) normalizes a `(0028,0101)` Bits Stored that is spelled as a bitmask rather than a count — `0xffff→16`, `0x0fff→12`, `0x00ff→8` (a defensive remap for FUJIFILM CR MONO1 files) — and then ignores the assignment entirely unless `bs <= BitsAllocated && bs != 0` (with `HighBit` re-derived as `bs-1`). A conforming consumer that read the tag verbatim would instead compute `2^BitsStored`-shaped mins/maxes from the raw bitmask (e.g. `1 << 0xffff`), which is exactly the overflow GDCM's remap exists to prevent. Found 2026-07-11 while auditing this port's own DICOM reader, which had ported the sibling `SetBitsAllocated` normalization but assigned Bits Stored raw — a debug-build shift panic (release: garbage min/max mis-driving pixel-type promotion) on the FUJIFILM class, reachable whenever Rescale Slope/Intercept is present. **Reproduced** (2026-07-11) — `dicom.rs` `set_bits_stored` now applies the same three remaps and the same guard; pinned by `set_bits_stored_remaps_fujifilm_bitmask_and_guards`. | `sitk-io` `dicom.rs` (`set_bits_stored`) |

## 3. SimpleITK wrapping issues

All nine items re-verified against SimpleITK master `3e193179` / ITK master
`e46eb723a5` and reported upstream 2026-07-10 as
[SimpleITK/SimpleITK#2625](https://github.com/SimpleITK/SimpleITK/issues/2625)
(issue items S1–S10; 3.7 filed as two items S4/S5).

| # | Site | Finding | doc |
|---|---|---|---|
| 3.1 | `{Landweber,ProjectedLandweber,RichardsonLucy}DeconvolutionImageFilter.yaml` | Exposes `OutputRegionMode` although the ITK base discards it (§1.17) — a dead parameter in the public API. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the parameter is live: §1.17's fix threads `OutputRegionMode` through the iterative deconvolvers, so the exposed knob now has its documented effect. | `deconvolution.rs` |
| 3.2 | `ThresholdSegmentationLevelSetImageFilter.yaml` | `EdgeWeight` and the three smoothing parameters are not exposed and ITK's constructor sets `EdgeWeight = 0` — the entire smoothing branch of `CalculateSpeedImage` is unreachable through SimpleITK. Branch not ported (documented). Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `level_set/mod.rs` |
| 3.3 | `sitkSTLVectorToITK` (`sitkTemplateFunctions.h:95-112`) | Per-axis vector parameters: too-short throws, too-long is truncated. The truncation is documented in the helper's own doc comment (`:91-93`) — the issue is that nothing at the public filter API re-checks length, so e.g. a 4-element `Size` on a 3-D `RegionOfInterest` call is quietly cut to 3 (setter is a plain store, `MemberGetSetDeclarations.h.jinja:31-32`). This port requires exact length instead. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `sources.rs` |
| 3.4 | `*ProjectionImageFilter.yaml` | `ProjectionDimension` default `0u` + unconditional `SetProjectionDimension` makes the §1.1 unsigned wraparound live for every default call — plain-ITK users who never call the setter get the (sane) last-axis default instead. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `projection.rs` |
| 3.5 | `ThresholdSegmentationLevelSetImageFilter` yaml/doc | Inherits ITK's wrong sign-convention statement (§2.3). Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `level_set/mod.rs` |
| 3.6 | `ReinitializeLevelSetImageFilter.yaml` | Exposes `InputNarrowBandwidth` and the generated code does call `SetInputNarrowBandwidth` — but its only read site (`.hxx:239`) is gated on `m_NarrowBanding && m_InputNarrowBand` (`.hxx:236`), and `m_InputNarrowBand` is settable solely via the unexposed `SetInputNarrowBand(NodeContainer*)` overload (`.h:122`), permanently null through SimpleITK — the parameter is **inert**. (`OutputNarrowBandwidth` is effective: read unconditionally at `.hxx:252`.) Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `reinitialize_level_set.rs` |
| 3.7 | `FastMarchingUpwindGradientImageFilter.yaml` | Never turns on `GenerateGradientImage`, so SimpleITK's `GetGradientImage()` measurement always returns an **unallocated** image; and `number_of_targets` maps only to `NoTargets`/`OneTarget`/`SomeTargets(min(n, len))`, making `AllTargets` unreachable through SimpleITK. This port exposes the flag and derives the mode the same way. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `fast_marching_upwind_gradient.rs` |
| 3.8 | `CoherenceEnhancingDiffusionImageFilter.yaml` | The doc's CED/EED formulas are **swapped** (the "Coherence Enhancing Diffusion" heading carries EED's `g(μᵢ − μ_min)`, `g(s) = 1 − (1−α)e^{−(λ/s)^m}` and vice versa). The current ITK header doc matches the code; only the yaml (generated from an older doc revision) is swapped. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `coherence_enhancing_diffusion.rs` |
| 3.9 | `PatchBasedDenoisingImageFilter.yaml` | The generated doc says `NoiseModel` "Defaults to GAUSSIAN" (`:82`) and `KernelBandwidthEstimation` "Defaults to true" (`:123`) — the yaml's own defaults (and ITK's constructor) are `NOMODEL` and `false`. Combined with §2.27, a user who *sets* GAUSSIAN/POISSON with the default 1 iteration still gets no noise-model effect. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 issue body (items S1–S10). | `patch_based_denoising.rs` |
| 3.10 | `TransformToDisplacementFieldFilter.yaml` | The `Size` default is `std::vector<unsigned int>(3, 64)` while ITK zero-fills `m_Size` (`.hxx:36`, empty image) — the two defaults disagree. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S11 (2026-07-10). This port follows SimpleITK, taken per the transform's dimension rather than always three-long. | `transform_to_displacement_field.rs` |
| 3.11 | `VectorConfidenceConnectedImageFilter.yaml` | `Multiplier` default `4.5` does not match ITK's constructor default `2.5` (`.hxx:36`). Documentation-only for this port (`multiplier` is a required explicit parameter), but a caller porting from either source could reasonably expect the other value. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S12 (2026-07-10). | `region_growing.rs` (`vector_confidence_connected` section) |
| 3.12 | `sitkPixelIDTypeLists.h:143` `RealVectorPixelIDTypeList` | `{VectorFloat32, VectorFloat64}` — SimpleITK's warp accepts only float displacement fields. An instantiation list, not a runtime check; ITK's template accepts any vector component type. This port enforces only vector-ness (see §4.17). Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S13 (2026-07-10). | `warp.rs:153-159` |
| 3.13 | `sitkLabelFunctorUtils.hxx` colormap loop | `SetLabelFunctorFromColormap`'s doc says a colormap length not divisible by 3 has its "remainder … ignored" (`:26-32`), but the loop reads `colormap[i+1]`/`colormap[i+2]` unconditionally on its last iteration (`:38-46`) — an out-of-bounds `std::vector` read (C++ UB) for lengths ≡ 1 or 2 (mod 3). Affects `LabelToRGB`/`LabelOverlay`'s `SetColormap`. Found after the #2625 report, not yet filed. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S15 (2026-07-10). | diverged (the *documented* behavior via `chunks_exact(3)`) | `label_to_rgb.rs` |
| 3.14 | `LabelSet{Dilate,Erode}ImageFilter.yaml` | `UseImageSpacing` defaults to `true` in both yamls, contradicting ITK's constructor default `false` (`itkLabelSetMorphBaseImageFilter.hxx:51`). Combined with §2.57(a), the SimpleITK default configuration is the identity on unit-spacing images. Port follows the yaml. Found after the #2625 report, not yet filed. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S45 (2026-07-10); the no-op consequence recorded in §2.57(a) was not re-verified and was therefore not asserted in that comment. | `label_set_morphology.rs` |
| 3.15 | `sitkSTLToITKDirection` empty-vector special case | An **empty** direction vector is silently `SetIdentity()` while every other wrong length throws (`sitkTemplateFunctions.h:187-207`) — so `GetOrientationFromDirectionCosines(std::vector<double>())` returns `"LPS"` instead of erroring. Found after the #2625 report, not yet filed. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 third comment's closing observations paragraph (2026-07-10). | `dicom_orient.rs` |
| 3.16 | `ComplexToPhaseImageFilter.yaml` `briefdescription` | Reads "Computes pixel-wise the modulus of a complex image" — copy-pasted from `ComplexToModulusImageFilter.yaml`. The filter computes `std::atan2(A.imag(), A.real())` (`itkComplexToPhaseImageFilter.h:50`). Documentation-only; the port implements the phase. Found after the #2625 report, not yet filed. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S20 (2026-07-10). | `complex.rs` |
| 3.17 | `LabelIntensityStatisticsImageFilter.yaml` | `NumberOfBins` is defaulted to a flat `128` for every pixel type. ITK's own default is `GetDefaultNumberOfBins()`, which is `1 << (8 * sizeof(FeaturePixelType))` for integral types of at most 2 bytes and `128` otherwise (`itkStatisticsLabelMapFilter.h:136-140`) — the value that also switches on the integer-centred bin bounds `[min - 0.5, max + 0.5]` (`itkStatisticsLabelMapFilter.hxx:74-85`). So through SimpleITK an 8-bit or 16-bit feature image silently loses ITK's default integer-exact `Median`, and the padded-bounds branch is reachable only by explicitly asking for 256 (resp. 65536) bins. The yaml's `detaileddescriptionSet` (`LabelIntensityStatisticsImageFilter.yaml:55-61`) warns the option "may have an effect on the value of the median" without saying the default was changed. This port follows the yaml. Filed in the SimpleITK #2625 third comment's closing observations paragraph (2026-07-10). | `sitk-filters` `label_intensity.rs` |
| 3.18 | `LabelMapContourOverlayImageFilter.yaml` | Two members whose yaml default contradicts both ITK and the yaml's own prose. (a) `SliceDimension` defaults to `0u` where ITK's is `ImageDimension - 1` (`itkLabelMapContourOverlayImageFilter.hxx:43`), and the yaml's `detaileddescriptionSet` still reads "defaults to image dimension - 1". Because the generated code always calls the setter, and because of §1.41, **every SimpleITK `SLICE_CONTOUR` run at the default `SliceDimension` draws nothing** and returns the plain grey feature image. (b) `DilationRadius` defaults to `std::vector<unsigned int>(3, 1)` where ITK's is all-zero (`.hxx:48-49`), and the yaml's own `detaileddescriptionSet` says "Set/Get the object dilation radius - 0 by default" — so SimpleITK silently dilates every object by one pixel before contouring. This port follows the yaml for both. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S19 (2026-07-10). | `sitk-filters` `label_map_overlay.rs` |
| 3.19 | `GradientImageFilter.yaml` / `GradientRecursiveGaussianImageFilter.yaml` `UseImageDirection` | Both yamls set `default: 'false'` (`GradientImageFilter.yaml:23-25`, `GradientRecursiveGaussianImageFilter.yaml:29-31`) while their own `detaileddescriptionSet`/`detaileddescriptionGet` prose says verbatim "The default value of this flag is On" (`GradientImageFilter.yaml:28-32/35-39`, `GradientRecursiveGaussianImageFilter.yaml:34-38/41-45`) — the yaml's default contradicts its own embedded documentation, and both also disagree with the ITK class default `true` (`itkGradientImageFilter.h:226`, `itkGradientRecursiveGaussianImageFilter.h:257`). Because generated SimpleITK code always calls the setter, every default-parameter SimpleITK call to either filter computes derivatives/gradients with respect to the **index grid**, not physical space, despite the class's own header and the yaml's own prose describing the opposite. This port follows the yaml default (`false`) for both `gradient` and `gradient_recursive_gaussian`, pinned by `gradient_yaml_default_use_image_direction_false_does_not_rotate` and `grg_yaml_default_use_image_direction_false_does_not_rotate`. | 3.21 | `ToVectorImage`/`ToScalarImage` silently drop `spacing[0]`/`origin[0]` and the metadata dictionary | `ToVectorImage` discards `spacing[0]` and `origin[0]`; `ToScalarImage` substitutes `1.0`/`0.0` for them (`sitkImageConvert.hxx:96-110/:148-162`), so `img.ToVectorImage().ToScalarImage()` is a lossy round trip with no warning; neither converter copies the meta-data dictionary. | 3.22 | `ToScalarImage`'s complex pass-through branch is dead code | `ToScalarInternal` has an `if constexpr (IsBasic<TImageType>::Value) return *this;` branch that a complex image satisfies (`sitkPixelIDTokens.h:39-49`), but the member-function factory registers only `ScalarPixelIDTypeList ++ VectorPixelIDTypeList` (`sitkImageExplicit.cxx:143-148`), so a complex image throws before reaching it. | 3.23 | `LabelMapMaskImageFilter.yaml` `BackgroundValue` is cast to the *label* type, not the output type | The yaml marks `BackgroundValue` `pixeltype: Output` (`LabelMapMaskImageFilter.yaml:29-32`), which `ExecuteInternalSetITKFilterParameters.cxx.jinja` expands to `static_cast<typename OutputImageType::PixelType>(...)` — but the yaml declares no `output_image_type`/`output_pixel_type`, so `sitkDualImageFilterTemplate.cxx.jinja`'s fallback binds `OutputImageType` to the input `itk::LabelMap`, whose `PixelType` is its `LabelType`. The caller's `double` is narrowed to the label type before the filter converts it to the feature pixel type: a negative `background_value` can never reach a signed feature image, and a value above the label type's range wraps. The yaml's `FeatureImage` input carries a `custom_itk_cast` spelling `typename FilterType::OutputImageType` explicitly, so the alias problem was known. Reproduced as a two-stage cast; pinned by `background_value_is_narrowed_through_the_label_type`, `a_negative_background_value_cannot_reach_a_signed_feature_image`, `the_label_typed_background_value_then_wraps_into_a_narrower_output`. Verified against sources 2026-07-10 (labelmask-porter finding, spot-checked). Not yet filed. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S16 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `background_value` is `static_cast`-ed once, straight to the feature image's pixel type, as `itkLabelMapMaskImageFilter.h:123`'s `itkSetMacro(BackgroundValue, OutputImagePixelType)` intends; pinned by `background_value_casts_directly_to_the_output_type`, `a_negative_background_value_reaches_a_signed_feature_image`, `an_out_of_range_background_value_saturates_into_the_output_type`, `a_fractional_background_value_survives_into_a_float_output`. | `sitk-filters` `label_map_mask.rs` |
| 3.24 | `LabelMapMaskImageFilter` `testIdxIsInside` is dead code | `itkLabelMapMaskImageFilter.hxx:281/:346` guard writes with `m_Crop && (GetBackgroundValue() == m_Label) ^ m_Negated` — `^` binds tighter than `&&`, so this is `m_Crop && (B ^ N)`; `B ^ N` is true only in the two combinations where `GenerateOutputInformation` already fell back to the full image, so `outputRegion.IsInside(idx)` can never fail, and in the two genuinely-cropping combinations the guard is `false` while the painted set is exactly what the bounding box was computed from. The guard cannot change an output pixel. Not ported: the fill-then-repaint formulation makes an out-of-region write unrepresentable. | 3.26 | `NormalizedCorrelationImageFilter.yaml` `MaskImage` | Declared as a required member with no `optional: true` marker (unlike e.g. `ConnectedComponentImageFilter.yaml`'s own `MaskImage`), so SimpleITK's generated procedural wrapper cannot be called without a mask at all — even though `itk::NormalizedCorrelationImageFilter` genuinely supports a null mask (`if (!mask) { ... }`, `itkNormalizedCorrelationImageFilter.hxx:167-198`) and its own class doc calls masking optional. | 3.27 | `ImageFileReader`'s two extraction pipelines disagree, and the doc describes only one | `ExecuteInternal` (`sitkImageFileReader.cxx:362-390`) branches on `m_ExtractSize.size() == ImageType::ImageDimension`. **Same-length** (no zero-size axis): the file is read straight into an `itk::Image` of the *output* dimension, so `itk::ImageFileReader::GenerateOutputInformation` substitutes `GetDefaultDirection()` — the identity — for the file's direction, and `ExecuteExtract`'s loop runs only over the output dimension, so a trailing `m_ExtractIndex` entry (`[…, k]` for a 3-D file read as 2-D) is **silently ignored**. **With a zero-size axis**: the file is read at its own dimension and `ExtractImageFilter` collapses, yielding the direction **submatrix** and honouring every index entry. Same file, same requested slice, two different directions and two different pixel sets. The header's blanket statement "when the dimension of the image is reduced, the direction cosine matrix will be set to the identity" (`sitkImageFileReader.h:196-200`) is true only of the first branch. Reproduced. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S17 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — one pipeline now honours the documented contract for every spelling: the direction collapses to the **identity** on any dimension reduction (equivalent to ITK's `SetDirectionCollapseToIdentity`), and every `extract_index` entry applies, so `[10,20]` and `[10,20,0]` return the same image; the now-unreachable `SingularCollapsedDirection` error was removed. Pinned by `extract_with_a_zero_size_axis_gets_the_identity_direction_and_honours_every_index`, `extract_without_a_zero_axis_agrees_with_the_zero_axis_spelling`, `extract_of_a_singular_file_direction_gives_the_identity_not_an_error`. | pinned by `extract_collapses_a_zero_size_axis_and_keeps_the_direction_submatrix`, `extract_without_a_zero_axis_gets_the_identity_direction_and_ignores_the_trailing_index` |
| 3.28 | Two vestigial statements on the IO path | (a) `MetaImage::CanRead` computes `std::string elementDataFileName = M_GetTagValue(header, "ElementDataFile");` and never reads it (`metaImage.cxx:1226`) — the value is discarded and `true` returned, so a `.mha` whose first 8000 bytes contain `NDims` but no `ElementDataFile` is still claimed. (b) `ImageFileReader::ExecuteExtract`'s guard `else if (i >= ImageType::ImageDimension) region.SetSize(i, 0u);` (`sitkImageFileReader.cxx:417-421`) is a condition that is always true where it is reached, i.e. equivalent to a bare `else`: the `else` arm needs `i >= m_ExtractSize.size()`, and this arm only runs in the branch where `m_ExtractSize.size() != ImageType::ImageDimension` (`:362`), where `ImageType::ImageDimension` is the count of *non-zero* entries of `m_ExtractSize` (`:309-318`) and is therefore strictly less than `m_ExtractSize.size()`. | 3.29 | `HashImageFilter` default hash function disagrees between ITK and SimpleITK | `itk::HashImageFilter`'s own constructor defaults `m_HashFunction = MD5` (`itkHashImageFilter.hxx:34`), but the hand-written SimpleITK facing layer defaults to `HashFunction m_HashFunction{ SHA1 }` (`sitkHashImageFilter.h:75`) and `HashImageFilter::ExecuteInternal` always calls `hasher->SetHashFunction(this->GetHashFunction())` before `Update()` (`sitkHashImageFilter.cxx:120-127`) — so the ITK-level `MD5` default can never actually reach a caller through `itk::simple::Hash`/`HashImageFilter::Execute`; it is a dead default. A caller porting code from raw ITK (where an unconfigured `itk::HashImageFilter` hashes with MD5) to SimpleITK (where an unconfigured `Hash()` call hashes with SHA1) silently gets a different digest — same shape as §3.10/§3.11's disagreeing defaults. | 3.30 | `itk::simple::ReadTransform` (`sitkTransform.cxx:668-723`) discards every transform after the first | A transform file may hold an arbitrary list; unless the first entry is a `CompositeTransform` (which `TransformFileReader::Update` folds the rest into), `ReadTransform` returns `list->front()` and merely prints `"There is more than one transform in the file! | 3.31 | `GetPixelIDFromImageIO` has no `SYMMETRICSECONDRANKTENSOR` branch, so `NrrdImageIO`'s tensor pixel type is unreachable | `itkNrrdImageIO::ReadImageInformation` maps a `3D-symmetric-matrix` or `3D-masked-symmetric-matrix` pixel axis to `IOPixelEnum::SYMMETRICSECONDRANKTENSOR` (`itkNrrdImageIO.cxx:243-250`), a type `itk::Image` fully supports. | 3.32 | SimpleITK cannot load the tensor pixel types `NiftiImageIO` reads | `NiftiImageIO::ReadImageInformation` maps `NIFTI_INTENT_SYMMATRIX` to `IOPixelEnum::SYMMETRICSECONDRANKTENSOR` (and a 6-component one to `DIFFUSIONTENSOR3D`), reordering the components lower- to upper-triangular via `UpperToLowerOrder` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:464-470`, "as per ITK bug 0007485"). But `ImageReaderBase::GetPixelIDFromImageIO` (`sitkImageReaderBase.cxx:213-237`) matches only `SCALAR`/`COMPLEX`/`RGB`/`RGBA`/`VECTOR`/`COVARIANTVECTOR`/`FIXEDARRAY`/`POINT`/`OFFSET` and ends in `sitkExceptionMacro("Unknown PixelType")`. | 3.33 | An initial transform is skipped by *class name*, so this port has no `IdentityTransform` at all | Both `ExecuteInternal` and `EvaluateInternal` guard each of the moving- and fixed-initial transforms with `if (strIdentityTransform != this->m_MovingInitialTransform.GetITKBase()->GetNameOfClass())` (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:781,793,1059,1071`) — a *class-name* test, not a value test. An identity-valued `AffineTransform` is therefore still composed into `m_CompositeTransform`, while a default-constructed `sitk::Transform` (an `itk::IdentityTransform<double,3>`) is skipped. This crate has no `IdentityTransform` class (see `erased.rs` module docs), so the two initial transforms are `Option<Transform>` and `None` is the skipped case — same set of composed transforms, no name-keyed dispatch. | 3.34 | A not-in-place `Execute` returns a single-entry `CompositeTransform` | When `m_InitialTransformInPlace` is false, `ExecuteInternal` wraps the optimized output transform in a fresh `itk::CompositeTransform`, adds exactly one sub-transform to it, and returns that (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:970-989`). Upstream's own comment marks it as unwanted: *"TOOD: It should not be necessary to return a composite transform the sitk::Transform class is missing a constructor which accepts an arbitrary ITK transform."* So the return type of `Execute` depends on a flag that is nominally about *aliasing*, and a caller who flips `inPlace` to false gets a different transform class back. Reproduced and pinned by `not_in_place_execute_leaves_the_stored_transform_and_returns_a_composite`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S42 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — a not-in-place `execute_with_initial_transform` now returns the optimized transform as the same concrete kind the caller configured (it only leaves the *stored* transform untouched); the single-entry `CompositeTransform` wrapper — an upstream workaround for `sitk::Transform` lacking an arbitrary-ITK-transform constructor — is not reproduced, so the return type no longer depends on the flag (test renamed `..._returns_the_concrete_kind`). | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (`execute_with_initial_transform`) |
| 3.35 | `MetricEvaluate` silently ignores the sampling strategy, the percentage, the seed, and the multi-resolution schedule | `EvaluateInternal` (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:1028-1093`) builds a bare `itk::ImageToImageMetricv4` and calls `Initialize()` + `GetValue()`. It never constructs the `itk::ImageRegistrationMethodv4` — and `SetMetricSamplingStrategy`, `SetMetricSamplingPercentage`, `MetricSamplingReinitializeSeed`, `SetShrinkFactorsPerLevel` and `SetSmoothingSigmasPerLevel` are all set on *that* object (`:854-886`), never on the metric. So a method configured with `RANDOM` 1% sampling and a 4-level pyramid still evaluates densely, at full resolution, through `MetricEvaluate`. The optimizer and the scales estimator are likewise never built. Nothing in the API signals this. Reproduced and pinned by `metric_evaluate_ignores_the_sampling_strategy_and_the_pyramid`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S36 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `metric_evaluate` now honours the sampling strategy, percentage (the finest level's) and seed, so `set_metric_sampling_*` takes effect instead of being silently dropped; the multi-resolution pyramid is inapplicable to a single evaluation by definition (it is `Execute`'s optimization schedule, and one value cannot span several levels), so a configured schedule is documented-as-ignored rather than silently ignored, and is not an error — erroring would break the standard configure-once idiom, since almost every registration sets shrink factors. The optimizer and scales estimator remain unbuilt, as upstream. Pinned by `metric_evaluate_honours_the_sampling_and_ignores_the_pyramid`. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (`metric_evaluate`) |
| 3.36 | `SetInitialTransform(const Transform &)` silently re-enables the in-place flag, and its "in place" cannot reach the caller | The single-argument overload ends with `this->m_InitialTransformInPlace = true` (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:115-122`), so a caller who set `SetInitialTransform(t, false)` and later re-sets the transform through the one-argument form gets in-place optimization back with no diagnostic. The same overload also calls `m_InitialTransform.MakeUnique()` on its *own* copy, so despite the flag the optimizer cannot write through to the caller's object — only the two-argument overload's `transform.MakeUnique()` (`:148`) makes the caller's transform the one that is mutated. The flag therefore means two different things across the two overloads. Reproduced (flag semantics) and pinned by `the_single_argument_setter_restores_the_in_place_flag`; see §4.64 for the aliasing half. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S43 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the single-argument `set_initial_transform` no longer touches the in-place flag; it is set only by the explicit `set_initial_transform_in_place`/`_as_bspline` overloads (default `true`), so the flag has one meaning on every path and a plain re-set never silently re-enables in-place optimization (test renamed `the_single_argument_setter_preserves_the_in_place_flag`). | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (`set_initial_transform`) |
| 3.37 | SimpleITK cannot load the `TENSORS` pixel type `VTKImageIO` reads | `InternalReadImageInformation`'s `tensors` arm sets `IOPixelEnum::SYMMETRICSECONDRANKTENSOR` with six components (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:341-351`), but `ImageReaderBase::GetPixelIDFromImageIO` (`sitkImageReaderBase.cxx:213-240`) has no arm for it and ends in `sitkExceptionMacro("Unknown PixelType")` — the same wall §3.32 describes for NIfTI's `NIFTI_INTENT_SYMMATRIX`. So a tensor `.vtk` is readable through ITK and unreadable through SimpleITK. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S40 (2026-07-10), which covers the Nrrd/Nifti/VTK tensor readers together. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `Header::pixel_id` now maps `SYMMETRICSECONDRANKTENSOR` to a vector pixel id, so a `TENSORS` attribute loads as a 6-component vector image. A VTK `TENSORS` attribute stores the **full 9-component 3×3 matrix** per pixel on disk; `VTKImageIO` reads all nine and keeps the six symmetric components at row-major indices `[0,1,2,4,5,8]` — the diagonal and upper triangle `[a,b,c,d,e,f]` of a symmetric tensor. ASCII `ReadTensorBuffer` loops `fileComponents = num/6*9` with a hit-hit-hit / skip-hit-hit / skip-skip-hit pattern (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:415-451`); binary `ReadSymmetricTensorBufferAsBinary` reads row1=3 / seek1 / row2=2 / seek2 / row3=1 (`:494-525`). `vtk::read` reproduces this 9-read/6-keep contract for both paths. Pin renamed to `vtk_tensors_load_as_a_six_component_vector_image`. | `vtk.rs` |
| 3.38 | `FFTPadImageFilter.yaml` documents the wrong default `SizeGreatestPrimeFactor` | The yaml's `detaileddescriptionSet` (copied into every language binding) says "The default value is 5 for VNL, which is the greatest prime number for which the FFT are precomputed in FFTW". Neither half is current. The default comes from `custom_methods: DefaultSizeGreatestPrimeFactor()`, which calls `itk::FFTPadImageFilter<Image<float,2>>::New()->GetSizeGreatestPrimeFactor()`; that constructor seeds from `ForwardFFTImageFilter<…>::New()` (`itkFFTPadImageFilter.hxx:34-35`), which the object factory resolves to the always-registered `PocketFFTForwardFFTImageFilter` (`itkPocketFFTImageFilterInitFactory.cxx:48`), whose override returns **11** (`itkPocketFFTForwardFFTImageFilter.hxx:72-76`). `itkFFTPadImageFilter.h:84-86` is closer but also stale ("13 for FFTW, and 5 for VNL"). This port takes 11 and says so. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S21 (2026-07-10). | `fourier.rs` (`DEFAULT_SIZE_GREATEST_PRIME_FACTOR`) |
| 3.39 | `ActualXDimensionIsOdd` is computed by the forward filter and thrown away by the wrapper | `RealToHalfHermitianForwardFFTImageFilter::GenerateOutputInformation` ends with `this->SetActualXDimensionIsOdd(inputSize[0] % 2 != 0)` (`.hxx:70`), so ITK *knows* the parity that the `N/2+1`-wide output cannot express. `RealToHalfHermitianForwardFFTImageFilter.yaml` has `members: []` — no getter is wrapped — while `HalfHermitianToRealInverseFFTImageFilter.yaml` exposes `ActualXDimensionIsOdd` as a settable `bool` defaulting to `false`. A SimpleITK caller must therefore carry the parity by hand, and the default silently produces an even-width image: a 13-wide input round-trips to 12 wide with no error. This port has the same signature and the same trap; pinned by `fourier::tests::actual_x_dimension_is_odd_selects_between_two_output_widths`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S33 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `real_to_half_hermitian_forward_fft` now returns `(Image, bool)`, the `bool` being ITK's own `GetActualXDimensionIsOdd()`, so the parity the forward filter computes reaches the inverse and the round trip cannot silently narrow a 13-wide input to 12; pinned by `fourier::tests::the_forward_transform_returns_the_parity_that_restores_the_width`. | `fourier.rs` |
| 3.40 | `SetUseCompression` and `SetCompressionLevel` are both dead for NIfTI | `ImageFileWriter::ExecuteInternal` forwards both to `itk::ImageFileWriter` (`sitkImageFileWriter.cxx:230-231`), which forwards them to the `ImageIO`. `NiftiImageIO` consults neither: `nifti_image_write` opens through `znzopen(fname, "wb", nifti_is_gzfile(fname))` (`nifti1_io.c`), so compression is decided by the last three characters of the file name, and `gzopen` names no level, so a `.nii.gz` is always `Z_DEFAULT_COMPRESSION` (6). `WriteImage(image, "out.nii", useCompression=true)` therefore writes plain bytes and `WriteImage(image, "out.nii.gz", useCompression=false)` writes gzip. Compare `MetaImageIO` and `NrrdImageIO`, which both honour the level after `itkSetClampMacro(CompressionLevel, int, 1, 9)` and default to `2`, while SimpleITK's own default is `-1` — meaning "do not forward" (`itkImageFileWriter.hxx:199-201`), so the IO keeps its `2`. Pinned by `nifti_ignores_use_compression_entirely` and `compression_level_is_clamped_not_rejected`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S26 (2026-07-10). | `nifti.rs`, `compression.rs` |
| 3.41 | `SetMetricUseFixedImageGradientFilter` is inert for every metric except Demons, and `SetMetricUseMovingImageGradientFilter` is inert *only* for Demons | `SetupMetric` pushes both flags onto the metric unconditionally (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:1119-1120`), but `ImageToImageMetricv4::Initialize` gates each one on the gradient **source**: the fixed gradient image is built only `if (GetGradientSourceIncludesFixed() && m_UseFixedImageGradientFilter)` and the fixed *calculator* only `if (!m_UseFixedImageGradientFilter)` (`itkImageToImageMetricv4.hxx:138-172`) — and nothing else ever reads the fixed gradient when the source excludes it. `m_GradientSource` defaults to `GRADIENT_SOURCE_MOVING` (`itkObjectToObjectMetricBase.hxx:28`) and SimpleITK never calls `SetGradientSource`. The one exception is `DemonsImageToImageMetricv4`, whose constructor flips it to `GRADIENT_SOURCE_FIXED` (`itkDemonsImageToImageMetricv4.hxx:42`) — so for Demons the fixed flag is live and the *moving* flag is the dead one. Mean squares, Mattes, correlation, ANTS neighborhood correlation and joint-histogram MI all leave `SetMetricUseFixedImageGradientFilter` with no observable effect. Nothing in the SimpleITK API signals this. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S37 (2026-07-10). | `sitk-registration` (not exposed — see §4.76) |
| 3.42 | `SetUseCompression` and `SetCompressionLevel` are both dead for GIPL too | Same shape as §3.40, a different class: `GiplImageIO::Write` opens through `gzopen(m_FileName.c_str(), "wb")` (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:671`) — no level argument — whenever `CheckExtension` set `m_IsCompressed` from the `.gipl.gz` suffix (`:1085-1090`); `m_UseCompression`/`m_CompressionLevel` are never read. A `.gipl.gz` therefore always compresses at zlib's `Z_DEFAULT_COMPRESSION` (6) regardless of `WriteOptions`, and a `.gipl` never compresses no matter what `use_compression` says. Pinned by `gipl_gz_write_ignores_use_compression_and_compression_level`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S27 (2026-07-10). | `gipl.rs` |
| 3.43 | `HDF5TransformIO`'s deflate path is unreachable from SimpleITK | `HDF5TransformIOTemplate::WriteParameters` deflate-5s the `TransformParameters` dataset in chunks of `min(dim, 1 MiB)` when `GetUseCompression()` is set (`itkHDF5TransformIO.cxx:112-146`) — and `TransformFixedParameters` never, whatever the flag. `itk::TransformFileWriterTemplate` does have the setter (`itkTransformFileWriter.h:91-93`, defaulting to `false`), but `itk::simple::WriteTransform` (`sitkTransform.cxx:733-740`) is four lines — `New()`, `SetFileName`, `SetInput`, `Update()` — and never calls it, nor does `Transform::WriteTransform`; SimpleITK wraps `SetUseCompression` on `ImageFileWriter` alone. So no SimpleITK caller can produce a compressed transform file, and this port writes contiguous datasets only (§5.22). Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S32 (2026-07-10). | `transform_hdf5.rs` |
| 3.44 | `sitkProcessObject.h`'s no-exception-on-abort promise is false on the multi-threaded path | The `Abort()` documentation states "The expected behavior is that not exception should be throw out of this processes Execute method" (`sitkProcessObject.h:313-318`). But `ProgressReporter::CheckAbortGenerateData` throws `ProcessAborted` whenever the abort flag is set (`itkProgressReporter.h:78-90`), `ProcessObject::UpdateOutputData` catches it, fires `AbortEvent`, resets the pipeline, and **rethrows** (`itkProcessObject.cxx:1686-1692`), and SimpleITK catches `ProcessAborted` nowhere (`rg ProcessAborted Code/` over the SimpleITK tree: zero hits outside that comment) — so a filter whose `GenerateData` reports progress escapes `Execute` with a `ProcessAborted` exception, exactly what the documentation promises cannot happen. Found by the observer design work; see `doc/observer-design.md` §1.5, which recommends not porting `Abort()` at all (it is also a no-op for the registration process object — nothing reads `GetAbortGenerateData` in `RegistrationMethodsv4`/`Optimizersv4`). Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S22 (2026-07-10). | not ported — no `Abort()` surface exists in this port, and §5.23's design keeps it that way |
| 3.45 | A 2-channel (gray + alpha) PNG is readable/writable by raw `PNGImageIO` but unrepresentable through SimpleITK | `ReadImageInformation` sets `m_PixelType = SCALAR` unconditionally (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:444/449), then `SetNumberOfComponents(png_get_channels(...))` (`:452`), and only afterward upgrades to `RGB`/`RGBA` for 3/4 components (`:454-461`) — 1 and 2 components stay `SCALAR`. `ImageReaderBase::GetPixelIDFromImageIO` accepts `SCALAR` only when `numberOfComponents == 1` and otherwise requires `RGB`/`RGBA`/`VECTOR`/… (sitkImageReaderBase.cxx:215-228), so `SCALAR` with `numberOfComponents == 2` matches neither arm and falls into `"Unknown PixelType: ..."` (`:236-237`). This port raises the same condition as `IoError::UnsupportedPngFeature` at header-parse time. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S44 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the unrepresentability is SimpleITK's pixel-ID wrapping, not a PNG-format limit, and this port's `PixelId::VectorUInt8`/`VectorUInt16` has no such restriction, so [`header_from_reader`] now treats 2 channels like 3 and 4: a 2-component vector image; pinned by `png_roundtrip_gray_alpha_vector_uint8` and `png_roundtrip_gray_alpha_vector_uint16`. | `png.rs` |
| 3.46 | `SetUseCompression`/`SetCompressionLevel` are dead for PNG unless compression is "on" — every PNG is deflated regardless | Third instance of this shape after NIfTI (§3.40) and GIPL (§3.42), distinct from both: `Write` only calls `png_set_compression_level` **inside `if (m_UseCompression)`** (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:661-665) — a PNG's pixel data is always deflated (PNG has no uncompressed pixel encoding), so turning compression "off" does not skip deflating, it only skips *choosing a level*, leaving zlib at its own built-in default (`Z_DEFAULT_COMPRESSION`, 6) rather than at `PNGImageIO`'s own constructed default of 4 (`:271-272`). `write` reproduces this: `options.use_compression` gates whether `Encoder::set_deflate_compression` is called at all; left alone, the `png` crate's own default is `DeflateCompression::Level(6)` (`flate2::Compression::default()`), matching zlib's default byte for byte — pinned by `use_compression_off_matches_the_crates_own_default_level_not_pngs_own`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S29 (2026-07-10). | `png.rs` |
| 3.47 | SimpleITK can write an HDF5 vector or complex image and can never read one back | `HDF5ImageIO::ReadImageInformation` calls `SetNumberOfComponents(Dims[nDims - 1])` when the `VoxelData` rank exceeds the image dimension (`:758-766`) but never calls `SetPixelType`, so `m_PixelType` keeps its `IOPixelEnum::SCALAR` default (`itkImageIOBase.h:801`). `ImageReaderBase::GetPixelIDFromImageIO` takes its scalar branch only for `numberOfComponents == 1`, matches `SCALAR` against none of `RGB`/`RGBA`/`VECTOR`/`COVARIANTVECTOR`/`FIXEDARRAY`/`POINT`/`OFFSET`, fails the `COMPLEX` test too, and throws `"Unknown PixelType: <component>(<n>)"` (`sitkImageReaderBase.cxx:215-238`). The writer has no such gate: `ImageFileWriter` on a `VectorImage` or a `complex` image produces a perfectly good file with a trailing component axis. Every other `ImageIO` SimpleITK ships sets a pixel type. **Reproduced** — `write` accepts any pixel type; `read` and `read_information` raise `IoError::UnknownPixelType`. §5.25. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S18 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the read side supplies the `SetPixelType(VECTOR)` upstream omits: `pixel_id_from_image_io` maps `numberOfComponents > 1` through `PixelId::vector_id`, so `read`/`read_information` reconstruct the vector image the trailing component axis records — a vector image round-trips byte-for-byte, and a complex image reads back as a two-component float vector (the file carries no complex marker). Pinned by `a_vector_image_round_trips_through_the_component_axis` and `a_complex_image_reads_back_as_a_two_component_float_vector`. | `image_hdf5.rs` |
| 3.48 | `SetUseCompression` is dead for HDF5 images, but `SetCompressionLevel` is live | `WriteImageInformation` calls `plist.setDeflate(this->GetCompressionLevel())` with no `GetUseCompression()` guard, under its own comment "we have implicit compression enabled here?" (`:1186-1195`). `HDF5ImageIO`'s constructor sets `SetMaximumCompressionLevel(9)` then `SetCompressionLevel(5)`, and `itkSetClampMacro(CompressionLevel, int, 1, GetMaximumCompressionLevel())` (`itkImageIOBase.h:288`) clamps the low end to `1`, so the deflate filter can never be switched off — not by `SetUseCompression(false)`, not by `SetCompressionLevel(0)`. This is the mirror image of §3.40 (NIfTI) and §3.42 (GIPL), where both setters are dead; here the level alone survives. **Reproduced** — `write` ignores `WriteOptions::use_compression` and passes `resolved_level(5)` to `deflate`. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S28 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — `use_compression` now gates the deflate filter: `write` deflates only when the flag is set, and `compression_level` is meaningful only then; chunking at `[1, ...]` stays unconditional (matching ITK's own `plist.setChunk`), so an uncompressed write is a chunked dataset with no filter, not a contiguous one. Pinned by `use_compression_gates_the_deflate_filter` (off vs on boundary) and `every_compression_level_round_trips` (levels under compression on). | `image_hdf5.rs` |
| 3.49 | `JPEGImageIO::SetQuality`/`GetQuality` is a thin alias over `CompressionLevel`, clamped `1..=100`, default 95 | `SetQuality`/`GetQuality` (`itkJPEGImageIO.h:56-67`) call straight through to `SetCompressionLevel`/`GetCompressionLevel` — there is no separate `m_Quality` field. `itkSetClampMacro(CompressionLevel, int, 1, GetMaximumCompressionLevel())` (`itkImageIOBase.h:288`) clamps it, and unlike every other format ported so far, `JPEGImageIO`'s constructor never calls `SetMaximumCompressionLevel` — so the ceiling stays at `ImageIOBase`'s own default of **100** (`itkImageIOBase.h:830`), not the `9` that bounds MetaImage/NRRD/PNG. The constructor sets the default quality to 95 (`itkJPEGImageIO.cxx:300`). **Reproduced** — `resolved_quality` is a JPEG-specific `1..=100` clamp; this crate cannot reuse `WriteOptions::resolved_level` (hardcoded `1..=9`). Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S30 (2026-07-10). **Verified** (2026-07-11) — no change needed. The ITK-side `SetQuality`/`SetCompressionLevel` alias is a *single* field, and this port already exposes a single knob, `WriteOptions::compression_level`, that `resolved_quality` interprets as the JPEG quality (negative → the constructor default 95; otherwise clamped `1..=100`). There is no second `Quality` option and thus no dual-meaning ambiguity to close — the alias collapses cleanly to one field with one meaning. Pinned by `resolved_quality_defaults_to_95_when_unset`, `resolved_quality_clamps_to_one_through_one_hundred`, and `resolved_quality_ignores_use_compression`. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 3.50 | `Progressive` and `CMYKtoRGB` are always on, and SimpleITK exposes no way to change either | Both are in-class initializers on `JPEGImageIO` itself — `m_Progressive{ true }`, `m_CMYKtoRGB{ true }` (`itkJPEGImageIO.h:125,127`) — and the constructor never touches them, unlike `m_UseCompression` a few lines above (§2.138). SimpleITK's `ImageFileWriter`/`ImageFileReader` expose only the generic `SetUseCompression`/`SetCompressionLevel`/`SetCompressor`; neither `SetProgressive` nor `SetCMYKtoRGB` is wrapped anywhere in `Code/IO/include/sitkImageFileWriter.h` or `sitkImageSeriesWriter.h`. Through SimpleITK's own public surface a JPEG is therefore always written progressive and a CMYK source is always converted to RGB on read. **Reproduced** — [`write`] calls `encoder.set_progressive(true)` unconditionally; [`read`] always applies [`cmyk_to_rgb`] to a 4-component source. Filed as SimpleITK #2625 comment item S31 (2026-07-10). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — the capability upstream hides is exposed on the `jpeg` module's own surface, with the defaults byte-identical to before. Write: `JpegWriteOptions { progressive, chroma_subsampling }` (default `true` / 4:2:0) via `jpeg::write_with_jpeg_options`; the `ImageIo::write` path keeps the defaults. Read: `jpeg::read_preserving_cmyk` keeps a CMYK source's raw four uninverted channels as a 4-component `VectorUInt8` — `jpeg_decoder` hands back `PixelFormat::CMYK32` itself, so the always-on `CMYKtoRGB` was never a decoder limit, only the absence of a read option. These live on the module surface because the shared `WriteOptions` carries no format-specific fields and `read` takes no options; a future shared `ReadOptions`/`WriteOptions` unification could lift them into the generic surface. Pinned by `jpeg_write_defaults_match_upstream_progressive_and_4_2_0`, `jpeg_progressive_false_produces_a_baseline_jpeg`, `jpeg_chroma_subsampling_selects_the_sampling_factor`, and `read_preserving_cmyk_keeps_the_raw_four_uninverted_channels`. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 3.51 | ~~`TIFFImageIO::InternalSetCompressor` reaches only `PackBits`, and SimpleITK cannot say otherwise~~ | **Refuted at the 2026-07-10 re-verification — the premise is false, and this row was never filed.** `ImageFileWriter` *does* expose a compressor string: `SetCompressor(const std::string &)` is declared at `sitkImageFileWriter.h:123` (member `m_Compressor` at `:192`), and `ExecuteInternal` forwards it — `if (!this->m_Compressor.empty()) { imageio->SetCompressor(this->m_Compressor); }` (`sitkImageFileWriter.cxx:237-240`) — onto the same ImageIO the writer uses. `ImageIOBase::SetCompressor` uppercases and dispatches to `InternalSetCompressor` (`itkImageIOBase.cxx:327-337`), and TIFF's resolves `PACKBITS`, `NOCOMPRESSION`, `JPEG`, `DEFLATE`, `ADOBEDEFLATE` and `LZW` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:260-290`). Only the *default* (empty) compressor resolves to PackBits. This port's `COMPRESSION_NONE` ↔ `COMPRESSION_PACKBITS`-only mapping is therefore a limitation of **this port**, not of SimpleITK. Pinned by `tiff_packbits_compression_round_trips_through_multi_row_strips`. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — a limitation with a pure-Rust path available is implemented, not left refused: `WriteOptions::compressor` (`TiffCompressor::Lzw`/`Deflate`/`PackBits`) plus `ImageFileWriter::set_compressor` now reach every compressor the `tiff` crate's encoder can write (`JPEG` and upstream's legacy tag-`32946` `Deflate` stay unreachable — no encoder for either exists in pure Rust), gated by `use_compression` exactly as `itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:692-716` gates `m_Compression` on `m_UseCompression`; pinned by `tiff_lzw_compression_round_trips_and_shrinks_compressible_data`, `tiff_deflate_compression_round_trips_and_shrinks_compressible_data`, `tiff_explicit_packbits_compressor_matches_the_bare_use_compression_default` and `tiff_use_compression_off_ignores_an_explicit_compressor`. | `tiff.rs` |
| 3.52 | `SetCompressionLevel` on a TIFF is TIFF's *JPEG quality* — mis-mapped, but **not** dead | **Corrected at the 2026-07-10 re-verification; the "therefore dead" conclusion is refuted and this row was never filed.** The alias half holds: `TIFFImageIO`'s constructor calls `SetJPEGQuality(75)` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:213`), `SetJPEGQuality` is a straight alias for `SetCompressionLevel` (`itkTIFFImageIO.h:171-179`), the value is consumed only by `TIFFSetField(TIFFTAG_JPEGQUALITY, this->GetJPEGQuality())` in the `JPEG` compressor arm (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:749`), and `GetMaximumCompressionLevel()` stays at `ImageIOBase`'s `100` rather than the `9` the deflate-based IOs report (`itkImageIOBase.h:830`), so a level of `100` is not clamped on its way in. But the deadness conclusion depended on §3.51's false premise: `SetCompressor("JPEG")` + `UseCompressionOn()` selects `COMPRESSION_JPEG` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:705`), and a forwarded `SetCompressionLevel(n)` then drives `TIFFTAG_JPEGQUALITY`. The level is live and reachable from SimpleITK. Pinned by `tiff_compression_level_does_not_change_the_written_bytes` — which pins **this port's** behaviour, where no compressor selector is exposed. **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — now that §3.51 exposes `TiffCompressor::Deflate`, leaving `compression_level` permanently dead here (there being no pure-Rust JPEG encoder to reach `TIFFTAG_JPEGQUALITY` with) would waste the one compressor this port can actually vary; `deflate_level_for` maps the resolved `1..=9` level onto the `tiff` crate's three `DeflateLevel` tiers (`Fast`/`Balanced`/`Best`) — a new use of the knob, not a port of one upstream ever had, since TIFF's `CompressionLevel` was always JPEG-quality-only in `itkTIFFImageIO`. `tiff_compression_level_does_not_change_the_written_bytes` still holds exactly as before for the *default* (`PackBits`) compressor; pinned for `Deflate` by `tiff_deflate_compression_level_selects_one_of_three_ratio_tiers` and `deflate_level_for_partitions_one_through_nine_into_three_tiers`. | `tiff.rs` |
| 3.53 | `SetInitialTransformAsBSpline` ignores `SetVirtualDomain`, and with `inPlace` it rewrites the caller's mesh size | `SetVirtualDomain`/`SetVirtualDomainFromImage` reach only the metric (`SetupMetric` calls `metric->SetVirtualDomain(...)`, `sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:1121-1135`); the B-spline adaptor is built from `method->GetFixedImage()` unconditionally (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod_CreateParametersAdaptor.hxx:152`, `:57`, `:74`). So a registration whose samples live on a caller-supplied virtual grid still derives every level's B-spline transform domain from the fixed image's grid. Separately, `inPlace = true` (the default of both `SetInitialTransform` and `SetInitialTransformAsBSpline`) grafts the caller's transform as `m_OutputTransform` (`itkImageRegistrationMethodv4.hxx:733-751`), and the level-0 adaptor then calls `SetCoefficientImages` on it (`itkBSplineTransformParametersAdaptor.hxx:271`) — so after `Execute` the transform the caller handed in no longer has the mesh size the caller set, but the *last* level's. Both reproduced; the mesh rewrite is pinned by `bspline_scale_factors_multiply_the_initial_mesh_size_not_the_previous_levels` (the stored initial transform's `grid_size` is the adapted one). **Fixed in this port** (2026-07-11) — (1) the B-spline adaptor domain is now derived from the grid the metric samples in: the `set_virtual_domain` grid when one is set, otherwise the fixed image, so a virtual domain is honored rather than silently ignored (new test `the_bspline_adaptor_domain_follows_the_virtual_domain_when_one_is_set`). (2) The in-place mesh rewrite is made explicit in the API contract: there is no caller-object aliasing in this port (transforms are values passed by move), so the stored initial transform carrying the *finest* mesh after an in-place run is the intended optimized result, and `set_initial_transform_as_bspline`'s docs now state this and point to `in_place = false` for callers who want the original stored mesh preserved. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` (`set_initial_transform_as_bspline`, `execute_with_initial_transform`) |
| 3.54 | DICOM registry entry — the reader class is named `GDCMImageIO`, not `DICOMImageIO` (`dicom.rs` `DicomImageIo`, `lib.rs`) | SimpleITK reads DICOM through `itk::GDCMImageIO`; there is no separate "DICOMImageIO". The factory's `GetNameOfClass()` returns `"GDCMImageIO"` (`itkGDCMImageIO.h:138`), so `ImageIOBase::GetNameOfClass` and hence `GetRegisteredImageIOs()`/`ImageFileReader::GetImageIOFromFileName` all key off `"GDCMImageIO"`. This port therefore registers its DICOM `ImageIo` with `name() == "GDCMImageIO"` — matching upstream — rather than the `"DICOMImageIO"` a caller might infer from the `.dcm` extension. | Reproduced; the name is asserted by `image_io_by_name("GDCMImageIO")`, the two `registered_image_ios()` expectation lists, and `io_reports_gdcm_class_name_and_extensions`. | `dicom.rs` (`DicomImageIo`), `lib.rs` |
| 3.55 | `ImageSeriesWriter::ExecuteInternal`'s DICOM-extension guard checks the whole path string, and a dot-less name wraps around to reject itself | `std::string ext = fn.substr(fn.find_last_of(".") + 1);` (`sitkImageSeriesWriter.cxx:228`) runs on the full file-name string, not just its final component, so a `.` in a parent directory can feed the "extension." And when there is no `.` anywhere in the path, `std::string::find_last_of` returns `npos`, and `npos + 1` wraps (unsigned overflow) to `0` — `fn.substr(0)` is the entire path — so a file literally named `dcm` or `dicom`, with no extension and no separators, still matches `ext == "dcm" \|\| ext == "dicom"` (`:231`) and is rejected as if it were DICOM. | `image_series_writer.rs` (`is_dicom_extension`); pinned by `a_bare_dotless_filename_named_dcm_is_rejected_via_the_wraparound_quirk` and `dot_extension_dicom_is_rejected_case_insensitively` |
| 3.56 | `ImageSeriesWriter`'s `MemberFunctionFactory` registers only dimension 3 — the wrapper is narrower than the ITK template it wraps | `GetMemberFunctionFactory` calls `factory.RegisterMemberFunctions<PixelIDTypeList, 3>()` and leaves the 2-D registration commented out in the source itself (`// factory.RegisterMemberFunctions< PixelIDTypeList, 2 > ();`, `sitkImageSeriesWriter.cxx:49-51`) — unlike `ImageSeriesReader`, which registers `2..SITK_MAX_DIMENSION` (`sitkImageSeriesReader.cxx:42`). `itk::ImageSeriesWriter<TInputImage, TOutputImage>` itself is templated over any `TInputImage` dimension (with `TOutputImage` rebound to one dimension lower, `itkImageSeriesWriter.hxx`'s own template parameter), so the 3-D-only restriction is purely a SimpleITK dispatch-table gap, not a limitation of the underlying ITK class. Any other dimension — 2-D included — reaches `MemberFunctionFactory::GetMemberFunction`'s generic "Pixel type: ... is not supported in ...D by ..." exception (`sitkMemberFunctionFactory.hxx:134-135`) before `ExecuteInternal` ever runs. | `image_series_writer.rs` (`ImageSeriesWriter::execute`, `IoError::SeriesWriterUnsupportedDimension`); pinned by `non_3d_image_is_rejected_with_the_dispatch_message` |

## 4. Deliberate divergences of this port (no upstream defect implied)

| # | Site | Divergence and reason | doc |
|---|---|---|---|
| 4.1 | crate-wide | Internal computation in `f64` where ITK pins `float`/`RealType = float` (distance maps, N4, min-max flow, FFT correlation, SLIC noted exception). Precision superset; documented per module. | per-module docs |
| 4.2 | ~~`fft.rs` backend~~ **closed 2026-07-10** | Was: radix-2 power-of-two padding instead of ITK's factorable padding. Now aligned exactly, and the row records the measurement the old row asserted without evidence. `convolution.rs`/`deconvolution.rs` pad with `itkFFTPadImageFilter`'s search at `SizeGreatestPrimeFactor == 11` (§2.110, §3.38); `fft_correlation.rs` uses `FindClosestValidDimension`'s 2/3/5 search, which is what *that* filter actually calls (§2.110). No pinned output moved: under either rule `fft_convolution` agrees with `convolution`'s spatial ground truth to ≤ 2.7e-15 (measured 2026-07-10 over `[7]`, `[13]`, `[9,11]`, `[12,5]` with 3- and 4-tap kernels; 1.8e-15 under the old power-of-two rule, 2.7e-15 under GPF ≤ 11), and the whole `sitk-filters` suite passes under either. The transform is now mixed-radix (2/3/5/7/11) plus Bluestein, matching PocketFFT's supported lengths. | `fft.rs`, `fourier.rs`, `convolution.rs`, `fft_correlation.rs` |
| 4.3 | `noise.rs` random filters | Single-region reseeding: bit-for-bit equal to ITK single-threaded output, **not** to ITK's default multi-threaded stream. | `noise.rs` |
| 4.4 | `math.rs` binary ops | Intermediates in `f64` with saturating narrowing (NaN → 0 for integers) instead of C++ wrapping overflow ("no numeric overflow checking is performed" upstream). Non-uniform vs raw C++ by design. | `math.rs` |
| 4.5 | `label_shape.rs` | Determinant via LU instead of eigenvalue product (exact-arithmetic identical); `Indexes`/`RLEIndexes` attributes not ported. | `label_shape.rs` |
| 4.6 | `curvature_flow` / `min_max_curvature_flow` | Crate-added `time_step` stability rejection (`FilterError::UnstableTimeStep`) that ITK does not perform (ITK warns or says nothing). **Candidate for removal if strict parity is preferred — open question, see §5.2.** | `min_max_curvature_flow.rs`, `denoise.rs` |
| 4.7 | `overlap.rs` | Requires both images integer-typed instead of silently casting `TargetImage` to the source label type. | `overlap.rs` |
| 4.8 | `morphology_reconstruction.rs` | `Seed` bounds-checked (`FilterError::InvalidSeedIndex`) where ITK does an unchecked `GetPixel` — an out-of-range multi-index could alias a valid flat offset over this crate's linear buffer. | `morphology_reconstruction.rs` |
| 4.9 | `sources.rs`, geometry-taking filters | Exact-length per-axis vectors (vs §3.3 truncation). | `sources.rs` |
| 4.10 | `windowed_sinc` interpolator gradient | Analytic gradient `w'(x)·sinc(x) + w(x)·sinc'(x)` derived for this crate (ITK has no original — SimpleITK never exposes interpolator gradients); FD-validated. | sitk-registration `metric.rs` / interpolator docs |
| 4.11 | `kmeans.rs` | Brute-force Lloyd replaces `KdTreeBasedKmeansEstimator` with a written identical-result argument (§2.13). | `kmeans.rs` |
| 4.12 | `fast_marching_upwind_gradient.rs` gradient output | ITK's `m_GradientImage` is `Image<CovariantVector>`; pending the vector pixel model this port returns the **scalar decomposition** — `Vec<Image>` of length `dim`, `gradient[j]` holding `gradientPixel[j]`. Empty unless `generate_gradient_image` is set (matching ITK's never-allocated default, §3.7). | `fast_marching_upwind_gradient.rs` |
| 4.13 | `coherence_enhancing_diffusion.rs` numerics | Computation in `f64` — **matching** ITK, which runs `double` for every input type including `Float32` (the yaml's `filter_type` uses the `TScalar` default = `NumericTraits<PixelType>::RealType` = `double`; the earlier "ITK runs float" note here was the §2.39 RealType misbelief, corrected 2026-07-10). The remaining divergence is the symmetric eigensolver (cyclic Jacobi vs ITK's `SymmetricEigenAnalysis`) — bit-exactness out of reach by design. `noise_scale == 0`/`feature_scale == 0` are the identity here where ITK divides by zero in `RecursiveGaussianImageFilter::SetUp`. Selling bailout is silent (no stderr, §2.25). | `coherence_enhancing_diffusion.rs` |
| 4.14 | `transform_geometry.rs` error paths | Singular transform → `TransformError::NonInvertibleTransform`; non-linear transform → typed error. ITK crashes on a null `GetInverseTransform()` deref / warns-then-crashes respectively (§1.25). | `transform_geometry.rs` |
| 4.15 | `sitk-core` `PixelId` discriminants — **closed 2026-07-10** | Was: `VectorUInt8..VectorFloat64` at `10..=19` where SimpleITK numbers them `12..=21`. Complex pixels landed, so `ComplexFloat32`/`ComplexFloat64` now occupy `10`/`11` and the vectors moved to `12..=21` — SimpleITK-exact (`sitkPixelIDValues.h:103-131`), pinned by `pixel_id_discriminants_match_simpleitk`. `22..=25` (`sitkLabelUInt8..UInt64`) stay unassigned; an `itk::LabelMap` has no pixel container (`itkLabelMap.h:69`) and is not an `Image` here. Remaining (unrelated) divergences once filed under this row: `vector_index_selection_cast` bounds-checks the component index directly (ITK's check is `sizeof`-derived), and `compose` checks size by dimension only — both documented at the function. | `sitk-core` `pixel.rs`, `sitk-filters` `vector.rs` |
| 4.16 | `patch_based_denoising.rs` threading model | Single work unit: the sampler seed is the work-unit id (`SetSeed(threadId)`, `.hxx:1319`), so output is bit-reproducible and equals ITK's single-work-unit output, not ITK's default multi-threaded stream — same divergence class as §4.3. | `patch_based_denoising.rs` |
| 4.17 | `warp.rs` | (a) Size added to the same-information test — identical on the path ITK intends (sizes equal by construction there); on the geometry-equal/size-unequal configuration this port takes the general path and produces output **where ITK throws/aborts in its iterator containment assert** (§1.31) — a documented behavioral divergence, not a memory-safety fix; (b) integer-component displacement fields accepted (SimpleITK instantiates float vectors only, §3.12) — field read through `components_to_f64_vec`, identical arithmetic; (c) continuous index clamped in the float domain before conversion (§1.33 — a defensive implementation choice; the operand is geometry-derived and finite on every input upstream defines). Displacement-field family computes in `f64` per §4.1. | `warp.rs` |
| 4.18 | `vector_connected_component.rs` labels | Contiguous `1..=N` by first-appearance order, where ITK's own docstring says labels are "in no particular order" and may have gaps — matches the sibling `scalar_connected_component.rs` convention. | `vector_connected_component.rs` |
| 4.19 | `displacement_field/inverse.rs` TPS solve | Symmetric eigendecomposition where ITK takes an SVD in `ComputeWMatrix` — `L` is symmetric by construction, so the pseudo-inverses agree exactly (`σᵢ = \|λᵢ\|`, `uᵢ = sign(λᵢ)vᵢ`); ITK's absolute `1e-8` singular-value floor matched (`itkKernelTransform.hxx:148-153`). | `displacement_field/inverse.rs` |
| 4.20 | `demons/compose.rs` field exponential | `2^numiter` computed in `f64` instead of `1 << numiter` on a signed `int` — closes the §1.36 shift UB; identical for every `numiter ≤ 30`, defined for all. | `demons/compose.rs` |
| 4.21 | `recursive_gaussian` helper (pre-existing, noted by `level_set_motion.rs`) | Computes in `f64` where ITK's `SmoothingRecursiveGaussianImageFilter` uses `float` internally for integer pixel types; filters axes `0..dim-1` in order while ITK filters the last axis first (separable passes commute — equal up to floating-point association, not bit-identical for integer inputs); `sigma == 0` leaves the axis untouched where ITK's recursion would divide by zero into NaN coefficients. Pinned: `a_zero_sigma_takes_the_gradient_of_the_unsmoothed_image`. | `demons/level_set_motion.rs` |
