| 4.22 | `fast_marching_base.rs` heap ties and stopping value | (a) Upstream's `std::priority_queue` compares node **values only** (`itkFastMarchingBase.h:259-262`, `itkNodePair.h:96-100`); tie order comes from `std::push_heap`/`pop_heap`'s sift pattern, unspecified by the standard and different between libstdc++/libc++ — no portable bit-for-bit target exists, so this port breaks ties by ascending flat index (tie order provably cannot reach the output without a topology constraint; under `Strict`/`NoHandles` it can decide which of two equal-valued nodes is seen as a junction — module doc). (b) `criterion->SetThreshold(m_StoppingValue)` narrows `double → float`, C++-undefined outside `float`'s range; here `as f32` yields an infinity. | `fast_marching_base.rs` |
| 4.23 | `Image::get_vector` / `set_vector` on a complex image | Return/accept the pixel's `[re, im]` (length = `buffer_stride()`), where SimpleITK's `GetPixelAsVectorFloat32` **throws** for a complex image — its `InternalGetPixelAsVector` is gated on `IsVector<ImageType>::Value` (`sitkPimpleImageBase.hxx`). One uniform "these are the pixel's components" rule is preferred here over a fourth runtime guard; the SimpleITK-shaped typed accessors are `get_complex`/`set_complex`. Note the *derived* `number_of_components_per_pixel()` still reports `1` for a complex image, exactly as upstream (`sitkPimpleImageBase.hxx:202-209`). | `sitk-core` `image.rs` |
| 4.24 | `complex.rs` numerics | Computes in the **component** type (`f32` for `ComplexFloat32`), matching ITK's functor templates exactly — a deliberate exception to §4.1's crate-wide `f64` promotion, because `ComplexToModulus`'s `f32` overflow/underflow (§2.58) is only observable that way. | `complex.rs` |
| 4.25 | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` — `LabelMap` is a separate type | `itk::LabelMap` derives from `ImageBase`, not `Image` (`itkLabelMap.h:69`): geometry, no `PixelContainer`. SimpleITK forces it into its single `sitk::Image` and pays with a runtime throw in every buffer accessor (`sitkPimpleImageBase.hxx:829-832`, `if constexpr (IsLabel<ImageType>::Value) sitkExceptionMacro(...)`). This port makes it a distinct `sitk_core::LabelMap`, so a label map can never reach a filter that wants pixel data — no `Option<PixelBuffer>` under every `match PixelId`, no throw. Faithful to ITK's object model, divergent from SimpleITK's class layout. Corollary: `PixelId` gains no `Label*` variants (SimpleITK's `22..=25`, `sitkPixelIDValues.h:130-133`); the label type is a stored `PixelId` on the map. | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` |
| 4.26 | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` — `LabelObject` is always optimized | ITK's `Optimize()` (`itkLabelObject.h:196-200`, `.hxx:303-361`) is opt-in, so `Size()` (`itkLabelObject.h:153-161`) warns it is only accurate afterwards and `AddLine` is documented as adding "without any check" (`itkLabelObject.hxx:182-190`, `itkLabelMap.h:216-222`). Here the optimized state — lines sorted by `LabelObjectLineComparator`, length ≥ 1, no two lines on a row touching or overlapping — is an **invariant** restored by `LabelObject::add_line`, its single owner. There is no public `optimize()`; `size()` is always exact and returns `u64` (ITK accumulates into an `int`, `itkLabelObject.hxx:217`). A deliberate strengthening: ITK's opt-in design exists because `LabelObject` is a `LightObject` shared by raw pointer, which `&mut` removes. Double coverage *across* objects stays representable — `LabelUniqueLabelMapFilter` exists to remove it, and `LabelMap::GetPixel` (`itkLabelMap.hxx:155-170`) is specified in terms of it. | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` |
| 4.27 | `sitk-filters` `label_map.rs` — `merge_label_map` KEEP drains its deferred list once per input | Closes §1.40. Upstream's never-cleared deque leaves two `std::map` keys aliasing one `LabelObject`, which the user-approved `objects[k].label() == k` invariant of this port's `LabelMap` makes unrepresentable by construction. This port drains the deque after each input, which is what the surrounding code plainly intends: a deferred object receives exactly one new label. Observable difference only with three or more inputs *and* a deferred object from input 1 — upstream yields the object at `L2` with a stale alias at `L1` and an object count one too high, this port yields it at `L1`. Pinned by `merge_keep_gives_a_deferred_object_one_label_across_three_inputs`. | `sitk-filters` `label_map.rs` |
| 4.28 | `sitk-filters` `label_map_overlay.rs` — overlapping label objects paint in ascending label order | `ThreadedProcessLabelObject` is dispatched from a multithreaded region (`itkLabelMapFilter.hxx:83-113`), so when two objects of one label map share a pixel — representable, and what `LabelUniqueLabelMapFilter` exists to remove — ITK's painted colour is whichever work unit wrote last, which is unspecified. `label_map_to_rgb` and `label_map_overlay` paint in ascending label order, so the greatest label wins deterministically. `label_map_contour_overlay` is unaffected: its temporary map has already been through `label_unique_label_map`. Pinned by `a_higher_label_wins_an_overlap_in_label_map_to_rgb`. Scope note (2026-07-10): the caveat bites only the *colouring* filters, where the painted value depends on the label — in `label_map_mask` and `label_map_to_binary` every overlap candidate paints the same value, so the ascending-label walk is bit-identical to any ITK thread interleaving; pinned by `overlapping_objects_are_painted_with_the_same_foreground` and `overlapping_objects_paint_the_same_value`. | `sitk-filters` `label_map_overlay.rs` |
| 4.29 | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` — labels are range-checked against `pixel_id` | `itk::LabelMap`'s `LabelType` *is* the label image's pixel type, so an out-of-range label cannot exist upstream; the narrowing happens in the caller's `static_cast` before `AddLabelObject`/`SetLine` are ever reached. This port carries labels as `i64`, so it enforces the same guarantee at a single private seam (`insert_object`): every key, and the background value, must lie inside `PixelId::integer_scalar_bounds`, else `Error::LabelOutOfRange`. `add_label_object`, `push_label_object` and `set_line` all route through it; `new` and `set_background` range-check the background for the same reason (`to_label_image` fills every uncovered pixel with it). No upstream behaviour is lost: the states this rejects are exactly the ones `LabelType` makes unrepresentable. | `sitk-core` `label_map.rs` |
| 4.30 | `sitk-io` `meta_image.rs` — `ElementNumberOfChannels` written unconditionally | `metaImage.cxx:2341-2346` emits the key only when the count is > 1; this port's writer emits it for every image, including `= 1` for scalars (pre-existing behavior from before multi-channel support, kept so existing single-channel files/tests stay byte-identical). Semantically inert to real MetaIO readers: the field is optional and defaults to 1. | `sitk-io` `meta_image.rs` |
| 4.31 | `sitk-core` `image.rs` — `Display`/`to_string()` is not `itk::Image::Print` | Upstream's text embeds RTTI names, reference counts, `PipelineMTime`/`UpdateMTime`, the observer list, and raw addresses (`itkDataObject.cxx:258-283`, `itkImageBase.hxx:501-531`, `itkImage.hxx:146-155`) — unreproducible without the ITK object model. This port prints pixel type, geometry, and the dictionary. | `sitk-core` `image.rs` `Display` |
| 4.32 | `sitk-core` `image.rs` — `transform_physical_point_to_index` saturates out-of-range floats | ITK's `static_cast<IndexValueType>` after `RoundHalfIntegerUp` is C++-undefined outside the target range (the round's own doc warns the magnitude must stay below `max()/2`); Rust `as` saturates, defined. In-range values agree exactly. | `sitk-core` `image.rs` |
| 4.33 | `sitk-core` `image.rs` — `meta_data` returns `Option<&str>` | SimpleITK's `GetMetaData` throws on an absent key (`MetaDataDictionary::Get`, `itkMetaDataDictionary.cxx:150-158`); an `Option` is the idiomatic Rust shape for the same information. | `sitk-core` `image.rs` |
| 4.34 | `sitk-core` `image.rs` — `to_vector_image`/`to_scalar_image` have no `inPlace` flag | Upstream's `inPlace` bool decides whether the receiver is also rebound; Rust ownership collapses the flag — `img = img.to_vector_image()?` is the in-place spelling. Both take `&self` and return a new `Image`. | `sitk-core` `image.rs` |
| 4.35 | `math.rs` `round` | `itk::Math::Round<TOutput,TInput>` (`RoundHalfIntegerUp`, `itkMath.h:191-204`) dispatches purely on `sizeof(TReturn)` via `itkTemplateFloatingToIntegerMacro` (`:130-146`) to an `int32_t`- or `int64_t`-intermediate `RoundHalfIntegerUp_base` (`itkMathDetail.h:108-116`), with **no check that `TReturn` is actually an integer type** despite the doc comment two lines above claiming it must be (`:171`) — `RoundImageFilter`'s `TOutput` is `Float32`/`Float64`, so it silently takes the `int32_t`/`int64_t` path regardless. When `\|round(x)\|` exceeds that intermediate integer type's range, the `static_cast<int32_t>(x)`/`static_cast<int64_t>(x)` step is itself an out-of-range float-to-int cast — C++ UB (commonly the "integer indefinite" sentinel via `cvttss2si`/`cvttsd2si` on real hardware). This port's `f64`-compute engine has no such intermediate: it always returns the mathematically correct rounded value directly, never that sentinel. | `math.rs` module doc (`round` section) |
| 4.36 | `rank.rs` `rank` empty-window wraparound | `RankHistogram`'s order-statistic index is computed as `m_Entries - 1` on an unsigned `SizeValueType`; when a caller-built `StructuringElement::from_mask` excludes the center offset, a boundary pixel can have every on-cell cropped away (`m_Entries == 0`), and the subtraction wraps to a huge value — well-defined C++ unsigned overflow, but nonsensical output, not raised as an error upstream. (`box_`/`cross`/`ball` structuring elements always keep the center on, so this needs a hand-built mask to reach.) This port rejects the condition explicitly with [`FilterError::EmptyRankNeighborhood`] instead of reproducing the wraparound. | `rank.rs` module doc / `error.rs` |
| 4.37 | `sitk-io` `error.rs` | `IoError::UnknownExtension` is gone, replaced by one variant per upstream throw site: `NoReaderFound` (`ImageReaderBase::GetImageIOBase`'s "Unable to determine ImageIO reader"), `NoWriterFound` (`ImageFileWriter::GetImageIOBase`'s "Unable to determine ImageIO writer"), `FileNotFound` (the `itksys::SystemTools::FileExists` check that precedes the reader lookup, `sitkImageReaderBase.cxx:74-100`), `UnknownImageIo` (`ioutils::CreateImageIOByName`). The port never carried the extension in the message because it never matched on the extension alone. | `sitk-io/src/error.rs` |
| 4.38 | `ImageFileReader::set_extract_index` | Takes `&[usize]`; upstream is `std::vector<int>` and its bounds check `largestRegion.IsInside(region.GetIndex())` is what rejects a negative index. Making it unrepresentable is a strict narrowing of the accepted inputs, not of the accepted *results*: every negative index upstream throws. | `sitk-io/src/reader.rs` |
| 4.39 | `ImageFileReader::information()` / dimension ceiling | `GetPixelID`/`GetSize`/… on a reader that has not run `ReadImageInformation` return `sitkUnknown` / empty vectors upstream; this port returns `Option<&ImageInformation>` so the un-read state is one value, not eight sentinels. No `SITK_IO_INPUT_MAX_DIMENSION` / `SITK_MAX_DIMENSION` ceiling is enforced (`sitkImageFileReader.cxx:300-325`), matching the rest of this port, which does not cap `Image` dimension; `IoError::UnsupportedImageDimension` still rejects the `dimension < 2` half of upstream's check. | `sitk-io/src/reader.rs` |
| 4.40 | `sitk-io` MetaImage `LIST` reader | The three §1.44 paths are closed rather than reproduced, because each of them hands back uninitialized memory — unrepresentable in safe Rust and uncheckable by a caller. A header listing fewer slice files than `totalFiles` is `IoError::TruncatedData` instead of a silent success. A **negative** `fileImageDim` folds into the same `NDims - 1` fallback upstream already applies to `0` and `> NDims`, instead of indexing `m_DimSize[-1]`. `fileImageDim == NDims` means "one file holding the whole image" — the value the surrounding `totalFiles`/stride arithmetic implies — instead of reading past the end of `m_SubQuantity`. | `sitk-io/src/meta_image.rs` |
| 4.41 | `sitk-io` MetaImage writer | Does **not** emit the meta-data dictionary as header fields, though `MetaImageIO::WriteImageInformation` stringifies every dictionary entry except `ITK_ExperimentDate` / `ITK_VoxelUnits` (which become `AcquisitionDate` / `DistanceUnits`) and appends it as a MetaIO user field (`itkMetaImageIO.cxx:383-533`). The written bytes are pinned by this crate's header tests, and round-tripping the dictionary would grow every file by the `ITK_InputFilterName` / `Modality` lines the reader itself synthesizes (`:271-277`). See §5.13. | `sitk-io/src/meta_image.rs` |
| 4.42 | `ImageFileReader` extract on complex pixels | Region extraction rejects complex pixel types with `IoError::Unsupported` instead of copying interleaved real/imaginary components. Unreachable through `MetaImageIo`, whose element types have no complex member; the guard exists so the next format that does cannot silently produce a half-copied buffer. | `sitk-io/src/reader.rs` |
| 4.43 | `sitk-core::ops` scalar-constant arithmetic vs. `sitk-filters`'s existing `*_constant` functions | `sitk-filters::add_constant`/`subtract_constant`/`multiply_constant`'s module doc (`lib.rs:14-18`) claims accumulating in `f64` then narrowing with a saturating cast "matches SimpleITK's double-constant functor" — verified false: `sitkBinaryFunctorFilterTemplate.cxx.jinja:140-147` converts the `double` constant to the **image's pixel type first** via `ToPixelType` (`sitkToPixelType.hxx:31-36`, a plain `static_cast<TPixel>`), then runs the *same* wrapping pixel-type `Add2`/`Sub2`/`Mult`/`Div`/`Modulus`/`AND`/`OR`/`XOR` functor as the image⊕image case — cast-first-then-wrap, uniformly across every `constant_type` (`double` for Add/Subtract/Multiply/Divide, `uint32_t` for Modulus, `int` for And/Or/Xor; all four yamls share `template_code_filename: BinaryFunctorFilter`). `sitk_core::ops`'s new `Image + f64` etc. implement the verified cast-first-then-wrap policy directly (via `Scalar::from_f64`), which now **disagrees** with `sitk_filters::add_constant`/`subtract_constant`/`multiply_constant` for a fractional or out-of-range constant. `add_constant`/`subtract_constant`/`multiply_constant` are unchanged (out of scope for the operator-surface task that found this); `modulus`/`and`/`or`/`xor` have no existing `sitk-filters` `*_constant` counterpart to disagree with. See §5.14. | `sitk-core` `ops.rs` module doc |
| 4.44 | `sitk-registration` `BSplineTransformInitializer` order/dimension caps | SimpleITK's filter supports spline order 0-3 (`SetOrder`, `sitkBSplineTransformInitializerFilter.h:86-95`; dispatch table `.cxx:123-136`) but registers member functions only for 2-D/3-D images (`.cxx:53-56`) — even though `itk::BSplineTransformInitializer`'s own domain math and this port's `BSplineTransform` are both dimension-generic. This port's `BSplineTransform` hardcodes cubic order 3 only, so `BSplineTransformInitializer::execute` rejects any `order != 3` (`RegistrationError::UnsupportedBSplineOrder`) — narrower than upstream's order range — but places no dimension cap at all — wider than upstream's 2-D/3-D registration limit, since the port's domain math never needed one. Mesh-size length is validated exactly against the image's dimension rather than SimpleITK's hardcoded 3-long truncate-if-longer vector (ledger §3.3/§4.9 convention). | `bspline_initializer.rs` module doc |
| 4.45 | `sitk-transform` `VersorRigid3DTransform::set_matrix` has no separate cached matrix | `MatrixOffsetTransformBase::SetMatrix` (`itkMatrixOffsetTransformBase.h:232-236`) stores the caller's matrix verbatim in `m_Matrix` and only *derives* the versor (parameters) from it via the virtual `ComputeMatrixParameters` (`itkVersorTransform.hxx:130-135`: `m_Versor.Set(this->GetMatrix())`) — a subsequent `GetMatrix()` echoes the caller's input exactly, bit for bit. This port's `VersorRigid3DTransform` has no matrix distinct from its versor: [`matrix()`](VersorRigid3DTransform::matrix) is always re-derived from the stored versor, as every other mutator on the type already does, so after `set_matrix(M)`, `matrix()` can differ from `M` by a few ULPs from the round trip through quaternion conversion — even when `M` was already accepted as sufficiently orthonormal by the `Epsilon()` gate. | `transform.rs` (`VersorRigid3DTransform::set_matrix` doc comment) |
| 4.46 | `sitk-transform` `TranslationTransform::fixed_parameters` | `itk::TranslationTransform` never overrides `GetFixedParameters`, so it inherits `itk::Transform`'s `m_FixedParameters` — a **zero-length** array (`itkTransform.h`), which is what `itkTxtTransformIO` writes as an empty `FixedParameters:` line. `SetFixedParameters` is likewise a no-op that accepts any input. This port returns an empty `Vec` (matching the write side exactly) but *rejects* a non-empty `set_fixed_parameters` with `TransformError::InvalidFixedParameters` rather than ignoring it, so a mis-sized transform file cannot silently produce a transform whose fixed parameters were dropped. Pinned by `translation_has_no_fixed_parameters`. | `sitk-transform` `transform.rs` |
| 4.47 | `sitk-io` transform reader demands an exact parameter count | ITK's `SetParameters` overrides disagree on strictness: `MatrixOffsetTransformBase` and `TranslationTransform` throw only when the vector is *shorter* than needed and silently ignore trailing values, `VersorTransform::SetParameters` checks nothing at all and indexes `parameters[0..3]`, and `BSplineTransform::SetParameters` demands exact equality. Rather than reproduce four policies (one of which is an out-of-bounds read on a short vector), every transform's own `set_parameters` requires `parameters.len() == number_of_parameters()` uniformly and returns `TransformError::InvalidParameters` otherwise. **Revised 2026-07-10 (§5.16 option (b) executed):** this check used to live only in the reader's `apply()`, duplicated ahead of an infallible `set_parameters`; now that `set_parameters` validates its own length, `apply()` just propagates the transform's own error via `?` and the pre-check was deleted. Files ITK itself wrote always satisfy this. Pinned by `a_parameter_count_that_does_not_match_the_transform_is_an_error`. | `sitk-io` `transform_io.rs` (`apply`), `sitk-transform` `transform.rs` (`check_len`) |
| 4.48 | `sitk-transform` erased `Transform::class_name` / `Display` | Upstream's `itk::simple::Transform::GetName()` returns the constant `"Transform"`; each *derived* SimpleITK class (`AffineTransform`, `Euler2DTransform`, …) overrides it. This port has no derived classes — the enum *is* the erased type — so `class_name()` reports the wrapped concrete transform's name, the useful half of that pair. Likewise `ToString()` embeds the ITK object's `PrintSelf` dump upstream; this port's `Display` prints the transform's file-format identity (class name, parameters, fixed parameters), which is stable and testable. | `sitk-transform` `erased.rs` module doc |
| 4.49 | `sitk-transform` `Transform::inverse` on `DisplacementFieldTransform` | `itk::DisplacementFieldTransform` inverts by holding a *separately set* inverse displacement field (`SetInverseDisplacementField`); `GetInverse` merely swaps the two fields and fails when no inverse field was supplied. This port does not model a second field, so `Transform::inverse()` returns `TransformError::NoInverse` for it — as it does for `BSplineTransform` (no ITK inverse at all) and for `ScaleVersor3DTransform`/`ScaleSkewVersor3DTransform`, whose `ComputeMatrixParameters` throws upstream. | `sitk-transform` `erased.rs` |
| 4.50 | `sitk-io` `ComponentTransformFile:` recursion is depth-capped | `TxtTransformIO::ReadComponentFile` (`itkTxtTransformIO.cxx:82-104`) constructs a fresh `TransformFileReader` per reference with no cycle or depth check, so a file naming itself recurses until the C++ stack is exhausted. This port caps the chain at `MAX_COMPONENT_DEPTH = 32` and returns `IoError::MalformedTransformFile`. Not a memory-safety bug in Rust (the stack overflow would abort, not corrupt), but a denial of service on untrusted input with no upstream behavior worth preserving. | `sitk-io` `transform_io.rs` |
| 4.51 | `sitk-io` NRRD per-axis numeric field parsers | `sizes`, `spacings`, `thicknesses`, `axis mins` and `axis maxs` parse exactly `dim` values and raise `IoError::MalformedNrrdHeader` when the field carries a different count. Upstream detects the same "too many values" condition by parsing `dim + 1` values into a `NRRD_DIM_MAX`-long stack array, which overflows at `dim == 16` (§1.46). The observable behaviour is identical for every `dim < 16`; at `dim == 16` this port errors where upstream corrupts the stack. Closed rather than reproduced because the defect is memory unsafety, unrepresentable in safe Rust. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` |
| 4.52 | `sitk-io` NRRD meta-data dictionary is `String -> String` | ITK's `MetaDataDictionary` is type-erased, so `NrrdImageIO` stores `NRRD_thicknesses[i]`, `NRRD_old min`, `NRRD_old max` as `double` and `NRRD_measurement frame` as a `std::vector<std::vector<double>>`, and its writer reads those types straight back out (`itkNrrdImageIO.cxx:800-880`). This crate's dictionary is `BTreeMap<String, String>` (`Image::meta_data`), so the reader stringifies the doubles with Rust's shortest-round-trip formatting and the frame with the header's own parenthesised column spelling `(a,b,c) (d,e,f)`, and the writer parses them back. A dictionary value a caller wrote by hand in another spelling (`1.0e0`, a comma-free frame) will not parse; upstream would have rejected it at the `Get<double>` type check instead. Round trips through this crate's own reader/writer are exact. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` |
| 4.53 | `sitk-io` NRRD encoding and `data file:` coverage | Reads and writes `encoding: raw` and `encoding: gzip`; reads `encoding: ascii`/`text`/`txt` but never writes it. **Corrected 2026-07-10** (this row previously claimed "ITK's writer hardcodes `nrrdEncodingTypeRaw`, `itkNrrdImageIO.cxx:940`", which is wrong): `itkNrrdImageIO.cxx:1404-1411` sets `nio->encoding = m_NrrdCompressionEncoding` and `nio->zlibLevel = GetCompressionLevel()` whenever `GetUseCompression()` is set, and the constructor's `SetCompressor("")` resolves that encoding to `nrrdEncodingGzip` (`:380-392`). So upstream *does* write gzip under `SetUseCompression(true)`, and this port now does too. The `else` arm picks `nrrdEncodingAscii` only when `GetFileType() == ASCII`, a setter SimpleITK never calls — hence "never writes ascii" still holds. `bzip2` is rejected with `IoError::UnsupportedNrrdFeature` (no bzip2 dependency, §5.8), as are `hex` and `zrl`, which have no ITK write path; `block` element type is rejected as `NrrdImageIO` rejects it (`:145-147`). `line skip` is applied on the *file* stream for every encoding and `byte skip` on the file stream only for the non-compression encodings, exactly as `formatNRRD_read` splits them (`formatNRRD.c:577-605`); under gzip the byte skip runs inside the decompressed buffer and a negative value is legal there (`encodingGzip.c:81-155`), where `nrrd__ByteSkipSkip` rejects it for ascii (`read.c:320-327`). `data file:` supports the bare-filename and `LIST` forms; the `%d` printf-template form and `SKIPLIST` raise `IoError::UnsupportedNrrdFeature`. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` |
| 4.54 | `sitk-io` NRRD checks kind/size consistency at header-parse time | `nrrdKindSize`'s constraint — a `3-vector` axis must have size 3, `3D-symmetric-matrix` size 6, `complex` size 2, and so on — is enforced upstream by `nrrdCheckMore`, which `NrrdImageIO` reaches only indirectly, on the path through `nrrdSpacingCalculate`/`nrrd__HeaderCheck`. This port runs the same check unconditionally as the last step of header parsing, so `read_information` on a header with `kinds: 3-vector` and `sizes: 4 ...` errors immediately instead of after the geometry is built. Same predicate, earlier and unconditional. | `sitk-io/src/nrrd.rs` |
| 4.55 | `nifti.rs::is_affine` keeps only the two live tests of ITK's | ITK's `IsAffine` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:1535-1590`) makes three checks: (a) the bottom row is `(0,0,0,1)` to within `float` epsilon; (b) `vnl_matrix_inverse::well_condition()` — the SVD's `σmin/σmax` — exceeds `DBL_EPSILON`; (c) the top-left 3×3 of the 4×4 inverse equals the inverse of the top-left 3×3, and the two translations agree. Given (a), (c) holds by construction: a matrix with bottom row `(0,0,0,1)` has an inverse whose top-left block *is* `inv(top3x3)` and whose translation *is* `−inv(top3x3)·t`. The two one-norm comparisons against `1e-2` can therefore only fire on `float` rounding. This port implements (a) and (b), over its own `jacobi_svd`. Same accept/reject verdict; no upstream defect implied. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.56 | `qfac` and `qto_xyz` are omitted from the meta-data dictionary | `SetImageIOMetadataFromNIfTI` encapsulates `qfac` as a `float` and `qto_xyz` as an `itk::Matrix<float,4,4>` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:625-800`). This crate's `ImageInformation::metadata` and `sitk_core::Image`'s dictionary are `BTreeMap<String, String>`, matching SimpleITK's flattened view, and SimpleITK's `GetMetaData` cannot surface a non-string entry either. Every string-valued key upstream writes is present. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.57 | Hand-rolled one-sided Jacobi SVD in place of VNL/`itk::Math::SVD` | Used in the three places `NiftiImageIO` needs singular values — `IsAffine`'s `well_condition()` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:1558`), `sform_and_qform_are_very_similar`'s two `itk::Math::SVD` calls (`:1771-1781`), and the `ITK_NIFTI_SFORM_PERMISSIVE` polar factor `U·Vᵀ` (`:1810`). The workspace has no VNL, no Eigen, and no linear-algebra dependency. Singular values agree to `f64` rounding; `U` and `V` are canonical only up to a per-column sign, which cancels in `U·Vᵀ` and is irrelevant to the two comparisons. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.58 | Little-endian hosts only, for writing | `nifti_image_write_engine` emits the header and data in **host** byte order, so an ITK built on a big-endian host writes big-endian NIfTI. This port always writes little-endian. Reading is unaffected: a big-endian file is detected by `dim[0]` being out of range and byte-swapped on load, exactly as `need_nhdr_swap` does upstream. Pinned by `nii_big_endian_file_reads_on_a_little_endian_host`. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.59 | A rescaled integer *vector* image is refused rather than read out of bounds | Closes ITK's heap over-read §1.49, which Rust cannot reproduce without `unsafe`. `read` returns `IoError::UnsupportedNiftiFeature` naming the heap overflow when `MustRescale()` holds, the on-disk type is an integer, and the image has more than one component per voxel. Pinned by `nii_rescaled_integer_vector_image_is_refused_rather_than_overflowing`. The memory-safe sibling §1.50 (partial rescale of a complex image) has since been fixed in this port rather than reproduced. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.60 | `ITK_NIFTI_SFORM_PERMISSIVE` is read per call, not cached at construction | ITK reads the environment variable once, into a static, on first use. `sform_permissive()` calls `std::env::var` on each orientation decode. Observable only if the variable changes mid-process; no reader in this crate holds state across files, and a per-call read keeps `NiftiImageIo` zero-sized so it can live in the `static` registry. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.61 | An intent-vector header with `dim[5] == 0` is rejected | ITK computes `numComponents = dim[5]` for `NIFTI_INTENT_VECTOR`/`DISPVECT` (`itkNiftiImageIO.cxx:786-805`) without checking it, and the strides computed from it divide by zero downstream. This port returns `IoError::MalformedNiftiHeader`. Upstream defect is division-by-zero UB, not memory unsafety, but the header is unusable either way. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.62 | `.nia` and legacy-Analyze *writing* are unimplemented | `NIFTI_FTYPE_ASCII` (`.nia`) and `SetUseLegacyModeForTwoFileWriting`'s Analyze-7.5 output are dead through SimpleITK, which exposes neither switch; both are refused with `IoError::UnsupportedNiftiFeature` after the extension has been classified exactly as upstream classifies it (so `.nia` is *claimed* for writing and then refused — pinned by `nia_is_claimed_for_writing_and_then_refused`). Reading an Analyze-7.5 *header* is supported — `nifti_convert_nhdr2nim`'s `is_nifti` gate makes it nearly free. **Updated 2026-07-10**: `.nii.gz` / `.hdr.gz` / `.img.gz` were recognised and refused pending §5.8; they now read and write (§2.113, §3.40, §5.18). | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.63 | Dictionary numbers are formatted by Rust's `Display`, not `itk::NumberToString` | Both are shortest-round-trip decimal, so every value in the `.nii` range prints identically. They differ only in the exponential-notation threshold: Google's double-conversion, which `itk::NumberToString` wraps, switches to `1e-07`-style output outside `1e-6 .. 1e21`, whereas Rust's `Display` never does. Affects only dictionary *strings* (`scl_slope`, `srow_*`, `cal_min`, …), never header bytes. Note both render a negative zero as `-0`, which is what an identity-direction image's `srow_x[3] = -0.0f` produces. | `nifti.rs` |
| 4.64 | An in-place initial transform does not alias the caller's `Transform` | `SetInitialTransform(Transform &, bool inPlace)` with `inPlace = true` calls `transform.MakeUnique()` and then shares the refcounted `itk::TransformBase::Pointer` with the method, so `Execute` mutates the *caller's* C++ object in place (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:136-155`, `itkImageRegistrationMethodv4.hxx:733-751`, where the initial transform is grafted as the output). A Rust `Transform` is a value, not a refcounted handle, so this port takes it by value and there is nothing to alias. Everything else the flag controls is reproduced exactly: in-place updates the method's stored transform and returns it with its concrete kind; not-in-place leaves the stored transform alone and returns a composite (§3.34). Read the optimum back with `execute_with_initial_transform`'s return value or `initial_transform()`. | `method.rs` (`set_initial_transform_in_place`) |
| 4.65 | With no initial transform set, `metric_evaluate` evaluates at a dimension-matched identity instead of throwing | Upstream's `m_InitialTransform` default-constructs to `itk::IdentityTransform<double,3>`; `EvaluateInternal` then `dynamic_cast`s it to the image's `InitialTransformType`, which succeeds for 3-D images and throws `"Unexpected error converting initial transform! Possible miss matching dimensions!"` for 2-D ones (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:1082-1086`). This crate has no `IdentityTransform` class (§3.33), so an unset initial transform becomes a zero `TranslationTransform` of the images' dimension — the identity, at every dimension. `execute_with_initial_transform` still requires one explicitly (`RegistrationError::NoInitialTransform`), since there the transform is what gets optimized. | `method.rs` (`metric_evaluate`) |
| 4.66 | The fixed image is read with linear interpolation, not with the configured interpolator | `SetupMetric` builds *both* interpolators from `m_Interpolator` (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:1137-1143`), so upstream's fixed interpolator follows `SetInterpolator`. This port materializes `F(fixed_initial(x))` by resampling the fixed image onto the virtual grid once per level, with linear interpolation, rather than interpolating per sample. `set_interpolator` therefore selects the *moving*-image interpolator only — which is the one the metric's parameter derivative flows through, and the one every `set_interpolator` test exercises. Pre-existing in `prepare_level`; made explicit now that a virtual domain and a fixed-initial transform can move the fixed sample points off the voxel centers. | `method.rs` (`prepare_level`) |
| 4.67 | `metric_evaluate` does not reject a fixed/moving pair of differing pixel types | `MetricEvaluate` raises `"Fixed and moving images must be the same datatype!"` when the two `PixelIDValue`s differ (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:998-1002`), because its member-function factory dispatches one template instantiation on the fixed type alone. Every metric in this crate reads both images through `Image::to_f64_vec`, so there is no instantiation to mismatch and mixed pixel types evaluate correctly. The dimension check (`:1004-1008`) *is* reproduced, as `RegistrationError::DimensionMismatch`. | `method.rs` (`metric_evaluate`) |
| 4.68 | `.gipl.gz` is wired to the compression module, closing the earlier claim-then-refuse stopgap | **Updated 2026-07-10**: `GiplImageIO` handles compressed files with a `gzFile` (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:249-256`, `:665-672`); this port now reuses [`crate::compression`]'s gzip door instead — `GiplImageIo::can_read_file`, `read` and `read_information` decompress with `gunzip_transparent`/`gunzip_transparent_prefix` before parsing exactly as the uncompressed path does, and `write` compresses the same bytes the uncompressed path would have written with `gzip_compress` at zlib's default level (never a chosen one — §3.41). This closes the earlier stopgap, which claimed `.gipl.gz` on its name alone — upstream verifies the magic number *through* the gzip stream, which the workspace's original zero-dependency state made unavailable (§5.8) — and refused every operation with `IoError::UnsupportedGiplFeature` naming zlib; same precedent as `.nii.gz`'s own now-closed stopgap, §4.62. Pinned by `gipl_gz_is_recognised_and_round_trips`, `gipl_gz_roundtrip_every_supported_scalar_type_2d_and_3d`, `gipl_gz_reads_a_hand_built_stored_block_gzip_stream`, `gipl_gz_over_a_non_gzip_stream_reads_transparently`. | `gipl.rs` |
| 4.69 | A truncated pixel block is an error, not an uninitialised buffer tail | GIPL's `Read` tests `!bad()` (§1.53) and VTK's discards `ReadBufferAsBinary`'s `bool` (§1.54); both return success over a buffer whose tail was never written. That is indeterminate-value C++ UB and unreachable in safe Rust, so `gipl::read` and `vtk::read` return `IoError::TruncatedData`. Pinned by `gipl_truncated_pixel_data_is_an_error` and `vtk_truncated_binary_data_is_an_error`. | `gipl.rs`, `vtk.rs` |
| 4.70 | An under-filled VTK `DIMENSIONS` line is an error; an under-filled `SPACING`/`ORIGIN` keeps the defaults | Upstream ignores every `sscanf` return value (§1.55). `dims[3]` is an uninitialised local, so this port raises `IoError::MalformedVtkHeader("DIMENSIONS needs three values")` rather than reading indeterminate axis lengths; `spacing`/`origin` are default-initialised to `1.0`/`0.0` by `ImageIOBase`, so a short line there keeps those defaults, which is what upstream effectively does. `sscanf`'s own semantics are otherwise reproduced: conversion stops at the first failure and leaves the remaining arguments untouched, `%u` accepts a sign (`DIMENSIONS -1 1 1` gives `4294967295`), and trailing junk in a token is ignored. Pinned by `vtk_under_filled_dimensions_line_is_an_error`, `vtk_under_filled_spacing_line_keeps_the_defaults`, `scan_u32_follows_sscanf_percent_u`, `scan_triple_stops_at_the_first_failed_conversion`. | `vtk.rs` |
| 4.71 | `VtkImageIo::can_read_file` returns `false` where upstream throws | `VTKImageIO::CanReadFile` lets `GetNextLine`'s `"Premature EOF"` escape through `ImageIOFactory::CreateImageIO` (§2.108). A probe that throws is not expressible in the `ImageIo` trait, whose `can_read_file` returns `bool`, so this port maps every error raised while reading the four probe lines to `false`; the file is then reported as `IoError::NoReaderFound`. Pinned by `vtk_can_read_file_does_not_throw_on_a_short_file`. | `vtk.rs` |
| 4.72 | The VTK 64-bit type names are pinned to the LP64 spellings | `VTKImageIO::GetComponentTypeAsString` overrides `LONGLONG`/`ULONGLONG` to VTK's `vtktypeint64`/`vtktypeuint64` (`itkVTKImageIO.cxx:151-163`) and delegates the rest to `ImageIOBase`, which prints `long`/`unsigned_long` for `LONG`/`ULONG`. Which arm an `int64_t` image takes is decided by the host: `MapPixelType<long>` is `LONG` and `MapPixelType<long long>` is `LONGLONG` (`itkImageIOBase.h:645-647`), and `int64_t` is `long` under LP64 (Linux) but `long long` on macOS and Windows. `sitk-io` has one `PixelId::Int64`, so `write` pins the LP64 spelling (`long`) and `read` accepts all four (`long`, `long_long`, `vtktypeint64`, and the unsigned counterparts). A `.vtk` written on Linux and read on macOS therefore differs in one header token from one written on macOS. Pinned by `vtk_int64_writes_as_long_and_both_spellings_read_back`. | `vtk.rs` |
| 4.73 | A GIPL header shorter than 256 bytes is an error | `ReadImageInformation` reads each field with an unchecked `m_Ifstream.read`, over locals (`pixdim`, `origin`, `matrix`, …) that are never zero-initialised, so a short header leaves the spacing and origin indeterminate. `gipl::parse_header` requires all 256 bytes and returns `IoError::TruncatedData`. `GiplImageIo::can_read_file` likewise reports `false` rather than reading a short seek. Pinned by `gipl_short_header_is_an_error`. | `gipl.rs` |
| 4.74 | `fft_correlation.rs::factorize_number(0)` returns `0` instead of hanging | `MaskedFFTNormalizedCorrelationImageFilter::FactorizeNumber` (hxx:528-545) runs `for (; n % ifac == 0;) n /= ifac;` — with `n == 0` the test stays true and the quotient stays `0`, so the loop never terminates. `FindClosestValidDimension` reaches it whenever `combinedImageSize` is `0`, i.e. for a zero-extent input axis, which `sitk-core::Image` permits. Not memory-unsafe, but a livelock is worse than an error in a library. This port returns `0` (no valid factorization), so the caller's search moves to `1` and the correlation produces the empty output the geometry implies. | `fft_correlation.rs` |
| 4.75 | A compressed stream that will not inflate is an error, not silent garbage | Upstream's `MET_PerformUncompression` returns `true` unconditionally (§1.57) and `MetaImage::M_ReadElements` guesses a `LOCAL` header's `CompressedDataSize` as the whole file size (§1.56); together they hand the caller uninitialised heap. Neither is expressible in safe Rust, so this port closes both: `compression::inflate_auto` maps an inflate error to `IoError::CorruptCompressedData` and a short inflate to `IoError::TruncatedData`, and `meta_image::read` refuses `CompressedData = True` in a `LOCAL` header that carries no `CompressedDataSize` with `IoError::Unsupported`, naming §1.56. The detached-file and `LIST` arms, where upstream's file-length guess is correct, are ported verbatim. Pinned by `mha_local_without_compressed_data_size_is_refused_not_read_as_garbage`, `mha_corrupt_compressed_payload_is_an_error`, `mha_compressed_data_size_beyond_the_file_is_truncation`, and `mhd_without_compressed_data_size_uses_the_zraw_file_length`. Note the divergence is MetaIO-only: NrrdIO and nifti do not error either, but they *transparently copy* (§2.113), which is reproducible and is reproduced. | `compression.rs`, `meta_image.rs`, `error.rs` |
| 4.76 | `SetMetricUse{Fixed,Moving}ImageGradientFilter` is not exposed | Upstream's flag selects between two *estimates* of the image gradient: `GradientRecursiveGaussianImageFilter` with `sigma = max(spacing)` and `NormalizeAcrossScale` (`itkDefaultImageToImageMetricTraitsv4.h:91-94`, configured in `InitializeDefaultFixedImageGradientFilter`, `itkImageToImageMetricv4.hxx:465-480`) when on, and `CentralDifferenceImageFunction` (`itkDefaultImageToImageMetricTraitsv4.h:103-106`) when off. Neither is the gradient of the value the metric actually interpolates. This port's metrics use a third thing: the **exact analytic gradient of the configured interpolant** (`metric.rs`'s `value_and_physical_gradient`), so the metric derivative is the true gradient of the metric value and a finite difference of the value reproduces it — the property both upstream options give up. There is therefore no toggle to port: a flag selecting between two gradient paths this crate does not have would have to either be a no-op or degrade the derivative. The pre-existing choice of the analytic gradient is documented at `metric.rs:27-35`; this row records that the *setter* is deliberately absent, not overlooked. Note the setter is also inert upstream for every metric but Demons (§3.41). | `sitk-registration` `metric.rs` |
| 4.77 | The scales estimator's random sampling uses SplitMix64, not ITK's Mersenne Twister | `SampleVirtualDomainRandomly` draws through `ImageRandomConstIteratorWithIndex` (`itkRegistrationParameterScalesEstimator.hxx:539-583`), seeded from ITK's global MT19937. This port draws the same *count* — `total` when the domain has ≤ `SizeOfSmallDomain = 1000` pixels, else `1000·(1 + ln(total/1000))` capped at `total` — uniformly with replacement from a fixed-seed SplitMix64, the same generator and the same reason `FixedSamples` already uses it for `SamplingStrategy::Random`. Draw-for-draw parity would require porting MT19937 and ITK's iterator ordering. The path is reached only by a transform that is neither linear nor local-support, i.e. only by `BSplineTransform` here (§4.78). | `sitk-registration` `scales.rs` |
| 4.78 | A B-spline transform takes the estimator's random-sampling path, not ITK's B-spline branch | `TransformHasLocalSupportForScalesEstimation()` is `IsDisplacementFieldTransform() \|\| IsBSplineTransform()` (`itkRegistrationParameterScalesEstimator.hxx:203-211`), the latter keyed on `GetTransformCategory() == BSpline` (`:130-144`). This crate's `ParametricTransform::has_local_support` is true only for `DisplacementFieldTransform`, and `BSplineTransform::is_linear()` is false, so a B-spline reaches `Sampling::Random` where ITK would reach `CentralRegionSampling` and then the special `EstimateScales` branch `parameterScales.Fill(minNonZeroShift)` — note that branch fills the *unsquared, unnormalized* min shift (`itkRegistrationParameterScalesFromShiftBase.hxx:98-101`), unlike every other parameter's `shift²/δ²`. Porting it needs a transform-category notion plus a local-support Jacobian for B-splines, neither of which this crate's registration path has. The dense per-parameter probe this port runs instead is exact for the scales it computes; only the sample set and the B-spline `Fill` shortcut differ. | `sitk-registration` `scales.rs` |
| 4.79 | A truncated or corrupt `.gipl.gz` pixel block is an error, extending §4.69 to the compressed path | Upstream's compressed-path success check is `p != nullptr` (§1.58) — even weaker than the uncompressed `!bad()` it sits beside (§1.53/§4.69) — so it is vacuously true regardless of what `gzread` actually delivered. Not expressible in safe Rust: `gipl::read` returns `IoError::TruncatedData` when the decompressed stream is shorter than the declared pixel block, and propagates `IoError::CorruptCompressedData` from `compression::gunzip_transparent` when the gzip stream will not inflate at all — the latter also surfaces from `GiplImageIo::can_read_file`'s own magic-number probe, so a corrupt `.gipl.gz` is never claimed by the registry either, exactly as a short-header `.gipl` is not (§4.73). Pinned by `gipl_gz_truncated_pixel_data_is_an_error` and `gipl_gz_corrupt_stream_is_an_error`. | `gipl.rs` |
| 4.80 | The transform reader asks the text IO before the HDF5 IO, and requires `/TransformGroup` to be a group | `TransformIOFactory::CreateTransformIO` polls each registered factory's `CanReadFile` in registration order. `TxtTransformIO::CanReadFile` looks at the extension alone (`.txt`, `.tfm`); `HDF5TransformIO::CanReadFile` looks at the content alone. The two overlap on one input — an HDF5 file named `.tfm`, which both claim — and upstream's answer there depends on the generated `itkTransformIOFactoryRegisterManager` order. `read_and_fold` fixes the order: text first, HDF5 second, so such a file is parsed as text and fails. Second, `can_read_file` requires the `/TransformGroup` link to actually be a group, closing §2.123's throw-instead-of-decline path. Pinned by `can_read_file_is_content_based_not_extension_based` and `a_transform_group_that_is_a_dataset_is_not_claimed`. | `transform_io.rs` (`read_and_fold`), `transform_hdf5.rs` (`can_read_file`) |
| 4.81 | A floating-point parameter dataset whose elements are neither 4 nor 8 bytes wide is rejected | `ReadParameters` branches on `ParamType.getSize() == sizeof(double)`, reading through `NATIVE_DOUBLE` or else `NATIVE_FLOAT` (`itkHDF5TransformIO.cxx:180-197`), and lets libhdf5 *convert* whatever float type is stored — a 2-byte half or a 16-byte long double included. `rust-hdf5`'s `read_raw::<T>` performs no conversion: it checks the stored element width against `T` and hands back the bytes. So this port reads the two widths it can reinterpret and returns `IoError::UnsupportedHdf5Transform` for any other, rather than mis-sizing the buffer. No ITK writer emits such a file. | `transform_hdf5.rs` (`read_double_array`), `error.rs` |
| 4.82 | A big-endian parameter dataset is rejected | The same `H5Dread` conversion byte-swaps a big-endian dataset into native order; `rust-hdf5`'s `read_raw` reinterprets the stored bytes, which would silently produce garbage doubles. This port checks the datatype's `byte_order` and returns `IoError::UnsupportedHdf5Transform` instead. ITK on a little-endian host always writes `NATIVE_DOUBLE`, so only a file produced on a big-endian machine can trigger it. | `transform_hdf5.rs` (`read_double_array`), `error.rs` |
| 4.83 | `/HDFVersion` and `/OSVersion` do not carry upstream's strings | `Write()` stamps four informational root datasets: `/ITKVersion` = `Version::GetITKVersion()`, `/HDFVersion` = `H5_VERS_INFO`, `/OSName` = `itksys::SystemInformation::GetOSName()`, `/OSVersion` = `GetOSRelease()` (`itkHDF5TransformIO.cxx:389-392`). This port writes `"6.0.0"` (the ITK release it mirrors, `ITK/CMake/itkVersion.cmake:2-4`), `"rust-hdf5 library version: 0.3.2"` (there is no libhdf5), `uname`'s `sysname` as `std::env::consts::OS` knows it (`Linux` / `Darwin` / `Windows`), and an **empty** `/OSVersion` — reading `uname`'s release needs libc. All four datasets are present, of the right type and shape; nothing in `Read()`, in this port or upstream, ever opens them. Pinned by `the_on_disk_layout_matches_itk_hdf5_transform_io`. | `transform_hdf5.rs` (`write_transform`) |
| 4.84 | `PngImageIo` implements only the always-expand-palette branch | `ReadImageInformation` branches on `m_ExpandRGBPalette` for a `PNG_COLOR_TYPE_PALETTE` source (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:381-414): `true` calls `png_set_palette_to_rgb`, `false` calls `png_set_packing` instead and keeps the raw indices plus `m_ColorPalette` (`m_IsReadAsScalarPlusPalette = true`). Since the flag is always `true` through this crate's ported surface (§2.127), only that branch is implemented: the `png` crate's `Transformations::EXPAND` does exactly `png_set_palette_to_rgb` + `png_set_expand_gray_1_2_4_to_8` + `png_set_tRNS_to_alpha` in one flag. The `m_IsReadAsScalarPlusPalette`/`m_ColorPalette` path — unreachable through `ImageFileReader`, §5.24 — is not ported. | `png.rs` |
| 4.85 | `sCAL`-chunk spacing is not implemented | `ReadImageInformation` reads `px_width`/`px_height` from `png_get_sCAL` when `PNG_sCAL_SUPPORTED` and `PNG_FLOATING_POINT_SUPPORTED` are both compiled in (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:467-478), and `WriteSlice` writes them back with `png_set_sCAL` under the same guard (`:671-673`). The `png` crate parses no such chunk — there is no `sCAL` entry in `png::chunk` at all — so `read_information`/`read` always report unit spacing `[1.0, 1.0]` and `write` never emits the chunk. | `png.rs` |
| 4.86 | `sBIT`-driven shifting is not implemented | `png_get_sBIT`/`png_set_shift` renormalizes samples that use fewer than the full bit depth (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:227-232); the `png` crate parses the chunk into `Info::sbit` but implements no shift transform, so a rare `sBIT`-bearing file reads at full range instead of upstream's renormalized range. | `png.rs` |
| 4.87 | `WritePalette`/indexed write is not implemented | `numComp == 1 && GetWritePalette()` selects `PNG_COLOR_TYPE_PALETTE` (itkPNGImageIO.cxx:582-585) and a following block fills `png_set_PLTE` from `m_ColorPalette` (`:620-659`); SimpleITK exposes no `WritePalette` setter anywhere, so the branch is unreachable through this crate's public writer (§5.24) and every 1-component image writes `Grayscale`, matching `color_type_for`'s never-`Palette` mapping, pinned by `color_type_for_never_selects_palette`. | `png.rs` |
| 4.88 | `image_hdf5` rejects the datasets `rust-hdf5` will not convert, where libhdf5 would | The image IO's counterpart of §4.81/§4.82. `H5Dread` converts the stored elements into the requested `NATIVE_*` memory type; `rust_hdf5::H5Dataset::read_raw` hands back the stored bytes and checks only the element width. So `datatype_to_component` rejects a big-endian dataset (which upstream byte-swaps for `Directions`, `Origin`, `Spacing` and `Dimension` — and, per §1.63, silently *fails* to swap for `VoxelData`), and rejects an integer whose bit precision or bit offset does not fill its bytes. `read_dimensions` additionally requires `Dimension` to be 8-byte unsigned, and `read_doubles` requires `Origin` / `Spacing` / `Directions` to be 4- or 8-byte floats; libhdf5 would convert any numeric type into `NATIVE_ULONG` / `NATIVE_DOUBLE`. Every ITK-written file satisfies all of these. | `image_hdf5.rs` |
| 4.89 | A non-square `Directions` matrix is an error, not a heap overread | The upstream defect is §1.62. `read_directions` requires `shape[0] == shape[1]`, and requires it non-zero — `SetNumberOfDimensions(0)` would leave `Image::assemble` with an empty size vector. | `image_hdf5.rs` |
| 4.90 | A `char`-width meta-data byte above 127 becomes its Latin-1 code point | SimpleITK stringifies a non-`std::string` dictionary entry through `MetaDataObject<T>::Print`, which is `os << value` (`itkMetaDataObject.hxx:65-82`, `sitkMetaDataDictionaryCustomCast.hxx:59-73`). For `signed char` / `unsigned char` and for `itk::Array` of either, `std::ostream`'s `char` overloads win, so the byte is emitted **as a character** into an `std::string` that may then hold a non-UTF-8 byte. This crate's dictionary is `BTreeMap<String, String>`, so `join_chars` maps the byte through `char::from`, i.e. Latin-1: byte `0xB5` becomes `"µ"` (two UTF-8 bytes) where SimpleITK would hold one raw `0xB5`. Bytes 0–127 — every value ITK's own writers produce — are identical. The write direction cannot diverge: this port has no `char` dictionary entry to write (§1.61). | `image_hdf5.rs` |
| 4.91 | `VoxelData`'s dataspace is checked against `Dimension` before any pixel is read | Upstream builds its hyperslab from `m_Dimensions` and lets `H5Sselect_hyperslab` decide (`SetupStreaming`, `:957-997`); a `VoxelData` whose rank or extents contradict `Dimension` produces an H5 exception, garbage, or the §1.62 overread depending on how they differ. `read_header` requires the rank to be the image dimension or one more than it, and the leading extents to be the reverse of `Dimension` exactly. `read_double_vector` and `read_dimensions` likewise reject a dataset shorter than the image dimension and truncate a longer one, which is what upstream's `for (i = 0; i < numDims; ++i)` loops do to a longer one. | `image_hdf5.rs` |
| 4.92 | A mid-scanline decode error returns a hard `Err` instead of a silently short-filled buffer | `Read`'s scanline loop catches a libjpeg longjmp with `itkWarningMacro` and a silent `return` (`itkJPEGImageIO.cxx:226-235, 265-273`), leaving whatever tail of the caller's buffer had not yet been decoded uninitialised while still reporting success — the same shape as the already-ledgered `MET_PerformUncompression` quirk (§4.75). Not expressible in safe Rust (would require exposing uninitialised or partial pixel data as a success): [`read`] returns [`IoError::JpegDecode`] for a failure at any point, header or mid-scan. Pinned by `jpeg_truncated_scan_data_is_claimed_and_then_a_decode_error`. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 4.93 | CMYK read no longer needs to reproduce upstream's branch-dependent behaviour — the ambiguity §1.65 described does not survive `jpeg-decoder` | Per §1.65 (**fixed in this port**, 2026-07-11), upstream's raw-libjpeg formula was right for plain CMYK and wrong for YCCK. This port never actually shared that ambiguity: `jpeg_decoder::Decoder` reads the JPEG's own Adobe APP14 colour-transform marker itself and normalizes both a plain-CMYK and a YCCK source to the same uninverted `PixelFormat::CMYK32` representation before [`read`] ever sees a byte (verified by round-tripping `jpeg_encoder::ColorType::Cmyk` and `::CmykAsYcck` through it). [`cmyk_to_rgb`] now inverts that normalized output before applying ITK's formula, so the same correct RGB comes out of either source encoding — no divergence remains. Pinned by `cmyk_and_ycck_sources_of_the_same_color_read_back_to_the_same_rgb` in `jpeg.rs`'s own test module. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 4.94 | `write` refuses any component count other than 1 or 3 outright; upstream falls to `JCS_UNKNOWN` plus a warning | `WriteSlice`'s `in_color_space` switch has arms only for 1 (`JCS_GRAYSCALE`) and 3 (`JCS_RGB`); anything else falls to `default: JCS_UNKNOWN` plus a warning (`itkJPEGImageIO.cxx:521-533`) — an encoding with no defined colour transform that `jpeg_encoder::ColorType`'s fixed-arity, named variants have no counterpart for. [`write`] refuses any component count other than 1 or 3 with [`IoError::UnsupportedJpegFeature`] rather than attempting an ill-defined write. Pinned by the CMYK write-rejection test in `jpeg.rs`'s own test module. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 4.95 | The density-write bug's *effect* is reproduced, not its exact on-wire bytes | Per §1.64, `jpeg_encoder::Density`'s `None`/`Inch`/`Centimeter` variants hardwire the on-wire JFIF unit byte per variant (`jpeg_encoder::writer::JfifWriter::write_header`), so upstream's actual buggy pattern — `unit = 0` with real computed `X_density`/`Y_density` — cannot be expressed. [`density_for_spacing`] reproduces the *effect* (a cm-favoured spacing round-trips to the default `[1.0, 1.0]`) via `Density::None`; [`spacing_from_density`]'s `unit == 2` guard fails identically for both byte patterns, so the observable round-trip behaviour matches exactly even though the on-wire bytes differ. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 4.96 | A 2- or 5-plus-component JPEG cannot be read; upstream reads it as `VECTOR` with a warning | `ReadImageInformation`'s component-count switch has a `default:` arm that accepts *any* component count as `IOPixelEnum::VECTOR` with only a warning (`itkJPEGImageIO.cxx:412-417`). `jpeg_decoder::Decoder` hard-rejects any frame with component count outside `{1, 3, 4}` — `Err(Unsupported(ComponentCount(n)))` before a `FrameInfo` is ever stored (jpeg-decoder's `decoder.rs:368-372`) — so this port cannot read a file upstream (oddly) can. Pinned by a hand-built 18-byte 2-component `SOF0` fixture asserting `IoError::JpegDecode`, not a panic. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 4.97 | A >8-bit-precision (lossless) JPEG is refused, matching every real ITK build | `m_ComponentType` is hard-coded `UCHAR` at compile time — `#if BITS_IN_JSAMPLE == 8` / `#error` otherwise (`itkJPEGImageIO.cxx:292-297`) — so no mainline ITK build reads a >8-bit/lossless JPEG either. [`header_from_info`] refuses `PixelFormat::L16` with [`IoError::UnsupportedJpegFeature`]. Not observably different from any real ITK build, since upstream's own restriction is a compile-time constant, not a runtime check this port could instead match at runtime. | `jpeg.rs` |
| 4.98 | `tiff.rs` | `ReadVolume`'s two heap overflows (§1.66) cannot be written in safe Rust. `read_current_page` refuses any page whose `pixel_offset + page_len` exceeds the buffer, so the `[REDUCEDIMAGE, 0, 0]` and `[untagged, 0]` page shapes report `IoError::UnsupportedTiffFeature` where upstream corrupts the heap. The common shapes — all directories untagged, or all tagged `0`, or all tagged `FILETYPE_PAGE` as upstream's own writer emits — are unaffected and assemble normally. | `tiff.rs` |
| 4.99 | `tiff.rs` | The mixed-page-geometry over-read (§1.67) is closed by one uniform rule rather than a guard per tag: every directory's `PageTags` — width, height, photometric, bits-per-sample, samples-per-pixel, sample format, planar config, orientation, tiled — must equal directory 0's, and the file is refused otherwise. Upstream reads such a file, silently, past the end of its scanline buffer. This is stricter than upstream on files upstream cannot read correctly anyway. | `tiff.rs` |
| 4.100 | `tiff.rs` | **Palette TIFFs are not readable.** `TIFFReaderInternal::CanRead` admits `PHOTOMETRIC_PALETTE` when `m_BitsPerSample != 32` (`itkTIFFReaderInternal.cxx:286`) and, `m_ExpandRGBPalette` being forced `true` by `ImageIOBase::Reset(false)` (`itkImageIOBase.cxx:45`) exactly as for PNG (§2.131) — `TIFFImageIO`'s constructor never touches it (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:206-233`), and no SimpleITK entry point reaches `SetExpandRGBPalette` — upstream always expands the palette to RGB. The `tiff` crate cannot decode palette pixel data at all: `Decoder::colortype()` returns `UnsupportedError` for `PhotometricInterpretation::RGBPalette`, and every read path goes through it. Per ledger §5.8 the gap is refused rather than substituted; `read` and `read_information` both report `IoError::UnsupportedTiffFeature`. Pinned by `a_palette_tiff_is_refused_by_both_entry_points`. See §5.28. | `tiff.rs` |
| 4.101 | `tiff.rs` | **Superseded by §2.139 — 32-bit-float `MINISWHITE` now reads.** This row described a refusal that existed only to keep an inversion invertible: to reproduce upstream's raw, un-inverted `MINISWHITE` value, the port used to undo the `tiff` crate's own inversion, which for the integer types is an involution (`!x`, `0xffff - x`, `0xffff_ffff - x`) but for `f32` is `1.0 - v` — not invertible under rounding — so a 32-bit-float `MINISWHITE` page was refused rather than risk a last-bit mismatch. §2.139's fix keeps the crate's already-correct inversion instead of reversing it, which removes the only reason the reversal needed to be invertible in the first place: a 32-bit-float `MINISWHITE` page now reads like any other bit depth, pinned by `minis_white_float32_reads_the_crates_own_inverted_value`. | `tiff.rs` |
| 4.102 | `tiff.rs` | **libtiff's `TIFFReadRGBAImageOriented` fallback is not ported.** `TIFFReaderInternal::CanRead` (`itkTIFFReaderInternal.cxx:276-290`) gates the scanline reader on `BitsPerSample ∈ {8,16,32}` (`:289`), a recognised `Photometric` (`:283-286`), `TileDepth == 0` (`:281`), `PlanarConfig == CONTIG \|\| SamplesPerPixel == 1` (`:287`) and `Orientation ∈ {TOPLEFT, BOTLEFT}` (`:288`); everything else — tiled images, planar-separate multi-sample images, `YCbCr`, `CMYK`, `CIELab`, `Logl`, odd bit depths, other orientations — falls back to `RGBAImage`, which asks libtiff to render the page to 8-bit RGBA. The `tiff` crate has no analogue, and reproducing it would mean re-implementing libtiff's colour conversions; per §5.8 the gap is refused. The same refusal covers RGB pages whose `SamplesPerPixel` the crate's `ColorType` cannot name — including the `SamplesPerPixel = 2` files upstream's own writer emits (§2.141). | `tiff.rs` |
| 4.103 | `tiff.rs` | **The TIFF metadata dictionary is not ported.** `ReadTIFFTags` walks libtiff's `TIFFFieldArray` and installs every tag it finds into `m_MetaDataDictionary` (`itkTIFFImageIO.cxx:1055-1256`), and `WriteImageInformation` never reads it back — nothing round-trips, and no SimpleITK entry point exposes the dictionary for a TIFF. `read_information` returns an empty `metadata` map. `TIFFImageIO::WritePalette` is likewise unreachable (no setter is exposed), as for PNG (§4.87). | `tiff.rs` |
| 4.104 | `transform_matlab.rs` | **Three refusals in place of upstream's undefined or non-deterministic behavior.** (a) A complex-valued record (`imag != 0`) is refused with `IoError::UnsupportedMatlabTransformFeature` rather than reproduced: upstream's `ReadMat` (`itkMatlabTransformIO.cxx:50-73`) ignores `vnl_matlab_readhdr::read_data`'s `bool` return, and `read_data` on a complex header fails `type_chck` and returns `false` **without reading the data blocks** — the C++ stream is left desynchronized, so every later record decodes relative to whatever bytes happen to follow next; that has no stable, reproducible outcome to match. (b) A short read of the *second* (fixed) header of a pair is treated uniformly as `"Only vector parameters supported"` regardless of how many of the 20 bytes were actually obtained; upstream's ungated `mathdr2.cols() != 1` check (`:109-114`) only has one *deterministic* input — the clean-end-of-file case, where the header's `std::memset`-zeroed fields make `cols()` read `0` — a genuinely *partial* short read instead leaves indeterminate C++ stack memory in the untouched header fields, which this port cannot reproduce a specific value for. Only the deterministic clean-EOF path is reproduced; the non-deterministic partial-truncation path folds into the same uniform rule rather than being distinguished. (c) A truncated variable name or a truncated data block is a plain IO error (`read_exact`'s `UnexpectedEof`), not an attempt to reproduce whatever indeterminate bytes upstream's own uninitialized buffers would have held. | `transform_matlab.rs` |
| 4.105 | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` | **`execute` never runs the B-spline parameters adaptor; only `execute_with_initial_transform` does.** Upstream has exactly one entry point, `Execute(fixed, moving)`, which always optimizes the stored `m_InitialTransform`, and `m_TransformBSplineScaleFactors` is reachable only through `SetInitialTransformAsBSpline` — every other `SetInitialTransform` overload clears it (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.cxx:121`, `:154`). This port additionally offers `execute(fixed, moving, initial)`, which takes its initial transform as an argument and has no upstream counterpart; it stays a plain multi-level run with no adaptor, so `set_initial_transform_as_bspline` has no effect on it. The adaptation hook itself is a closure parameter of the private `execute_levels`, standing in for ITK's `SetTransformParametersAdaptorsPerLevel` container of one adaptor per level (`itkImageRegistrationMethodv4.hxx:809-849`); a null adaptor is `Ok(())`. | `sitk-registration` `method.rs` |
| 4.106 | `dicom.rs` `read_header` (transfer-syntax gate) | **Encapsulated (compressed) transfer syntaxes are refused, not decoded.** `GDCMImageIO::Read` decompresses through `gdcm::ImageChangeTransferSyntax` (`itkGDCMImageIO.cxx:295-305`), dispatching to GDCM's bundled JPEG (libijg), JPEG-LS (CharLS), JPEG 2000 (OpenJPEG) and RLE codecs, whose pixel output is those libraries' bit-for-bit (a different IDCT / chroma upsampler / planar dance yields *different pixels*, not a different implementation). A pure-Rust substitute (§5.8(a)) would approximate, so every encapsulated syntax raises `IoError::UnsupportedDicomFeature`. Native syntaxes — Implicit VR LE, Explicit VR LE, Explicit VR BE, Deflated Explicit VR LE — are read. Pinned by `encapsulated_transfer_syntax_is_refused`, `native_transfer_syntaxes_only`. | `dicom.rs` (`read_header`, `is_native_transfer_syntax`) |
| 4.107 | `dicom.rs` `read_header` (SOP-class gate) | **Sequence-driven SOP classes are refused.** For the enhanced multi-frame classes `ImageHelper` reads spacing/origin/direction/rescale out of the Shared and Per-frame Functional Groups Sequences `(5200,9229)`/`(5200,9230)`, and for Nuclear Medicine out of `(0054,0022)` (`gdcmImageHelper.cxx:542-574, :676-724, :1087-1149, :1489-1527`). That sequence traversal is not ported; `read_information` refuses those classes rather than read the wrong (top-level) geometry. Pinned by `sequence_driven_sop_class_is_refused`. | `dicom.rs` (`MediaStorage::is_sequence_driven`, `read_header`) |
| 4.108 | `dicom.rs` `z_spacing` | **The `(0028,0009)` Frame Increment Pointer Z-spacing fallback is not ported.** `ImageHelper::GetSpacingValue` (`gdcmImageHelper.cxx:1663-1769`) falls back to the Frame Increment Pointer only when the SOP class has no Z-spacing tag at all; every such class already lands in `MediaStorage::itk_overrides_spacing` or `is_sequence_driven` here, so the fallback is unreachable and `z_spacing` returns the same `1.0` default GDCM produces when the pointer is absent. | `dicom.rs` (`z_spacing`) |
| 4.109 | `dicom.rs` `can_read_file` | **`CanReadFile` additionally requires the file to be openable and to hold an image.** Upstream `GDCMImageIO::CanReadFile` sniffs the `DICM` magic (offsets 128 and 0) plus the `readNoPreambleDicom` heuristic (`itkGDCMImageIO.cxx:196-261, :121-182`), but the reader it fronts (`gdcm::ImageReader::Read`) also requires the object to parse *and* carry an image. `dicom-object` only parses, so that image test is spelled out: a parseable DICOM with no `(7fe0,0010)` Pixel Data (an RTSTRUCT/SR) or zero rows/cols answers `false`. Pinned by `can_read_valid_file_and_rejects_garbage`. | `dicom.rs` (`can_read_file`) |
| 4.110 | `dicom.rs` `apply_palette` | **Segmented palette colour lookup tables `(0028,1221-1223)` are refused.** GDCM routes them through `SegmentedPaletteColorLookupTable` after its own `gdcm_assert(0 && "Please report this image")` (`gdcmPixmapReader.cxx:263-267`) — its author flags them untested — so this port raises `IoError::UnsupportedDicomFeature` rather than guess the expansion. A PALETTE index wider than 8 or 16 bits allocated is refused on the same routine. | `dicom.rs` (`apply_palette`) |
| 4.111 | `dicom.rs` `read_header` / `decode_pixels` (pixel-format gates) | **Five further pixel-format cases are refused rather than approximated:** 12-bit-allocated pixels (GDCM unpacks the packed 12-bit stream in its codec layer, unported); native `YBR_FULL_422` (GDCM's RAWCodec upsamples 4:2:2 chroma through `DecodeByStreams`, unported); `MONOCHROME1` with Bits Allocated ∉ {8,16} (`gdcm::ImageCodec::DoInvertMonochrome` inverts only 8/16-bit pixels — `gdcmImageCodec.cxx:367-430` — so reproducing the no-op would emit an un-inverted MONOCHROME1 as MONOCHROME2); `PALETTE_COLOR` with a Rescale Slope/Intercept and `YBR_FULL` with a Rescale Slope/Intercept (ITK rescales the already-expanded / pre-YCbCr buffer and reinterprets it as `unsigned char`, a size/type mismatch when the output widens — `itkGDCMImageIO.cxx:325-360, :404-417`). `UINT64`/`INT64`/`FLOAT16`/`UNKNOWN` component types are rejected to match upstream's own `itkExceptionMacro`, so those are parity, not divergence. | `dicom.rs` (`read_header`, `decode_pixels`, `apply_palette`) |
| 4.112 | `image_series_reader.rs` | **A wrong-length `ITK_ImageOrigin` override is ignored, not partially applied.** Per §1.73, upstream's `ExposeMetaData` resizes `position1`/`positionN` to whatever length the stored override array happens to have, and the geometry code that follows indexes both up to `ImageDimension` unconditionally — an out-of-bounds `vnl_vector` read for any override shorter than the output dimension. This port cannot reproduce an out-of-bounds read in safe Rust: [`itk_image_origin_override`] parses the meta-data value's whitespace-separated tokens and applies the override only when the count matches `ImageDimension` exactly, falling back to the file's own real origin otherwise — the same "refuse the malformed input rather than reproduce undefined behavior" policy used throughout this crate's IO layer. Pinned by `a_wrong_length_itk_image_origin_override_is_ignored` and `itk_image_origin_override_feeds_spacing_but_not_the_output_origin`. | `image_series_reader.rs` (`itk_image_origin_override`) |
| 4.113 | `image_series_reader.rs` | **Every slice must share the series' own pixel type — a check upstream has no equivalent of.** `itk::ImageFileReader<TOutputImage>::GenerateData` (used per-slice by `itk::ImageSeriesReader`) reads each file's raw samples straight into the fixed compile-time `TOutputImage::PixelType` the series established from its first file, silently narrowing a later slice of a different type — SimpleITK's own header documents the risk without preventing it ("If this leads to a narrowing conversion ... the returned image does not represent the data correctly," `sitkImageSeriesReader.h:56-65`) but adds no check. This crate's `ImageIo` layer has no per-pixel numeric-casting machinery anywhere (`ImageFileReader` does not implement `SetOutputPixelType` either, ledger §6), so silently proceeding would misinterpret one slice's raw buffer as another slice's pixel type — not merely narrow a value, but corrupt the shared output buffer's layout. [`ImageSeriesReader::execute`] instead rejects a slice whose `ImageInformation` disagrees with the series' pixel type (or, for a vector image, its component count) with [`IoError::SeriesPixelTypeMismatch`], a deliberate divergence with no upstream counterpart to be faithful to. Pinned by `pixel_type_mismatch_at_a_middle_slice_is_reported`. | `image_series_reader.rs` (`check_pixel_type`, `IoError::SeriesPixelTypeMismatch`) |

## 5. Open decision points

| # | Question | Options |
|---|---|---|
| 5.1 | **Projection origin bug (§1.1)** — keep bit-for-bit parity (current state) or fix? | (a) keep verbatim; (b) fix to `(size − 1)/2` centering + document divergence; (c) **done 2026-07-10** — reported upstream as ITK issue #6575 (item B1); upstream fix branch prepared same day (incl. `AccumulateImageFilter` sibling + regenerated `.mha` baselines), PR pending test-data upload; parity-vs-fix decision still pending on their resolution. |
| 5.2 | **Crate-added `time_step` guards (§4.6)** — `curvature_flow` and `min_max_curvature_flow` reject unstable steps; ITK does not. Keep the safety guard or drop for parity? Currently inconsistent with `anisotropic_diffusion` (which faithfully warns-and-proceeds… except it can't warn, so it just proceeds). | (a) keep guards; (b) drop both for parity; (c) unify on warn-and-proceed semantics via a returned diagnostic. |
| 5.3 | **`#[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]`** on `threshold_segmentation_level_set` (9 args) and `canny_segmentation_level_set` (11 args), matching existing practice in `region_growing.rs`/`geodesic_active_contour_level_set`/registration modules. Structural fix would be a params struct across the whole family. | (a) accept as crate convention; (b) params-struct refactor for every >7-arg filter. |
| 5.4 | **`fast_marching()` trial-point length rule** — SimpleITK's `sitkSTLVectorToITK` accepts any length ≥ dim and reads `point[dim]` as the seed's initial arrival time; `fast_marching()` (`fast_marching.rs:190`) rejects length ≠ dim, pinned by `trial_point_of_wrong_length_is_an_error`. The newer `fast_marching_upwind_gradient`/`colliding_fronts` implement the upstream rule — so `[0,0,3]` is a valued seed in those two and an error in `fast_marching`. Fixing changes existing public behavior and deletes a pinned test. | (a) align `fast_marching` on len ≥ dim + trailing seed value (parity, breaking); (b) keep the strict check as a documented divergence (§4.9-adjacent), inconsistent within the crate. |
| 5.5 | **`n4_bias_field.rs` mask pixel-type handling** — quantizes any mask pixel type to `UInt8` by value, but SimpleITK's codegen (`CastImageToITK`, `sitkProcessObject.h:386-400`) uses a strict `dynamic_cast`: a non-`UInt8` mask **errors** upstream. The newer `stochastic_fractal_dimension` implements the strict rule (`RequiresUInt8MaskPixelType`) — crate-internal inconsistency. Fixing n4 changes existing public behavior. | (a) align `n4_bias_field` on strict `UInt8` (parity, breaking); (b) keep value-converting quantize as a documented §4 divergence. |
| 5.6 | **`RealType = double` output-type family** — ITK defines `NumericTraits<float>::RealType` as `double` (`itkNumericTraits.h:1349/1356`); several port mappings keep `Float32 → Float32`, so every member outputs `Float32` where upstream outputs `Float64` for a `Float32` input. Full family (audited 2026-07-10, anchor `PixelId::Float32 => PixelId::Float32`): `lib.rs::real_pixel_id` (`fast_marching`, `anti_alias_binary`, `normalize_to_constant`, `normalized_correlation`), `math.rs::real_type` (`divide_real`), `intensity.rs::real_type` (`normalize`), `projection.rs::real_type` (mean/sum/std projections), `fft_correlation.rs::real_type` (both filters), and `vector.rs::edge_potential`'s Float32 output branch. All are now documented divergences at each function. The *non-breaking* members of the misbelief (f32 accumulation branches in `vector_magnitude`/`edge_potential`/`vector_connected_component`; `watershed_classic`'s internal `real_pixel_type`) were fixed 2026-07-10 — only the public output-type flips remain. | (a) flip all six to `double` semantics in one release (parity, breaking); (b) keep as documented divergences. |
| 5.7 | **FFT padding rule and `ForwardFFT` exposure** — `fft.rs:8-20`'s radix-2-only justification is stale: in this ITK checkout the VNL backend is a deprecated wrapper (`itkVnlForwardFFTImageFilter.h:27/:34`) and the always-compiled default is PocketFFT, whose `GetSizeGreatestPrimeFactor()` returns **11** (`itkPocketFFTForwardFFTImageFilter.hxx:72-76`), seeded into `FFTConvolutionImageFilter` at `.hxx:39` — so `itkFFTPadImageFilter` pads each axis to GPF ≤ 11 while this port pads to a power of two (100 → 100 upstream vs → 128 here; whether outputs differ after cropping is **unverified**). And a public `ForwardFFT` does no padding at all (yaml has no pad parameter) — it needs mixed-radix/Bluestein transforms the radix-2 backend cannot provide. Verified against sources 2026-07-10 (pixel-architect finding, spot-checked). **Status: option (a) executed 2026-07-10** (complex pixel type + the six `ComplexTo*`/`*ToComplex` filters merged; `fft.rs` untouched). Remaining open: the mixed-radix/Bluestein rewrite to expose `ForwardFFT`/`InverseFFT` (plus `RealToHalfHermitianForwardFFT`/`HalfHermitianToRealInverseFFT`/public `FFTPad`, surfaced by the 2026-07-10 coverage audit), and whether to align `padded_length` on GPF ≤ 11 (changes existing `fft_convolution`/`deconvolution`/`fft_correlation` transform sizes; output impact after cropping unverified — worth measuring before deciding). **Decided 2026-07-10 (user): proceed with both.** **Executed 2026-07-10 (wave-20, fft-porter): row closed.** `fft.rs` is now a mixed-radix (2/3/5/7/11) Cooley-Tukey transform with a Bluestein fallback, using pocketfft's exact radix constants (`pass3b`/`pass5b`/`pass7`/`pass11`) and its octant-reduced `sincos_2pibyn` twiddle; the five filters live in `sitk-filters::fourier`. `padded_length` is `itkFFTPadImageFilter`'s search at GPF ≤ 11 for `convolution`/`deconvolution`, and `fft_correlation` was moved to the 2/3/5 `FindClosestValidDimension` that filter actually calls (§2.110 — the task's premise that it too should take GPF ≤ 11 was wrong). **No pinned output changed**; the outputs-agree-after-cropping claim of §4.2 was measured, not assumed. New findings: §2.109, §2.110, §2.111, §3.38, §3.39, §4.74. |
| 5.8 | **External dependencies for IO formats** — the workspace has exactly one external crate (`thiserror`). Compressed MetaImage / NRRD gzip / `.nii.gz` / `.gipl.gz` need zlib (`flate2` or pure-Rust `miniz_oxide`, or in-tree inflate/deflate); PNG/JPEG/TIFF need format crates (`png`, `jpeg-decoder`/`zune-jpeg`, `tiff`); DICOM needs `dicom-rs`; transform `.h5` needs the C-binding `hdf5` crate (recommendation: skip `.h5`, ship dep-free `.tfm`/`.txt`). Surfaced by the 2026-07-10 coverage audit; gates the binary-format IO waves. | (a) pure-Rust crates only, no C bindings; (b) all listed; (c) no new deps — in-tree zlib only, dropping PNG/JPEG/TIFF/DICOM; (d) decide per format later; dep-needing waves stay blocked meanwhile. **Decided 2026-07-10 (user): option (a)** — pure-Rust crates only, no C bindings. zlib via a pure-Rust implementation (`flate2` rust-backend / `miniz_oxide`); PNG/JPEG/TIFF/DICOM via pure-Rust crates when those waves run; HDF5 exclusively via the user's own `rust-hdf5` crate — never the C-binding `hdf5` crate.
