| 5.11 | **`Image::get_vector` leniency on complex vs `get_pixel_as` strictness** — `get_vector` serves complex images (returning `[re, im]`, §4.23) where SimpleITK's `GetPixelAsVector*` throws; the new `get_pixel_as`/`set_pixel_as` (2026-07-10) follow upstream and reject complex — so the two accessor families now differ in strictness. | (a) tighten `get_vector`/`set_vector` to reject complex (parity, breaking; deletes §4.23); (b) keep the documented leniency and the inconsistency. |
| 5.12 | **`sitk-registration` pyramid smoothing vs its `SmoothingRecursiveGaussian` parity claim** — `method.rs::prepare_level` doc-claims parity with `SmoothingRecursiveGaussianImageFilter` but calls the lower-level `recursive_gaussian()`, which narrows back to the *input's* pixel type, while the newly-ported `smoothing_recursive_gaussian()` always narrows to Float32/VectorFloat32 (`RebindImageType<float>`). For integer-typed registration inputs each pyramid level quantizes the smoothed intensities to the integer type before resampling — a real precision divergence from the claimed upstream semantics (gaussian-porter finding, 2026-07-10). | (a) correct the doc comment to describe the actual behavior; (b) switch the pyramid to `smoothing_recursive_gaussian` (changes registration numerics for integer inputs). |
| 5.13 | **Should `write_image` round-trip the meta-data dictionary into the header (§4.41)?** ITK does; this port drops it. Doing so changes the bytes every `.mha`/`.mhd` this crate writes — the reader synthesizes `ITK_InputFilterName = MetaImageIO` and `Modality = MET_MOD_UNKNOWN` on every read, so a read→write round trip would append two user fields — and the header-pinning tests exist precisely to freeze those bytes (io-architect finding, 2026-07-10). | (a) keep dropping it (current state), so writes stay a pure function of the pixel/geometry model; (b) write the dictionary and re-pin the header tests, accepting the two synthesized lines; (c) write the dictionary but suppress keys the reader itself synthesized, which upstream does not do. |
| 5.14 | **`sitk-filters::add_constant`/`subtract_constant`/`multiply_constant` vs. the verified upstream cast-first-then-wrap policy (§4.43)** — the operator-surface task (`sitk-core::ops`) found these three functions' f64-accumulate-then-saturate policy does not match `Add`/`Subtract`/`Multiply`'s actual `double`-constant codegen, which casts the constant to the pixel type first and wraps. Fixing `add_constant`/`subtract_constant`/`multiply_constant` to match changes their existing, tested, shipped output for a fractional or out-of-range constant; leaving them as-is leaves `sitk-core::ops`'s new (verified-correct) operators disagreeing with the equivalent named procedural functions. Facade-porter finding, 2026-07-10 (facade-porter wave). | (a) align `add_constant`/`subtract_constant`/`multiply_constant` on the verified cast-first-then-wrap policy (parity, breaking); (b) keep the current f64-then-saturate behavior as a documented §4 divergence and correct its module-doc rationale, accepting the operator/procedural inconsistency. |
| 5.15 | **`Image: PartialEq` includes the metadata dictionary** — `Image` derives `PartialEq` and `metadata: BTreeMap<String, String>` is a field (`image.rs:239-252`), so two images with identical pixels/geometry but different dictionaries compare unequal. SimpleITK's `Image` has no `operator==` at all — its tests compare via hash/statistics — so there is no upstream behavior to be faithful to; this is a pure API-design choice. Load-bearing consequence: every read-vs-computed comparison test (`read_image(f) == expected`) fails once a reader synthesizes dictionary keys (`MetaImageIo` synthesizes `ITK_InputFilterName`/`Modality` on every read, §4.41), and the divergence-family risk grows with each IO format. io-architect finding, 2026-07-10. | (a) keep metadata in `PartialEq` (current) — equality means "same value including header provenance", tests must strip/set metadata explicitly; (b) exclude metadata from `PartialEq` (manual impl over pixels+geometry only) and expose the dictionary comparison separately; (c) keep the derive and add a named `same_pixels_and_geometry`-style comparator for tests, mirroring the existing `is_congruent_image_geometry` family. |
| 5.16 | **`ParametricTransform::set_parameters` is infallible and panics on a length mismatch** — every other mutator that can reject its input (`set_fixed_parameters`, `CompositeTransform::add_transform`) returns `Result`, and ITK's `SetParameters` overrides throw. The panic is unreachable from the transform-file reader, which now length-checks first (§4.47), but any other caller feeding externally-derived parameters (an optimizer restoring a checkpoint, a future `.h5` reader) has no non-panicking path. transform-porter finding, 2026-07-10. | (a) keep it infallible and require callers to length-check, documenting the panic as a contract; (b) change the signature to `Result<()>` (breaking: ~13 impls plus the `sitk-registration` optimizer loops) so a wrong-length vector is recoverable everywhere, as it is upstream. **Decided 2026-07-10 (user): option (b)** — queued behind the wave-19 registration branch (same files); execute immediately after it merges. **Status: option (b) executed 2026-07-10** — `set_parameters` returns `Result<(), TransformError>` on the trait and all sixteen concrete impls (`transform.rs` ×13, `bspline.rs`, `displacement.rs`, `composite.rs`) plus the erased `Transform` forwarder (`erased.rs`), reusing `TransformError::InvalidParameters` uniformly via a new `check_len` helper (mirrors `check_fixed_len`). `sitk-registration::method.rs`: the `Composed`/`CompositeTransform` delegate chains propagate via `?`; the direct calls inside `execute`'s `Result`-returning body (`RegistrationError` has `#[from] TransformError`) propagate via `?`; the `Objective`-trait-bound closures (`MetricObjective`, the `objective!`/`value_objective!` macros) have no fallible surface to propagate through — those `.expect(...)`, justified because the optimizer only ever probes at the transform's own `number_of_parameters()`. `sitk-io`'s reader pre-check is removed — see the revised §4.47. One error-path test added per representative impl family (translation, matrix-offset/affine, small-literal-count/euler2d, similarity2d, versor, scale, scale-logarithmic delegate, bspline, displacement field, composite, and the erased surface). |
| 5.18 | **Which pure-Rust zlib crate implements §5.8's compression wave** — the workspace's second external crate after `thiserror`. compression-porter, 2026-07-10. | (a) `miniz_oxide` directly; (b) `flate2` with `default-features = false, features = ["rust_backend"]`, whose only backend is `miniz_oxide`. **Chosen: (b).** All three formats need the *gzip container*, not just deflate: NrrdIO's `gzio.c` and zlib's `gzopen` both write a ten-byte header plus a CRC-32/ISIZE trailer, and readers must accept concatenated members. `miniz_oxide` exposes raw and zlib streams only, so (a) means hand-rolling that framing and its checksums — the exact code most likely to diverge from upstream unnoticed. `flate2`'s `GzBuilder`/`MultiGzDecoder` already have it, and its `XFL` rule (2 at level 9, 4 below level 2, else 0) is zlib's `deflate.c` rule, so with `mtime(0)` and `operating_system(3)` the ten header bytes match upstream's byte for byte (pinned by `gzip_header_matches_upstream_ten_bytes`). `default-features = false` plus the explicit `rust_backend` feature keeps `zlib-sys`, `zlib-ng` and `libz-rs` out of the tree; `cargo tree -p sitk-io -e normal` shows `flate2 1.1.9 → {crc32fast → cfg-if, miniz_oxide → {adler2, simd-adler32}}` — six pure-Rust crates, no `*-sys` and no `build.rs` linking C. Deflate *output* bytes still differ from zlib's at the same level (different match/block choices), which is why §5.8's wave pins this port's own bytes rather than upstream's — see the `tests/compression.rs` module doc. |
| 5.19 | **`set_optimizer_scales_from_physical_shift()` takes no estimator arguments** — upstream's `SetOptimizerScalesFromPhysicalShift(centralRegionRadius = 5, smallParameterVariation = 0.01)` (`sitkImageRegistrationMethod.h:503`) exposes both knobs as C++ default arguments; the two new setters `set_optimizer_scales_from_jacobian(radius)` and `set_optimizer_scales_from_index_shift(radius, small_variation)` take them explicitly, since Rust has no default arguments. The physical-shift setter kept its existing no-argument signature and uses the upstream defaults, so the three setters are now inconsistent with each other. Both knobs are inert for every transform this crate registers (§2.115, and δ cancels analytically in `scale = (δ‖Jᵢ‖/δ)²`), so this is an API-shape question, not a numerics one. | (a) leave as is; (b) change to `set_optimizer_scales_from_physical_shift(radius, small_variation)` — a breaking change to a setter with existing callers in `method.rs` tests and the crate docs; (c) add `set_optimizer_scales_from_physical_shift_with(radius, small_variation)` alongside the no-arg form |
| 5.20 | What ends up on disk when a `.gipl.gz` write fails partway through (a 32-bit or 64-bit integer image)? `GiplImageIO::Write`'s two throws (`"Invalid type"`, `"Pixel Type Unknown"`) happen while `m_Internal->m_GzFile` is still open (`itkGiplImageIO.cxx:759-761`, `:1010`/`:1024`); `gzclose` runs only in the destructor (`:81-95`), once the throwing call unwinds and the `GiplImageIO` object is destroyed — flushing zlib's internal write buffer (well under its default size for either failure mode: 8 or 256 bytes) and writing the gzip trailer over whatever `gzwrite` had accumulated. gipl-gz-porter finding, 2026-07-10. | (a) model the eventual on-disk state as gzip-compressing the same partial bytes the uncompressed path already writes verbatim. **Chosen: (a)** for the 64-bit-integer arm (upstream's own `"Invalid type"` case, unaffected by §1.52's fix), pinned by `gipl_int64_write_leaves_eight_bytes_and_then_fails`/`gipl_gz_int64_write_leaves_eight_bytes_and_then_fails`; (b) leave the `.gz` file absent or empty on these paths, on the theory that a stream never explicitly `gzclose`d might not reach disk at all under some buffering configuration. Not run against a live ITK+zlib build to observe `gzclose`'s destructor timing directly — (a) is inferred from zlib's internal-buffer-then-flush semantics and C++ RAII, not independently verified. The 32-bit-integer arm this decision originally also covered no longer reaches `gzopen`/`write_bytes` at all: §1.52, fixed in this port (2026-07-11), rejects that pixel type before any file I/O. |
| 5.21 | **`rust-hdf5` raises `sitk-io`'s effective MSRV from 1.85 to 1.89** — §5.8 named `rust-hdf5` as the only permitted HDF5 crate. `cargo add rust-hdf5 --dry-run -p sitk-io` reports `warning: ignoring rust-hdf5@0.3.2 (which requires rustc 1.89) to maintain sitk-io's rust-version of 1.85` and falls back to `0.3.2`'s predecessor line, `0.2.7`. hdf5-porter, 2026-07-10. | (a) pin `rust-hdf5 = "0.3"` (resolves to the registry's `0.3.2`; builds clean on the 1.96 toolchain here, but `workspace.package.rust-version = "1.85"` is now a claim no `sitk-io` consumer on 1.85–1.88 can satisfy); (b) pin `rust-hdf5 = "0.2"`, whose `H5File`/`H5Group`/`H5Dataset` surface this port does not use anything outside of, keeping the MSRV claim true; (c) raise `workspace.package.rust-version` to `1.89`. **Taken for now: (a)**, since the task named `0.3`; the MSRV claim in the root `Cargo.toml` is left untouched (another porter holds that file) and is now inaccurate for `sitk-io`. | 5.22 | **`SetUseCompression` for transform writing** — `HDF5TransformIOTemplate::WriteParameters` deflate-5s `TransformParameters` in `min(dim, 1 MiB)` chunks when the flag is set, and leaves `TransformFixedParameters` uncompressed regardless (`itkHDF5TransformIO.cxx:112-146`). | 5.23 | **Callback representation for the observer/introspection surface** (`sitk::Command`/`sitk::Event`, `AddCommand`, and `ImageRegistrationMethod`'s active measurements `GetOptimizerIteration`/`GetMetricValue`/`GetOptimizerPosition`/…/`StopRegistration`). Upstream's `Command::Execute()` takes no arguments (`sitkCommand.h:60-61`) and reaches back into the invoking object mid-`Execute`; in Rust that is `&self` inside a `&mut self` region while `run_single_level`'s objective closure already holds `&mut transform`. Upstream also documents two UB clauses — deleting a `Command` during a callback, and `RemoveAllCommands` while invoking (`sitkProcessObject.h:265-266, 284-288`). Full design, upstream citations, hook sites, and the phase-1/1b/2 split: **[`doc/observer-design.md`](observer-design.md)** (observer-architect, 2026-07-10). | (a) **recommended — observers passed *into* `execute`**: `execute_observed(&self, fixed, moving, initial, &mut Observers<'cb>)`, callbacks are `FnMut(&IterationContext<'_>) -> Control` receiving the measurements as a borrowed context built from the optimizer's loop locals, `Control::Stop` replacing `StopRegistration()`. The borrow problem dissolves (the callback never names the method), both UB clauses become unrepresentable (`Observers` is uniquely borrowed for the call), and callbacks need no `'static` bound — upstream's stack-`Command` use case. Cost: no `add_command` spelling, observer set is per-call rather than object state. (b) **`add_command`-stored boxes + `&mut self` execute** — closest to upstream's spelling, but `Box<dyn FnMut + 'static>` forces owned captures, or a `'cb` lifetime parameter infects `ImageRegistrationMethod` and every caller; invoking stored observers needs `&mut self` against the level loop's existing `&self` borrows, so it re-opens the reentrancy question and is closeable only with interior mutability. (c) **channels** (`Sender<RegistrationEvent>`) — `Send`, decoupled, but `StopRegistration` has no return path (needs a second `AtomicBool`), `position`/`scales` must be cloned per message, and asynchronous delivery loses "the metric value at the iterate where it was evaluated", the guarantee ITK commit `cf929f2ca7` exists to provide. Buildable as an adapter on top of (a); (a) is not buildable on top of it. |
| 5.24 | **Should this port expose `ExpandRGBPalette`/`WritePalette` beyond SimpleITK's own surface (§4.84, §4.87)?** — `PNGImageIO` supports reading a palette PNG as raw indices plus a stored color table (`m_ExpandRGBPalette = false`) and writing a 1-component image as an indexed PNG (`GetWritePalette()`), but SimpleITK's wrapping layer calls neither setter, so both paths are unreachable through the surface this crate ports — the same line every sibling format already draws (GIPL, VTK, NRRD, NIfTI never surface capability beyond what SimpleITK's own wrapper reaches either). png-porter, 2026-07-10. | (a) keep matching only the reachable SimpleITK surface — always-expand on read, never-indexed on write; (b) add crate-only `read_as_scalar_plus_palette`/`write_indexed` free functions beyond the `ImageIo` trait, surfacing capability SimpleITK itself does not expose. **Decided (png-porter, 2026-07-10): option (a)** — no upstream-reachable behavior is lost by omission, and adding it would be the first format in this crate to exceed SimpleITK's own capability surface. |
| 5.25 | **Should `image_hdf5::write` refuse a vector or complex image?** Per §3.47 such a file writes cleanly and `ImageReaderBase::GetPixelIDFromImageIO` can never load it — SimpleITK produces a file only SimpleITK cannot read. This port reproduces that asymmetry. | (a) reproduce upstream (current state): `write` accepts any pixel type, `read` raises `UnknownPixelType`; (b) refuse the write, diverging from SimpleITK for files ITK's own C++ readers *can* load into a `VectorImage`; (c) fix the read side by inferring `IOPixelEnum::VECTOR` from `numberOfComponents > 1`, diverging from SimpleITK in the other direction and loading files upstream rejects. Upstream fix would be one `SetPixelType` call in `HDF5ImageIO::ReadImageInformation`. **Resolved** (2026-07-11): option (c) — the read side infers `IOPixelEnum::VECTOR` from `numberOfComponents > 1`, loading a vector or complex image SimpleITK writes but its own reader rejects. `write` still accepts any pixel type, so a scalar file is unaffected; a complex image reads back as a two-component float vector, since the format records no complex marker. See §3.47. |
| 5.26 | **Which pure-Rust crates should back `.jpg`/`.jpeg` image IO**, given §5.8(a)'s "pure-Rust only, no `*-sys`" rule? | (a) `jpeg-decoder` (read) + `jpeg-encoder` (write) — both `#[deny(unsafe_code)]`/`#[forbid(unsafe_code)]` safe Rust outside an unused `simd` feature, verified via `cargo tree -p sitk-io` showing no `*-sys` crate anywhere in the dependency tree; `jpeg-decoder` built with `default-features = false` to drop its default `rayon` dependency, which this crate (one image at a time, no parallel decode need) has no use for. **Chosen: (a).** (b) the `image` crate's bundled JPEG codec — internally the same `jpeg-decoder`, but drags in the rest of `image`'s multi-format surface as unused dependency weight; rejected as heavier than needed for one format. (c) `mozjpeg-sys`/`turbojpeg` bindings around libjpeg-turbo — rejected outright, both are `*-sys` crates, violating §5.8(a) directly. |
| 5.27 | **Should JPEG writes match `jpeg-encoder`'s own quality-based chroma-subsampling default, or upstream's constant behaviour?** `jpeg_default_colorspace`/`jpeg_set_colorspace` (`jcparam.c`) map `JCS_RGB` input to `JCS_YCbCr` output with constant 2x2/1x1/1x1 (4:2:0) chroma subsampling regardless of quality (`SET_COMP` calls, `jcparam.c:374-382`) — every upstream JPEG write of a 3-component image subsamples chroma, at any quality setting. `jpeg_encoder::Encoder::new` instead selects `SamplingFactor::F_2_2` only when quality < 90, else `F_1_1` (no subsampling) — a quality-dependent default that would silently diverge from upstream at quality ≥ 90, exactly the range a caller optimizing for fidelity is most likely to choose. | (a) leave the crate's own quality-dependent default — rejected, diverges from upstream's constant 4:2:0 for the highest-quality writes. (b) explicit `encoder.set_sampling_factor(SamplingFactor::F_2_2)` for every 3-component write, matching upstream's constant behaviour regardless of quality. **Chosen: (b).** **Resolved** (2026-07-11) — the constant 4:2:0 is now the *default* rather than the only option: `JpegChromaSubsampling { None (4:4:4), Chroma422, Chroma420 }` on `JpegWriteOptions`, selected through `jpeg::write_with_jpeg_options`, with `Chroma420` the default (byte-identical to upstream). The `ImageIo::write` path is unchanged. See §3.50. |
| 5.28 | **Palette TIFFs (§4.100) and the `TIFFReadRGBAImageOriented` fallback (§4.102) are unreadable on the `tiff` crate.** Together they are the whole of what upstream reads and this port does not. | (a) **current state** — refuse both with `IoError::UnsupportedTiffFeature`, per §5.8's pure-Rust constraint; (b) hand-implement palette expansion by reading `TIFFTAG_COLORMAP` through `Decoder::get_tag` and decoding the index plane ourselves, which the `tiff` crate does not expose a path for (its `colortype()` gate precedes every decode); (c) port libtiff's RGBA renderer, a large body of colour-conversion code, for the exotic photometrics; (d) revisit §5.8 and take a libtiff binding. Palette TIFFs are common enough that (b) may be worth its cost; (c) is not, and (d) is excluded by §5.8. **Resolved** (2026-07-11) — stayed on (a); (b) is not merely costly but impossible against `tiff` 0.11.3: every public decode entry point (`read_image`, `read_image_to_buffer`, `read_image_bytes`, `read_chunk`, `read_chunk_bytes`, `read_chunk_to_buffer`, `read_coding_unit_bytes`) calls `Image::readout_for_size`, which invokes the `colortype()` gate unconditionally (decoder/image.rs:698) before any chunk offset, compression, or strip-decompression step runs, and `Decoder::image()` plus the `Image` type it returns are `pub(crate)` — there is no lower-level door outside the crate to reach `TIFFTAG_COLORMAP`'s index plane. Palette expansion cannot be hand-rolled against this crate's public surface; (c)/(d) remain excluded as originally reasoned. Still refused with `IoError::UnsupportedTiffFeature`, pinned by `a_palette_tiff_is_refused_by_both_entry_points`. |
| 5.29 | **Should `transform_matlab::write_transform` refuse a non-empty `CompositeTransform` up front?** Per §2.144 such a write always succeeds and produces a `.mat` file that can never be read back (a parameter-count mismatch on the fresh empty composite `read_transform_list` reconstructs) — upstream produces a file only upstream itself cannot read back through this same IO. This port reproduces that asymmetry rather than closing it. | (a) reproduce upstream (current state): `write_transform` accepts any `Transform`, including a non-empty composite; `read_transform` raises `TransformError::InvalidFixedParameters`/`InvalidParameters` on the way back in; (b) refuse the write for a non-empty composite with a clear, purpose-built error (e.g. an `UnsupportedMatlabTransformFeature` variant) instead of letting the caller discover the problem only on a later read — diverging from SimpleITK, whose real `MatlabTransformIO::Write` has no such guard and would happily write the same unreadable file. Same shape as §5.25 (`image_hdf5::write` and a vector/complex image). **Resolved** (2026-07-11): option (b) — `write_transform` refuses a non-empty (and, by extension, nested) `CompositeTransform` with `IoError::UnsupportedMatlabTransformFeature`, so the failure surfaces at write instead of on a later read. An empty composite still writes and round-trips. See §2.144/§2.145. |
| 5.30 | **Should `sitk-io` implement the DICOM *write* side?** Wave-25 ports the *read* side of `itk::GDCMImageIO` only. `GDCMImageIO::Write` (`itkGDCMImageIO.cxx:832-1416`) rebuilds a DICOM file from the meta-data dictionary, mints Study/Series/FrameOfReference UIDs from a global `gdcm::UIDGenerator`, and inverse-rescales the buffer. `DicomImageIo::can_write_file` answers `true` for the extensions upstream advertises (matching `GDCMImageIO::CanWriteFile`, which is just `HasSupportedWriteExtension(name, false)`, `:814-826`), and `write` then refuses with `IoError::UnsupportedDicomFeature` (pinned by `write_is_refused`). | (a) leave write unimplemented (current) — DICOM writing is a large surface (UID generation, VR/encoding decisions, inverse rescale, the SC/plane-module and rescale round-trip) whose byte output needs its own parity pass; (b) port `GDCMImageIO::Write` on `dicom-object`'s encoder in a later wave. Note byte-for-byte parity is impossible without pinning the UID source: `gdcm::UIDGenerator` seeds UIDs from wall-clock time plus a counter, so (b) must first decide how UIDs are made deterministic. |
| 5.31 | **Should `ImageSeriesReader` grow a pixel-casting layer so `SeriesPixelTypeMismatch` (§4.113) narrows instead of erroring, matching upstream's silent behavior?** Every other reader in this crate (`ImageFileReader` included) also has no such layer and also has no equivalent check to relax, so this would be the first. | (a) keep the strict per-slice pixel-type equality check (current state) — safe, but a mixed-type series this crate could theoretically assemble upstream-style is simply refused; (b) add a general numeric-narrowing cast layer to `ImageIo`/`Image` (a superset of `SeriesPixelTypeMismatch`'s scope, since it would also apply to any future `SetOutputPixelType` work, ledger §6) so a later slice narrows into the series' established pixel type exactly as `itk::ImageFileReader<TOutputImage>::GenerateData` does — meaningful new scope, not scoped to this filter alone. |

## 6. Remaining coverage gaps

Rewritten 2026-07-10 after a full-surface audit of the SimpleITK checkout
(all 298 `Code/BasicFilters/yaml/` definitions hand-adjudicated against every
`pub fn` in the workspace, plus the hand-written `Code/BasicFilters/include/`
layer, `sitkImage.h`, `Code/IO/`, and `sitkImageRegistrationMethod.h`).
Every cluster this section previously listed as blocked is ported: the vector
consumers (`LabelOverlay`, `LabelToRGB`, `ScalarToRGBColormap`,
`LabelMapToRGB`/`LabelMapOverlay`/`LabelMapContourOverlay`), the six complex
conversion filters (`sitk-filters::complex`, §2.58/§3.16/§4.23/§4.24), and the
LabelMap object type with its manipulation/statistics filters
(`sitk-core::label_map`, §4.25–4.29). Multi-channel (vector/complex) MetaImage
read/write landed 2026-07-10 (§2.67/§4.30). Every non-FFT `BasicFilters` gap
this section used to list has now landed 2026-07-10: the three near-mechanical
recursive-Gaussian composites — `SmoothingRecursiveGaussian`,
`GradientRecursiveGaussian`, `Gradient` — (§3.19), the ten `Equal`, `Greater`,
`Less`, `Round`, `CyclicShift`, `ShiftScale`, `NormalizeToConstant`, `Rank`,
`VotingBinaryHoleFilling`, `NormalizedCorrelation` (§1.43, §2.69-2.71, §3.26,
§4.35-4.36, §5.6), and the `LabelMap` residue — `LabelMapMask`,
`LabelMapToBinary` — (§1.42, §3.23-3.25).

What actually remains unported:

- ~~**FFT family (5)**~~: `ForwardFFT`, `InverseFFT`,
  `RealToHalfHermitianForwardFFT`, `HalfHermitianToRealInverseFFT`, public
  `FFTPad` — all five landed 2026-07-10 in `sitk-filters::fourier` (wave-20,
  §5.7 executed; §2.109-2.111, §3.38-3.39, §4.74).
- **Hand-written BasicFilters layer** (`Code/BasicFilters/include/`): fully
  ported as of wave-17. `sitkImageOperators.h`'s `std::ops` surface for `Image`
  landed 2026-07-10 (`sitk-core::ops`, §4.43/§5.14); `sitkHashImageFilter.h`'s
  `Hash`/`HashImageFilter` landed 2026-07-10 (`sitk-filters::hash`, §3.29);
  `BSplineTransformInitializer`/`CenteredVersorTransformInitializer` landed
  2026-07-10 (wave-17, §2.76/§4.44-4.45).
- **`sitk-core::Image` vs `sitkImage.h`**: the metadata dictionary
  (`{Get,Set,Erase,Has}MetaData*`, `sitkImage.h:401-432` — load-bearing: every
  real IO format round-trips header keys through it),
  `TransformIndexToPhysicalPoint`/`TransformPhysicalPointToIndex`,
  `EvaluateAtContinuousIndex`/`EvaluateAtPhysicalPoint`,
  `IsCongruentImageGeometry`/`IsSameImageGeometryAs`,
  `ToVectorImage`/`ToScalarImage`, scalar `GetPixelAs*`/`SetPixelAs*`,
  `GetSizeOfPixelComponent`, `GetPixelIDTypeAsString`, `ToString`.
  *Metadata + accessors assigned wave-16.*
- **`sitk-io`**: everything beyond MetaImage, NRRD and NIfTI-1, each now in
  both an uncompressed and a compressed form. SimpleITK registers every default ITK ImageIO
  factory (BioRad, BMP, Bruker2dseq, FDF, GDCM, GE4, GE5, GEAdw, Gipl, HDF5,
  JPEG, JPEG2000, LSM, MGH, MINC, MRC, Nifti, Nrrd, PhilipsREC, PNG, Scanco,
  SiemensVision, Stimulate, TIFF, VTI, VTK) against a factory protocol.
  Wave-17 landed that seam — an `ImageIo` trait plus a
  `registry`/`create_image_io` two-phase probe mirroring
  `itk::ImageIOFactory::CreateImageIO`, with `MetaImageIo` as its first
  implementor — and the class-level surface built on it: `ImageFileReader`
  (`read_image_information`, extract-region), `ImageFileWriter` (`set_image_io`),
  `registered_image_ios`. The one reader-layer behavior left unported by that
  seam — `itk::ImageFileReader`'s post-read geometry normalization, which flips a
  negative spacing component positive, negates the matching direction column, and
  records the raw values under `ITK_original_spacing`/`ITK_original_direction`
  (`itkImageFileReader.hxx:216-239`; GDCM is the motivating producer of a negative
  Z-spacing, `itkGDCMImageIO.cxx:703`) — **is now ported** (2026-07-11) in
  `reader::normalize_reader_geometry`, applied by both `ImageFileReader::execute`
  and the free `read_image` so every format gets it at once (each `ImageIo` still
  reports raw values). The two originals are stored as space-separated
  round-trippable f64 rather than through SimpleITK's `MetaDataObject::Print`,
  which renders the spacing vector as the useless `"[UNKNOWN PRINT
  CHARACTERISTICS]"` and the direction as a `vnl_matrix` dump — the silent-data-
  loss policy fix. Wave-18 landed `NrrdImageIo` (`.nrrd`/`.nhdr`, raw
  and ascii-read encodings, §1.46-1.48/§2.82-2.85/§3.31/§4.51-4.54), the
  Insight legacy transform reader/writer `read_transform`/`write_transform`
  (`.tfm`/`.txt`, §1.45/§2.78-2.81/§3.30/§4.47/§4.50 — since joined by the HDF5
  transform IO, below), and `NiftiImageIo` —
  uncompressed single-file `.nii` plus `.hdr`/`.img` pairs, read and write
  (§1.49-1.51, §2.86-2.92, §3.32, §4.55-4.63); `.nia` and legacy-Analyze
  writing are unimplemented (§4.62).
  Wave-19 landed `GiplImageIo` (`.gipl`, read and write; `.gipl.gz` read and
  write — §1.52-1.53, §1.58, §2.93-2.97, §2.118, §3.42, §4.68 (closed),
  §4.69, §4.73, §4.79)
  and `VtkImageIo` (legacy structured-points `.vtk`, `BINARY` and `ASCII` read,
  `BINARY` write — §1.54-1.55, §2.98-2.108, §3.37, §4.69-4.72).
  Wave-20 landed the compression half of
  §5.8 on the one new dependency §5.18 chose (`flate2`, `rust_backend`):
  MetaImage `CompressedData = True` read and write (`.mha` and `.mhd`/`.zraw`,
  §1.56-1.57/§2.112/§4.75), NRRD `encoding: gzip` read and write
  (`.nrrd` and `.nhdr`/`.raw.gz`, §2.113, §4.53 corrected), `.nii.gz` /
  `.hdr.gz` / `.img.gz` read and write (§2.113/§3.40), and the write-side opt-in
  `ImageFileWriter::{set_use_compression, set_compression_level}` /
  `write_image_with` that upstream spells `SetUseCompression` /
  `SetCompressionLevel` / `WriteImage(image, name, useCompression, level)`.
  `.gipl.gz` was wired to the same compression module afterward, on the same
  terms — see the Wave-19 citation above and §5.20.
  Wave-21 landed the **HDF5 transform IO** (`sitk-io::transform_hdf5`, a port of
  `itk::HDF5TransformIOTemplate<double>`) on the `rust-hdf5` crate §5.8 named:
  `/TransformGroup/N/{TransformType,TransformFixedParameters,TransformParameters}`
  read and write for all sixteen concrete transforms and `CompositeTransform`,
  dispatched from `read_transform`/`write_transform` alongside `.tfm`/`.txt`
  (§2.119-2.123, §3.43, §4.80-4.83, §5.21-5.22). The MATLAB transform IO
  (`sitk-io::transform_matlab`, a port of `itk::MatlabTransformIOTemplate<double>`)
  landed after it, on the MAT Level-4 binary format `vnl_matlab_write`/
  `vnl_matlab_readhdr` define — no external dependency — read and write for all
  sixteen concrete transforms and `CompositeTransform`, dispatched alongside
  `.tfm`/`.txt`/`.h5` (§1.69, §2.143-2.145, §4.104, §5.29). Unlike `.tfm`/`.h5`,
  it never flattens a composite: `TransformFileWriterTemplate`'s flattening
  helper only runs on the float↔double precision-mismatch write path, not the
  double→double path this crate always takes, so a composite is written as one
  opaque record and only an *empty* one can be read back (§2.144). Transform IO
  still missing: `TransformFileWriter::SetUseCompression` on the write side
  (§5.22), and the `.txt`-only `ComponentTransformFile:` indirection has no
  HDF5/Matlab counterpart because upstream has none.
  Wave-22 landed **`PngImageIo`** (`sitk-io::png`, a port of `itk::PNGImageIO`)
  on the pure-Rust `png` crate §5.8 chose: `.png`/`.PNG` read and write for
  grayscale and RGB/RGBA `UInt8`/`UInt16` images, reproducing the always-on
  palette expansion (§2.127/§4.84), the case-sensitive `CanWriteFile`
  (§2.124), the first-slice-only 3-D write and the >4-component row
  truncation as one routine (§2.125/§2.126), the dead-unless-`UseCompression`
  compression level (§3.46), and the unwritable-component-type
  truncate-then-throw (§1.59). A 2-channel gray+alpha PNG is readable/writable
  by raw `PNGImageIO` but unrepresentable through `GetPixelIDFromImageIO`
  (§3.45); `sCAL` spacing, `sBIT` shifting and indexed/palette writing are not
  implemented — the `png` crate has no support for the first two, and
  SimpleITK exposes no `WritePalette` setter for the third (§4.85-§4.87,
  §5.24).
  Wave-22 also landed the **HDF5 image IO** (`sitk-io::image_hdf5`, a port of
  `itk::HDF5ImageIO`) on the same `rust-hdf5` crate — no new dependency:
  the `/ITKImage/0/{Directions,Origin,Spacing,Dimension,VoxelType,VoxelData,MetaData}`
  layout, read and write for every scalar component type at any dimension, the
  meta-data dictionary round-trip, and the unconditional deflate upstream
  applies (§1.61-1.63, §2.128-2.134, §3.47-3.48, §4.88-4.91, §5.25). A vector
  or complex image writes but cannot be read back, exactly as upstream (§3.47).
  Wave-23 landed **`JpegImageIo`** (`sitk-io::jpeg`, a port of `itk::JPEGImageIO`)
  on the pure-Rust `jpeg-decoder` (read) and `jpeg-encoder` (write) crates §5.26
  chose: `.jpg`/`.JPG`/`.jpeg`/`.JPEG` read and write for grayscale and RGB
  `UInt8` images, reproducing the stricter-than-PNG `CanReadFile` (extension,
  magic, full header parse — §2.136), the case-sensitive four-spelling
  `CanWriteFile` (§2.137), the outright rejection of a non-2-D write where PNG
  truncates silently (§2.135), the dead `UseCompression` (§2.138), the
  `1..=100` `Quality`/`CompressionLevel` alias with default 95 (§3.49), the
  always-on `Progressive`/`CMYKtoRGB` SimpleITK cannot reach (§3.50), and the
  density-write bug's effect if not its exact bytes (§1.64/§4.95). CMYK reads'
  plain-CMYK-correct/YCCK-wrong inversion formula bug has been fixed in this
  port, since `jpeg_decoder` already normalizes both source encodings before
  this crate sees a byte (§1.65/§4.93); a 2- or 5-plus-component read and a >1-or-3
  -component write are refused where upstream (oddly) succeeds or falls back
  to an undefined colour space (§4.94/§4.96); a >8-bit/lossless JPEG is
  refused, matching every real ITK build (§4.97); a mid-scanline decode error
  is a hard `Err`, not a silently short-filled buffer (§4.92).
  Wave-23 also landed **`TiffImageIo`** (`sitk-io::tiff`, a port of
  `itk::TIFFImageIO`) on the pure-Rust `tiff` crate: `.tif`/`.tiff` read and
  write, multi-page → 3-D volume assembly with a uniform per-page geometry
  rule that closes upstream's two heap overflows at source (§1.66-1.67,
  §4.98-4.99), the stale-component-type ladder closed as a refusal (§1.68),
  `MINISWHITE` read out un-inverted (§2.139), the RGB-for-everything write
  photometric (§2.141), `f32`-precision spacing through `RESOLUTIONUNIT`
  handling (§2.142), and the PackBits-or-nothing compressor SimpleITK can
  reach (§3.51-3.52). Palette TIFFs and the `TIFFReadRGBAImageOriented`
  fallback are refused per §5.8's pure-Rust constraint (§4.100/§4.102,
  decision §5.28); the TIFF metadata dictionary is not ported (§4.103).
  Wave-25 landed **`DicomImageIo`** (`sitk-io::dicom`, the *read* side of
  `itk::GDCMImageIO`) on the pure-Rust `dicom-object` crate — no `*-sys` crate
  in the tree — registered in `image_io::IOS` after `TiffImageIo` under the
  name `GDCMImageIO` (§3.54), reading native transfer syntaxes (Implicit VR LE,
  Explicit VR LE, Explicit VR BE, Deflated Explicit VR LE) for scalar,
  RGB/palette and Y'CbCr images: the always-3-D geometry, component type from
  Bits Allocated + Pixel Representation, the Rescale Slope/Intercept promotion
  and its `ComputeInterceptSlopePixelType` output-type forcing, the swapped
  Pixel Spacing, the ultrasound spacing override, and the `"GGGG|EEEE"`
  meta-data dictionary with GDCM's own base64 and string-format quirks (§2.148).
  Encapsulated transfer syntaxes, sequence-driven SOP classes,
  12-bit/64-bit/Float16/YBR_FULL_422 pixels, non-8/16-bit MONOCHROME1,
  segmented palettes and rescale-combined-with-palette/YBR are refused rather
  than approximated (§4.106-4.111), and the memory-unsafe GDCM edges (Z-spacing
  VM1 out-of-bounds, single-valued ultrasound spacing, SINGLEBIT row padding)
  are closed by refusal (§1.70-1.72). The DICOM **write** side is not ported —
  `can_write_file` answers for the advertised extensions and `write` refuses
  (§5.30). `itk::ImageFileReader`'s negative-spacing sign flip and its
  `ITK_original_spacing`/`ITK_original_direction` metadata injection — which
  bites DICOM because GDCM's Z-spacing can be negative before that flip
  (`itkGDCMImageIO.cxx:703`) — were ported 2026-07-11 as
  `reader::normalize_reader_geometry`, applied crate-wide on the shared read
  path (`execute`/`read_image`, and — as of 2026-07-11 — inside
  `ImageSeriesReader::execute` too, on each per-slice read and on the
  first/last derivation geometry, which was the one read path that had
  bypassed the normalization; the sign-flip half is factored into
  `reader::flip_negative_spacing` so the series reader can apply it to the raw
  `ImageInformation` geometry it derives inter-slice spacing/direction from,
  matching upstream reading every slice through the same `ImageFileReader`,
  `itkImageSeriesReader.hxx:120-122,468`; `read_image_information` still
  reports raw geometry, as SimpleITK does).
  Wave-25 landed **`ImageSeriesReader`/`ImageSeriesWriter`**
  (`sitk-io::image_series_reader`/`image_series_writer`, a port of
  `itk::simple::ImageSeriesReader`/`ImageSeriesWriter` wrapping
  `itk::ImageSeriesReader<TOutputImage>`/`itk::ImageSeriesWriter<TInputImage,
  TOutputImage>`), stacking a list of already-supported single-slice files
  (`.mha`, `.nrrd`, `.nii`, `.gipl`, `.vtk`, `.h5`, `.png`, `.jpg`, `.tif`, ...
  via the existing `ImageIo` registry) into one `N+1`-dimensional volume and
  slicing a 3-D volume back out to numbered files. Dimension promotion
  (collapsing a 4-D result back to 3-D when the newly-stacked axis is size 1),
  the moving-axis walk-down for a first file with unit leading axes,
  first/last-file z-spacing and direction derivation (independently
  overridable per endpoint by an `ITK_ImageOrigin` meta-data array, honoured
  only at an exact length match — §1.73/§4.112), `ForceOrthogonalDirection`'s
  sign-flip-vs-replace split, per-slice size/pixel-type checks
  (`SeriesSizeMismatch` reproduced, `SeriesPixelTypeMismatch` a deliberate new
  check with no upstream counterpart — §4.113/§5.31), `ReverseOrder`, and the
  non-uniform-sampling detector that silently starts meta-data collection
  mid-series and shifts the collected array's slice index (§2.149) are all
  ported on the reader side. The writer's 3-D-only `MemberFunctionFactory`
  registration (§3.56), its raw-path-string DICOM-extension rejection and its
  no-dot wraparound quirk (§3.55), the literal (not physically reprojected)
  2-D origin/spacing/direction truncation with a singular-submatrix-to-identity
  fallback (§2.150), the file-name-count-vs-`size()[2]` hard mismatch, and the
  full per-slice `ITK_Origin`/`ITK_Spacing`/`ITK_NumberOfDimensions`/
  `ITK_ZDirection` meta-data (persisted only by formats whose `ImageIo::write`
  round-trips arbitrary meta-data, e.g. `image_hdf5`, not `meta_image`) are
  ported on the writer side. GDCM series file-name enumeration
  (`GetGDCMSeriesFileNames`/`GetGDCMSeriesIDs`) was out of scope for this wave
  and stays unported — callers must supply file names themselves.
  Still missing: every other format's `ImageIo`; `ImageFileWriter::SetCompressor`
  (upstream's `""` default is the only setting implemented, and the only
  alternative it selects is NRRD's `bzip2`, which needs a bzip2 dependency);
  bzip2/hex/zrl NRRD encodings; streaming reads; GDCM series file-name
  enumeration (the DICOM-specific half of `ImageSeriesReader`'s upstream
  surface); `ImportImageFilter`;
  `ImageViewer`/`Show`. Binary formats gated on §5.8 (dependencies) and §5.9
  (test data). *Uncompressed NIfTI assigned wave-18; compression wave-20.*
- **Registration/Transform**: the erased `Transform` value type landed
  wave-18 (§5.10 option (a) executed — `sitk-transform::erased`, sixteen
  concrete types, §4.46/§4.48/§4.49) with `read_transform`/`write_transform`
  for `.tfm`/`.txt`, since joined by `.h5`/`.hdf5` (wave-21) and `.mat`
  (matlab-transform-porter, §5.8); `.xfm` (MINC) stays unported — no upstream
  defect drives it, just coverage. The initial-transform model landed wave-19
  (`set_initial_transform`(+in-place)/`set_moving_initial_transform`/
  `set_fixed_initial_transform`, `set_virtual_domain{,_from_image}`,
  `metric_evaluate` — §3.33-3.36, §4.64-4.67), and was completed 2026-07-10 by
  `set_initial_transform_as_bspline` (the multi-level BSpline overload with
  per-level scale factors), which ports
  `itk::BSplineTransformParametersAdaptor` as
  `BSplineTransform::adapt_transform_parameters` and fires it per level from
  `execute_with_initial_transform` (§2.146-2.147, §3.53, §4.105). Still
  missing: the observer/introspection
  surface (`GetOptimizerIteration`/`GetMetricValue`/…/`StopRegistration`,
  upstream `sitkCommand.h`/`sitkEvent.h`) — designed but not implemented, see
  [`doc/observer-design.md`](observer-design.md), gated on §5.23;
  and `SetMetricUse{Fixed,Moving}ImageGradientFilter`, which this port
  deliberately does not expose (§4.76 — its metrics have a single, exact
  gradient path, and the flag is inert upstream for every metric but Demons,
  §3.41). `SetOptimizerScalesFrom{Jacobian,IndexShift}` and
  `Set/GetOptimizerWeights` landed with the estimator-owned virtual-domain
  sampling they need (§2.114-2.117, §4.77-4.78). All sixteen concrete
  transform classes, both `BSpline`/`CenteredVersor` transform initializers
  (wave-17, §2.76/§4.44-4.45), and all metrics/optimizers of
  `ImageRegistrationMethod` are already ported.
- **Facade (`crates/sitk`)**: docs rewritten and `LabelMap`/`LabelObject`/
  `LabelObjectLine`/the transform classes hoisted to the crate root
  2026-07-10. Wave-18 closed the remaining transform gap: the erased
  `Transform` enum, `TransformBase`, and the sixteen concrete transform types
  were already hoisted to the crate root as part of that same rewrite;
  `read_transform`/`write_transform` are now re-exported at the crate root
  too, and a top-level `resample` free function was added
  (`crates/sitk/src/lib.rs`) — it needed no new dispatch plumbing in
  `sitk-transform` since `Transform` already implements `TransformBase` and
  `ResampleImageFilter::execute` is generic over that trait. No top-level
  `Warp` free function yet (`transform::WarpImageFilter` is class-based
  only) — out of scope for this pass.
